Procedural Rulings on Claims of Error in Division
Summarizes procedural rulings for division disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on how a claim of error in division is adjudicated, including the role of partitioner testimony and evidentiary burden.

Core Idea
A claim of error in division is not automatically accepted; it requires evidence or the defendant's oath.

When jointly owned property is divided among partners, disputes may arise about whether each partner received their rightful share. The Hanafi school has specific procedural rules to resolve such claims. This lesson covers the key rulings from the chapter on claims of error in division, focusing on the testimony of partitioners, the burden of proof, and the consequences of disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of claim
Determine whether the claim is about error in the division itself, non-receipt of a specific share, or disagreement on boundaries/valuation. Each has a different ruling.
The passage covers multiple scenarios; isolate one at a time.
2
Assess the evidence
If two partitioners (qasims) testify that a partner received his share, their testimony is accepted. If only one partitioner testifies, it is not acceptable.
Testimony of two qasims is considered sufficient proof of receipt.
3
Apply the burden of proof
When a partner claims an error in the division, the division is not automatically repeated. The claimant must produce evidence. If he cannot, the judge administers an oath to the other partners.
According to Al-Hidayah, the claim should not even be entertained; the defendant's statement is taken as true.
4
Handle disagreements among partners
If partners disagree on valuation after division, the disagreement is ignored (the division stands). If they disagree on boundaries and both produce evidence, the matter is adjudicated accordingly.
Disagreement on valuation does not invalidate the division.
5
Consider appearance of a rightful claimant
If a third party appears and claims entitlement to part of the divided property, the ruling varies based on the strength of their claim. The passage references statements of jurists.
This is a separate issue not fully elaborated here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قاسمین نے شرکاء کے درمیان تقسیم کر دی پھر شرکاء میں اختلاف ہوا کسی نے کہا ر ا حصہ مجھے نہیں ملا حالانکہ میرے حصہ میں فلاں کمرہ داخل ہے اور دو قاسموں نے گواہی دی کہ اس نا لے لیا ہے تو گواہی قبول کی جائے گی امام محمد کی دلیل شیخین کی دلیل امام طحاوی کا نقطہ نظر صاحب ہدایہ کی امام طحاوی کی دلیل پر نگیر ایک قاسم نے گواہی بھی قابل قبول نہیں باب دعوى الغلط في القسمة والاستحقاق فيها کوئی شریک تقسیم کی غلطی کا دعویٰ کرے تو تقسیم کا اعادہ نہ ہوگا مدعی بینه قائم نہ کر سکا تو قاضی شر کاء سے حلف لے صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ دعوی قبول ہی نہ کیا جائے خصم کا قول معتبر ہے ایک شریک تقسیم سے حاصل ہونے والے پر عدم قبضہ کا دعوی کرے اسیم فسخ ہوگی یا نہیں دونوں شر کا ء قیمت لگانے میں اختلاف کریں تو التفات نہ کیا جائے شرکاء نے آپس میں تقسیم کی پھر اختلاف کیا ایک دعوی کرے اور دور امنکر ہو تو کیا حکم ہے؟ دونوں نے حدود میں اختلاف کیا اور بینہ بھی قائم کر دیئے تو کیا کیا ئے گا ؟ کوئی مستحق نکل آئے تو کیا حکم ہوگا، اقوال فقہاء
The two partitioners divided among the partners, then the partners disagreed: someone said, 'I did not receive my share, although my share includes such-and-such room,' and the two partitioners testified that he took it. Then the testimony will be accepted. The evidence of Imam Muhammad, the evidence of the two shaykhs. The viewpoint of Imam Tahawi. The author of Al-Hidayah's criticism of Imam Tahawi's evidence: the testimony of one partitioner is not acceptable. Chapter of claim of error in division and entitlement therein. If a partner claims an error in the division, the division will not be repeated. If the claimant cannot produce evidence, the judge takes an oath from the partners. The author of Al-Hidayah says the claim should not even be accepted. The word of the defendant is credible. If one partner claims non-possession of what he received from the division, will it be rescinded or not? If both partners disagree on valuation, it is not considered. The partners divided among themselves, then disagreed: one claims and the other denies, what is the ruling? If both disagreed on boundaries and both produced evidence, what should be done? If a claimant appears, what is the ruling? Statements of the jurists.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings from the chapter on claims of error in division. It begins with the scenario where two partitioners (qasiman) have divided property among partners, and then a partner claims he did not receive his share. If the two partitioners both testify that he did receive it, their testimony is accepted. The passage then references the evidence of Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), and the viewpoint of Imam Tahawi, but does not elaborate the differences. The author of Al-Hidayah criticizes Imam Tahawi's proof, stating that the testimony of a single partitioner is not acceptable. The chapter title is given. The rulings that follow include: if a partner claims an error in division, the division is not repeated; if the claimant has no evidence, the judge takes an oath from the partners; the author of Al-Hidayah holds that such a claim should not even be entertained; the defendant's statement is credible; a claim of non-possession of a specific share may or may not rescind the division; disagreements on valuation are ignored; if one partner claims and another denies, the ruling is unclear; if both disagree on boundaries and each produces evidence, the procedure is unspecified; if a rightful claimant appears, the ruling is given. These are summarized statements of the jurists, likely from the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
قاسم (qasim): A partitioner who divides jointly owned property among partners.
دعویٰ (da'wa): A legal claim made by a partner regarding an error in division or non-receipt of share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if two partitioners testify that a partner received his share after the partner claims otherwise?
A) The testimony is rejected
B) The testimony is accepted
C) The partner must take an oath
D) The division is repeated

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi procedure, a claim of error in division is resolved through evidence: two partitioners' testimony is conclusive, while a single partitioner's testimony is rejected; if no evidence, the defendant's oath settles the matter and the division stands.

Slaughter: Definition and Condition in the Hanafi School
Opening of the chapter on slaughter: definition and condition of halal slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for valid slaughter (dhabih) and distinguish between the two types (ikhtiyari and idtirari).

Core Idea
Slaughter is a condition for halal meat; it is valid only from a Muslim or Kitabi outside the Haram.

This passage opens the chapter on slaughter (Kitab al-Dhabaih) in the Hidayah. It establishes the foundational rule: for meat to be halal and pure, the animal must be slaughtered properly. The author then introduces two categories of slaughter based on circumstances and states the essential condition regarding the person performing the slaughter. Understanding this baseline is crucial for the detailed rules that follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and definition
The passage begins with the ruling: slaughter (dhakat) is a condition for meat to be halal and tahir (pure). Recognize that this makes dhakat a prerequisite, not a recommended act.
The term 'dhakat' is used here as a technical term for ritual slaughter.
2
Distinguish the two types
The author divides dhabihah (the act of slaughter) into two types: ikhtiyari (voluntary, normal slaughter) and idtirari (emergency slaughter, e.g., when the animal is about to die and proper slaughter is impossible).
Idtirari applies only when one cannot perform normal slaughter; its rules differ slightly.
3
State the condition
The condition for valid slaughter is twofold: (1) the slaughterer must be a Muslim or a Kitabi (Jew/Christian), and (2) the animal must be outside the Haram (the sacred precinct of Makkah).
Kitabi includes Jews and Christians; other non-Muslims are excluded.
4
Apply the condition to a scenario
Consider a Muslim slaughtering an animal inside the Haram: the meat is not halal because the location condition fails. Similarly, a Kitabi slaughtering outside the Haram yields halal meat.
The condition of 'outside Haram' refers to the boundaries of the Haram of Makkah, not other places.
5
Note the implication for later rulings
This condition sets the qualification of the slaughterer. Later rules will address the tools and method of slaughter, but the person's religion and the location are the primary conditions.
If the condition is not met, the meat is considered maytah (carrion) and is impermissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الذبائح
گوشت کی حلت وطہارت کے لیے ذبح شرط ہے ذکاۃ کی دو قسمیں ہیں، ذبیح اختیاری و اضطراری
ذبح کی شرط یہ ہے کہ ذابح مسلمان یا کتابی ہو نیز حلال اور حرم سے باہر ہو
Book of Slaughter. For meat to be permissible (halal) and pure (tahir), slaughter is a condition. There are two types of dhabihah: voluntary (ikhtiyari) and emergency (idtirari). The condition of slaughter is that the slaughterer be a Muslim or a Kitabi (People of the Book), and that the animal be outside the Haram (sanctuary).
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on slaughter (Kitab al-Dhabaih). It lays down two fundamental points: (1) Slaughter is a prerequisite for meat to be halal and tahir (ritually pure). (2) Dhabihah (the act of slaughter) is of two types: ikhtiyari (voluntary, i.e., normal slaughter) and idtirari (forced or emergency, as when one cannot perform normal slaughter). The condition for valid slaughter is that the person performing it (dhabih) must be either a Muslim or a Kitabi (a Jew or Christian). Additionally, the animal must be outside the boundaries of the Haram (the sacred precinct of Makkah) – meaning that hunting or slaughtering within the Haram is restricted. This concise statement sets the stage for further details on the rules of slaughter according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ذبیح (dhabīḥ): The animal that is slaughtered; also means the act of slaughter.
ذکاۃ (dhakāt): The ritual method of slaughtering an animal to make it permissible to eat.
اختیاری و اضطراری (ikhtiyārī wa iḍṭirārī): Voluntary and emergency; two categories of slaughter based on circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is valid to perform slaughter for halal meat?
A) Only a Muslim.
B) A Muslim or a Kitabi.
C) Any person of any religion.
D) Only a male Muslim.

Key Takeaway
Slaughter (dhabih) is a condition for halal meat; valid only when performed by a Muslim or Kitabi and the animal is outside the Haram.

The Definition and Components of Shuf'ah (Pre-emption)
Definitional introduction to shuf'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define shuf'ah technically, identify its cause, condition, and pillar, and explain why the Book of Shuf'ah is placed after the Book of Ghasp.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah is a permissible right to purchase immovable property from a buyer due to partnership or adjacency.

This lesson introduces the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) in Hanafi fiqh. You will learn why the author placed this book after ghasp (usurpation), the linguistic and technical definitions of shuf'ah, and its essential components: cause, condition, and pillar. Understanding these foundations is crucial for later detailed rulings.

Guided Path
1
Understand the placement after ghasp
Identify the connection between shuf'ah and ghasp: both involve taking property without consent. Since ghasp is unlawful and its avoidance is obligatory, it is placed first. Shuf'ah is permitted but not obligatory.
This ordering reflects the fiqh principle of prioritizing obligations over permissions.
2
Analyze the linguistic meaning
Shuf'ah is derived from shaf' (to join). The pre-emptor joins the purchased property to his own land.
The linguistic root helps remember the function of shuf'ah.
3
Grasp the technical definition
The technical definition: acquisition of immovable property at the price paid by the purchaser due to partnership or adjacency. Break down each component: acquisition, price, partnership/adjacency, immovability.
This definition distinguishes shuf'ah from other forms of acquisition.
4
Identify the components of shuf'ah
Extract the cause (sabab: partnership or adjacency), condition (shart: immovable property), pillar (rukn: the shafi's taking from a contracting party), ruling (hukm: permissibility of demand), and description (it is like a new purchase).
These components will be used in later lessons to verify valid shuf'ah claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
كتاب الشفعة
ترجمہ یہ کتاب شفعہ کے بیان میں ہے
مصنف کتاب الغصب سے فراغت کے بعد یہاں سے کتاب الشفعہ کا آغاز فرمارہے ہیں۔
سوال كتب الشفعہ کو کتاب الغصب سے مؤخر کیوں کیا ؟ اور دونوں میں مناسبت کیا ہے؟
جواب وجہ مناسبت تو یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں میں دوسرے کے مال کا بغیر رضامندی کے تملک ہوتا ہے لیکن چونکہ شفعہ مشروع اور غصب امر غیر مشروع ہے تو انصاف کا تقاضہ یہ تھا کہ مشروع کو غیر مشروع پر مقدم کیا جاتا لیکن چونکہ غصب سے بچنا ضروری ہے اور شفعہ میں مکان وغیرہ لینا جائز ہے نہ کہ واجب و ضروری اس وجہ سے جس سے اجتناب لازم ہے اس کو مقدم کر دیا۔
شفعہ کا لغوی و شرعی معنی ، وجہ تسمیہ
الشفعة مشتقة من الشفع وهو الضم سميت بها لما فيها من ضم المشتراة الى عقار الشفيع ترجمہ شفعہ شفع سے مشتق ہے اور وہ ( شفع ) ملانا ہے نام رکھا گیا شفعہ شفعہ کے ساتھ اس وجہ سے کہ شفعہ میں مشتراۃ کو ملانا ہے شفیع کی زمین کی جانب۔ تشریح یہاں سے مصنف تشفعہ کی تعریف کر رہے ہیں کہتے ہیں کہ شفعہ شفع سے مشتق ہے جس کے معنی ملانے کے ہیں۔ سوال اب سوال پیدا ہوا کہ معنی لغوی اور اصطلاحی میں کیا مناسبت ہے؟ جواب تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ ملانے کے معنی شفعہ اصطلاحی کے اندر بھی موجود ہیں کیونکہ شفعہ کے اندر شفیع مبیع کو اپنی زمین میں ملا لیتا ہے۔
شفع کے اصل معنی ہیں ضم مثلہ الیہ یعنی کسی شیء کو اس کی مثل کی جانب ملادینا مصنف نے اختصار املانے پر اکتفا کر لیا۔ شفعہ کی اصطلاحی تعریف ایسے کی جاتی ہے:
هي تملک البقعة بما قام على المشترى بالشركة او الجوار
سبب شفعہ شفیع کی ملکیت کا مبیع کے ساتھ اتصال ہے خواہ بطریق شرکت ہو یا بطریق جواز ۔ اور شرط حل شفعہ کا غیر منقول ہونا ہے
اور رکن شفعہ متعاقدین میں سے کسی ایک سے شفیع کا لینا ہے اور حکم شفعہ متحقق سبب کے وقت طلب کا جواز ہے اور شفعہ کی صفت یہ ہے کہ اس
کو لینا شراء جدید کے درجہ میں ہے۔ والبسط فی الشامی ج ۵ ص ۳۸۔
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The Book of Shuf'ah. Translation: This book is about the explanation of shuf'ah. The author, after completing the Book of Ghasp (usurpation), begins here with the Book of Shuf'ah. Question: Why was the Book of Shuf'ah placed after the Book of Ghasp? And what is the connection between the two? Answer: The reason for the connection is that in both, ownership of another's property is taken without consent. But since shuf'ah is legislated and ghasp is unlawful, justice would require that the legislated be given precedence over the unlawful. However, since avoiding ghasp is obligatory and taking property in shuf'ah is permissible, not obligatory, the one from which avoidance is necessary was given precedence. The linguistic and legal meaning of shuf'ah and the reason for its naming: Al-Shuf'ah is derived from al-shaf' which means joining. It was named thus because it involves joining the purchased property to the estate of the shafi' (pre-emptor). Translation: Shuf'ah is derived from shaf', and it (shaf') means to join. It was named shuf'ah because in shuf'ah, the thing purchased is joined to the land of the shafi'. Explanation: Here the author is defining shuf'ah. He says that shuf'ah is derived from shaf', which means to join. Question: Now a question arises: what is the connection between the linguistic and legal meanings? Answer: The answer was given that the meaning of joining is also present in the technical shuf'ah, because in shuf'ah, the shafi' joins the sold property to his own land. The original meaning of shaf' is joining something to its like. The author sufficed with the concise meaning of 'joining'. The technical definition of shuf'ah is: It is the acquisition of the property at the price paid by the purchaser due to partnership or adjacency. Cause: The shafi''s ownership is connected to the sold property either by partnership or adjacency. Condition: The subject of shuf'ah must be immovable property. Pillar: The shafi''s taking from one of the contracting parties. Ruling: When the cause is realized, the shafi''s demand is permissible. Description: Taking it is like a new purchase. And the details are in al-Shami, vol. 5, p. 38.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This is a definitional introduction to the Book of Shuf'ah (Pre-emption) in Ashraf al-Hidayah. The author begins by explaining why this book is placed after the Book of Ghasp (usurpation). Both involve taking another's property without consent, but ghasp is unlawful and shuf'ah is legislated. Since avoiding ghasp is obligatory, it takes precedence in order. Then the author defines shuf'ah linguistically and technically. Linguistically, it is derived from shaf' (joining). Technically, it is the acquisition of an immovable property at the price paid by the purchaser due to partnership or adjacency. The author enumerates the components of shuf'ah: cause (partnership or adjacency), condition (immovability), pillar (the shafi' taking from a contracting party), ruling (permissibility of demand when cause exists), and description (it is like a new purchase). The passage ends with a reference to al-Shami for details.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'ah): The right of pre-emption: acquisition of immovable property at the price paid by the purchaser by virtue of partnership or adjacency.
شفيع (shafi'): The person entitled to pre-emption (the pre-emptor).
شركة (shirkah): Partnership in ownership of the property giving right to pre-emption.
جوار (jiwar): Adjacency or neighborhood in property, giving right to pre-emption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the Book of Shuf'ah placed after the Book of Ghasp?
A) Because both involve ownership without consent, but ghasp is unlawful and avoiding it is obligatory.
B) Because shuf'ah is more important than ghasp.
C) Because ghasp is a type of shuf'ah.
D) Because the author forgot the ordering.

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah is a permissible right to acquire immovable property from a buyer due to partnership or adjacency, and its essential components are cause (shirkah/jiwar), condition (immovability), and pillar (the shafi's demand).

Shuf'ah by Neighbourhood: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Presents Shafi'i denial and Hanafi proof of shuf'ah by jiwar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Shafi'i objection to shuf'ah by neighbourhood and explain the Hanafi proof using qiyas on the effective cause of permanent attachment.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah by neighbourhood is justified by permanent property attachment causing harm, analogous to the co-owner case.

This lesson examines the classical disagreement between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i on whether the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) extends to mere neighbours. The Shafi'i position restricts shuf'ah to undivided co-ownership, while the Hanafis extend it to neighbours based on the common effective cause of permanent attachment and harm. We will unpack the arguments on both sides and see how the Hanafi response uses qiyas and rebuts the Shafi'i claim that shuf'ah is khilaf al-qiyas.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and the disputed category
Confirm that the Hanafi school recognizes shuf'ah for four categories: co-owner in property, co-owner in rights, neighbour, and owner of attachments. This lesson focuses on the neighbour.
The passage contrasts with Shafi'i who only accepts the first category.
2
Identify the opponent and their primary proofs
Imam al-Shafi'i denies shuf'ah by neighbourhood using two proofs: (1) the hadith 'al-shuf'ah fīmā lam yuqsam' and (2) the rational argument that shuf'ah is khilaf al-qiyās and therefore confined to its specific textual case.
The hadith is quoted in the passage; note the Shafi'i method of restricting the scope.
3
Follow the opponent's proof: the khilaf al-qiyas argument
The Shafi'i argues that shuf'ah forces ownership without consent, deviating from standard analogy; thus it cannot be extended beyond the text. The textual case is undivided property only.
This is a methodological objection: if a ruling is an exception, it cannot be analogized.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response: establishing qiyas
The Hanafis respond that the effective cause ('illa) in the original case is the permanent connection causing harm of neighbourhood, not simply the harm of division. This cause is equally present in the neighbour's case, justifying qiyas. They also cite their own hadith narrations.
The passage identifies the 'illa as ittiṣāl ta'bīd wa qarār (permanent and stable connection) leading to ḍarar al-jiwār.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In a Hanafi jurisdiction, a neighbour can pre-empt the sale of an adjacent property; in a Shafi'i jurisdiction, he cannot.
Also the order of priority among multiple claimants differs between the schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال الشافعي لاشفعة بالجوار لقوله عليه السلام الشفعة فيما لم يقسم فاذا وقعت الحدود وصرفت الطرق فلا شفعة ولان حق الشفعة معدول به عن سنن القياس لما فيه من تملك المال على الغير من غير رضاه وقدورد الشرع به فيما لم يقسم وهذا ليس في معناه لأن مؤنة القسمة تلزمه في الاصل دون الفرع ترجمہ اور فرمایا شافعی نے پڑوس کی وجہ سے شفعہ نہیں ہے نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان الشفعتہ الخ کی وجہ سے اور اس لئے کہ حق شفعہ ہٹا ہوا ہے قیاس کی روشوں سے اسلئے کہ اس میں غیر کے مال کا مالک ہوتا ہے بغیر اس کی رضامندی کے حالانکہ شریعت وارد ہوئی ہے اس کے ساتھ (حق شفعہ ) ایسی زمین میں جس کی تقسیم نہ ہوئی ہو اور یہ (جار) نہیں ہے اس کے معنی میں ( مورد شرع کے معنی میں ) اسلئے کہ ہوارہ کی مشقت لازم آتی ہے شفیع کو اصل میں نہ کہ فرع میں۔ تشریح امام شافعی فقتها شریک فی مین اسمیع کیلئے شفعہ کے قائل ہیں لہذا انہوں نے جوار کی وجہ سے ثبوت شفعہ کا انکار فرمایا۔ پھر اس پر انہوں نے ایک حدیث پیش فرمائی ، کہ شفعہ ایسی زمین میں ہے جس میں بلوارہ نہ ہوا ہو جب حدود واقع ہو گئیں اور راستے پھیر لئے گئے تو پھر شفعہ نہیں ملے گا۔ بہر حال اس حدیث سے بظاہر صاف یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ نفس جوار کی وجہ سے بغیر شرکت شفعہ نہیں ہے۔ یہ امام شافعی کی نفلی دلیل ہے اور عقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حق شفعہ تو خلاف قیاس ہے کیونکہ اس میں بغیر مالک کی رضامندی کے اسکے مال کا مالک ہونا ہوتا ہے اور اصول یہ مقرر ہے کہ جو چیز خلاف قیاس ہوتی ہے وہ مورد شرع تک رہتی ہے اور بقول شافعی مور د شرع فقط غیر مقسوم جائیداد ہے۔ اور باقی کو مور د شرع اصل مذکور کی وجہ سے قیاس نہیں کر سکتے ۔ معلوم ہوا کہ غیر کیلئے ثبوت شفعہ کی کوئی صورت بھی نہیں ہے وهذا ليس في معناه اور یہ یعنی جار مورد شرع کے معنی میں نہیں ہے۔ یعنی امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں ثبوت شفعہ کا اصل راز یہ ہے کہ مالک کو ہوارہ کا ضرر لاحق نہ ہو یعنی دو شریک ہیں ایک نے اپنا حصہ فروخت کر دیا اب دوسرے ساتھی کو مشتری سے نا چار ہزارہ کرنا پڑے گا تو اس شریک کو بٹوارہ کی مشقت سے بچانے کیلئے حق شفعہ دے دیا گیا۔ لیکن جار میں یہ بات نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہاں اشتراک ہی نہیں ہے اس کو کہا اور یہ یعنی جار نہیں ہے موردِ شرع کے درجہ میں اب اس کی وجہ بتائی۔ اسلئے کہ بنوارہ کی مشقت لازم آتی ہے اس کو اصل میں نہ کہ فرع میں ، اصل سے مراد مور د شرع اور فرع سے مراد غیر مور د شرع یعنی جار، امام شافعی کے دلائل نام ہوئے آگے ہمارے دلائل ہیں۔
ولنا ماروينا ولان ملكه متصل بملک الدخيل اتصال تابيد وقرار فيثبت له حق الشفعة عند وجود المعاوضة بالمال اعتبارا بمورد الشرع وهذا لان الاتصال على هذه الصفة انما انتصب سببا فيه لدفع ضرر الجواران هو مادة المضار على ما عرف وقطع هذه المادة بتملك الاصيل اولى لان الضرر في حقه بازعاجه عن خطته ابائه أقوى وضرر القسمة مشروع لا يصلح علة لتحقيق ضرر غيره
ترجمہ اور یہاں دلیل وہ روایات ہیں جو ہم روایت کر چکے ہیں، اور اسلئے کہ شفیع کی ملکیت مشتری کی ملکیت کے ساتھ متصل ہے اتصال تابید و قرار کیسا تھ تو ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ شفیع کیلئے حق شفعہ معاوضہ بالمال کے پائے جانے کے وقت مور د شرع پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے اور یہ حکم اس وجہ سے کہ اس صورت پر اتصال قائم ہوا ہے۔ سبب بن کر مور د شرع میں جوار کے ضرر کو دور کرنے کیلئے اسلئے کہ یہی (جوار) تمام معزتوں کی جڑ ہے جیسا کہ معروف ہے اور اس مادہ ضرور کو ختم کرنا شفیع کے مالک ہونے کے ذریعہ اولیٰ ہے اسلئے کہ ضر شفیع کے حق میں زیادہ قوی ہے اس کے دور کرنے کی وجہ سے اس کے اباء کے خطہ سے اور بٹوارہ کا ضرر مشروع ہے جو اس کے غیر کے ضر رکو ثابت کرنے کیلئے علت بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا۔ تشریح فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم تینوں قسم کے شفیع کیلئے جو شفعہ کے بارے میں تین حدیثیں پیش کر چکے ہیں ۔ جن سے امام شافعی کی تقریر بے جان ہو جاتی ہے کہ مقیس علیہ خلاف قیاس ہے یہ تقریر تو اسی وقت صحیح ہوئی کہ بقیہ دونوں کیلئے احادیث سے شفعہ کا ثبوت نہ ہوتا۔ پھر اگر آپ کی بات کو بالفرض تسلیم کر لیا جائے تو ہم یہ کہیں گے کہ مور د شرع میں شفعہ مفت نہیں ملا بلکہ معاوضہ کے ساتھ ملا ہے یعنی شفیع نے مالی معاوضہ دے کر مشتری سے گھر لیا ہے تو مقیس کے اندر بھی شفعہ کا ثبوت اسی طرح ہونا چاہئے یعنی معاوضہ مال کے ساتھ جبکہ مقیس علیہ کے اندر ثبوت شفعہ خلاف قیاس نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ شفیع کو مقیس علیہ میں شفعہ اسلئے ملا ہے کہ شفیع کی ملکیت مشتری کی ملکیت کے ساتھ متصل ہے اور یہ اتصال عارضی نہیں بلکہ دائمی ہے کیونکہ یہ اپنی زمین کو اٹھا کر لے جائے ایسا نہیں ہو سکتا۔ اس کو مصنف نے اتصال تابید و قرار سے تعبیر کیا ہے اور علت یعنی اتصال مذکور جوار کے اندر بھی موجود ہے لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ منفیس علیہ اور منفیس میں علت جامعہ مشترک ہے پھر اس کو خلاف قیاس کہنا اور باقی کو مور د شرع پر قیاس نہ کرنا کیسے صحیح ہوگا کیونکہ جہاں اس قسم کا اتصال ہوگا تو یہ ثبوت شفعہ کا سبب بنے گا تا کہ ضرر جوار دور ہو سکے اس لئے کہ یہی جوار مضرتوں کی جڑ ہے جیسا کہ برے پڑوسیوں کے درمیان اس کا ہر روز مشاہدہ ہوتا ہے۔ سوال .. جب شفیع کو معضرت ، جوار سے بچانا ہے تو اسکی صورت یہ بھی تو ہوسکتی ہے کہ شفیع کا مکان بھی مشتری کو دلوادیا جائے بجائے اس کے کہ مشتری کا مکان شفیع کو دلوایا جائے؟ جواب تو اس کا جواب دیا و قطع المادة ... الخ سے یعنی اس صورت میں حرج کثیر ہے کیونکہ شفیع کو اس کے آباء واجداد کے گھر سے علیحدہ کرنا لازم آتا ہے اسلئے آسان صورت وہی ہے کہ شفیع کو مشتری کا مکان دلوا دیا جائے ، پھر وضرر القسمہ الخ سے امام شافعی کا جواب ہے کہ آپ نے علت شفعہ ضر ر قسمت بیان کی ہے۔ محل تامل ہے کیونکہ ضر ر قسمت تو امر مشروع ہے لہذا اگر دو شریکوں میں سے کوئی قسمت کا دعوی کرے تو بڑارہ کر دیا جاتا ہے معلوم ہوا کہ امر مشروع دوسرے کو نقصان پہنچانے کی علت نہیں بن سکتا بلکہ علت اتصال تابید ہی ہے جیسا کہ ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔ یہاں تک کہ مصنف نے ثبوت پر گفتگو کی ہے آگے ترتیب پر گفتگو فرمائیں گے۔
And al-Shafi'i said: There is no shuf'ah by neighbourhood, because of his (peace be upon him) statement: 'Shuf'ah is in what has not been divided; when boundaries are set and roads are turned, then no shuf'ah.' And because the right of shuf'ah is deviated from the ways of analogy, due to what it entails of owning the property of another without his consent, and the Shariah has come with it in what has not been divided, and this (neighbour) is not in its meaning, because the burden of division is necessary for him (the sharer) in the original case, not in the branch. Translation: And al-Shafi'i said: There is no shuf'ah due to neighbourhood, because of the Prophet's statement (peace be upon him) 'al-shuf'ah...' and because the right of shuf'ah is removed from the ways of analogy because it involves owning someone else's property without his consent, even though the Shariah has come with it (the right of shuf'ah) in land that has not been divided, and this (neighbour) is not in its meaning (the meaning of the legal case) because the hardship of division is incumbent on the shafi' in the original case, not in the branch. Commentary: Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) believes in shuf'ah for the partner in the thing sold, so he denied the proof of shuf'ah due to neighbourhood. Then he adduced a hadith that shuf'ah is in land that has not been divided; when boundaries are set and roads are turned, then there is no shuf'ah. In any case, from this hadith it appears clearly that there is no shuf'ah due to mere neighbourhood without partnership. This is Imam al-Shafi'i's transmitted proof. And the rational proof is that the right of shuf'ah is contrary to analogy, because it involves owning someone's property without the owner's consent, and the principle is that something contrary to analogy remains confined to the legal case, and according to al-Shafi'i the legal case is only undivided property. And the rest cannot be analogized to the mentioned legal case. So it is understood that there is no way to prove shuf'ah for others. 'And this is not in its meaning' means the neighbour is not in the meaning of the legal case. That is, Imam al-Shafi'i says: The underlying secret of the proof of shuf'ah is that the owner should not suffer the harm of division; i.e., there are two partners, one sold his share; now the other partner will have to endure hardship from the buyer; so to save that partner from the trouble of division, the right of shuf'ah was given. But this is not present in the neighbour, because there is no partnership there. So the neighbour is not in the category of the legal case. Then he gave the reason: because the hardship of division is necessary for him in the original case, not in the branch. The original means the legal case, and the branch means what is not the legal case, i.e., the neighbour. These are the proofs of Imam al-Shafi'i; now are our proofs. And our proof: what we have narrated, and because his property is connected to the property of the buyer with a permanent and stable connection, so the right of shuf'ah is established for him when compensation with property is present, by analogy with the legal case. And this is because the connection in this manner has been set up as a cause to repel the harm of neighbourhood, for it is the source of harms, as is known, and cutting off this source by ownership of the original owner is more appropriate, because the harm to him is stronger due to his being uprooted from the land of his forefathers, and the harm of division is legitimate (recognized by Shariah) and is not suitable as a cause to establish harm to another. Translation: And here the proof is the narrations that we have narrated, and because the property of the shafi' is connected to the property of the buyer with a permanent and stable connection, so the right of shuf'ah will be established for the shafi' when compensation with property is found, using analogy on the legal case. And this ruling is because the connection in this form has been established as a cause to repel the harm of neighbourhood, because this (neighbourhood) is the root of all harms, as is known, and cutting off this source by making the shafi' the owner is more appropriate, because the harm to the shafi' is stronger in his being removed from the land of his forefathers, and the harm of division is legitimate and cannot be a cause to prove harm to another. Commentary: He (the author) says: We have presented three hadiths regarding shuf'ah for all three types of shafi', which render Imam al-Shafi'i's argument lifeless that the analogized-from (original case) is contrary to analogy. This argument would only be valid if the other two types did not have proof of shuf'ah from hadiths. Then if your statement is hypothetically accepted, we would say: In the legal case, shuf'ah was not given for free but with compensation; i.e., the shafi' took the house from the buyer by paying monetary consideration, so in the analogized case, the proof of shuf'ah should also be similarly with monetary compensation, while in the analogized-from (original case), the proof of shuf'ah is not contrary to analogy. Because the shafi' got shuf'ah in the analogized case because his property is connected to the buyer's property, and this connection is not temporary but permanent, because he cannot lift his land and take it away. The author expressed this as 'permanent and stable connection.' And the cause, i.e., the mentioned connection, is also present in the neighbour; therefore it became known that the analogized-from and the analogized-to share a common effective cause. So how can it be correct to call it contrary to analogy and not analogize the rest to the legal case? Because wherever this kind of connection exists, it will be a cause for the proof of shuf'ah so that the harm of neighbourhood can be avoided, because this neighbourhood is the root of harms, as is observed daily among bad neighbours. Question: When the shafi' is to be saved from the harm of neighbourhood, could it also be possible that the shafi's house is given to the buyer instead of the buyer's house being given to the shafi'? Answer: He answered this from 'qata' al-madah...' i.e., in that case there is great difficulty because it requires removing the shafi' from the house of his ancestors; therefore the easier way is that the shafi' is given the buyer's house. Then from 'wa darar al-qismah...' it is the answer to Imam al-Shafi'i that you have stated the cause of shuf'ah as the harm of division. This is questionable because the harm of division is a legitimate matter; therefore if one of two partners demands division, it is carried out. It became known that a legitimate matter cannot be a cause for causing harm to another; rather the cause is permanent connection, as we have mentioned. Up to this point the author has discussed the proof; next he will discuss the order.
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage presents the inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i on the issue of shuf'ah by neighbourhood (jiwār). The Shafi'i position is that shuf'ah is only established for a co-owner in undivided property (sharīk fī al-mabī'), not for a neighbour. Their proof includes the hadith 'al-shuf'ah fīmā lam yuqsam' and the argument that shuf'ah is a right that deviates from standard legal analogy (khilāf al-qiyās) because it forces ownership without consent; it is therefore restricted to the precise case specified by the Shariah (undivided property). The Hanafi response cites their own hadith narrations (mentioned previously) and uses a qiyas argument: the permanent attachment (ittiṣāl ta'bīd wa qarār) between the neighbour's property and the buyer's property is the same effective cause ('illa) as in the case of the co-owner, because it causes harm of neighbourhood. This harm is greater than the harm of division (which is a legitimate process and thus cannot be the cause). The passage further addresses a possible objection: if the aim is to remove harm from the shafi', why not give the shafi's property to the buyer? The answer is that this would cause greater harm by uprooting the shafi' from his ancestral home. Thus the Hanafi school establishes shuf'ah for neighbours based on analogy and istihsan.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf'ah): The right of pre-emption: a legal right to take ownership of property sold to another party under certain conditions, particularly to prevent harm.
الجوار (al-jiwār): Neighbourhood, adjacency of properties that are not shared in ownership.
اتصال التأبيد (ittiṣāl al-tabīd): Permanent connection of properties that cannot be moved apart, unlike temporary connection.
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning in legal theory; applying a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause.
خلاف القياس (khilāf al-qiyās): A ruling that deviates from standard analogical reasoning, often based on explicit text or necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the effective cause ('illa) identified by the Hanafis to establish shuf'ah for the neighbour?
A) The harm of division (darar al-qismah)
B) The permanent connection between properties causing harm of neighbourhood
C) The consent of the buyer
D) The proximity of the properties, regardless of attachment

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school extends shuf'ah to neighbours based on the common effective cause of permanent property attachment causing harm, using qiyas despite the Shafi'i objection that shuf'ah is an exception.

Priority of Shuf'ah Claimants: Sharīk, Khalīṭ, Shafī'
Establishes order of shuf'ah claimants via hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the order of priority among shuf'ah claimants according to the Hanafi school and apply it to a given scenario.

Core Idea
The co-owner in the property itself has the strongest right of shuf'ah, then the co-owner in rights, then the neighbour.

This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes the sequence of entitlement when multiple parties could claim shuf'ah (right of pre-emption) on a property sale. The Prophet's hadith defines a clear ranking based on the strength of connection to the property. Understanding this order is essential for correctly adjudicating shuf'ah claims in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three claimants
From the hadith, list the three types: sharīk (co-owner in the actual property), khalīṭ (co-owner in rights), and shafī' (neighbour).
Shafī' here is specifically the neighbour, not a general term.
2
Understand the priority order
The hadith states 'sharīk aḥaqq min al-khalīṭ, wa al-khalīṭ aḥaqq min al-shafī'. This means sharīk has superior right, then khalīṭ, then shafī'.
The word aḥaqq indicates a legal priority.
3
Apply the order
In a case where a property is sold, first offer shuf'ah to the sharīk; if he declines, to the khalīṭ; then to the neighbour.
If any prior claimant waives his right, the next in line may claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واما الترتيب فلقوله عليه السلام الشريك احق من الخليط والخليط احق من الشفيع فالشريك في نفس المبيع والخليط في حقوق المبيع والشفيع هو الجار ولان الاتصال بالشركة في المبيع أقوى لانه في كل
And as for the order, because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'The sharīk has more right than the khalīṭ, and the khalīṭ has more right than the shafī'.' So the sharīk is in the very thing sold, the khalīṭ is in the rights of the thing sold, and the shafī' is the neighbour. And because the connection by partnership in the thing sold is stronger, because it is in every part.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on the order (tartīb) of priority among shuf'ah claimants. The Prophet (peace be upon him) declared that the sharīk (co-owner in the same property being sold) has a stronger right than the khalīṭ (one who shares in the rights, such as right of pre-emption or way), and the khalīṭ has a stronger right than the shafī' (which is here defined as the neighbour). The reason given is that the connection (ittiṣāl) of the sharīk with the sold property is stronger because he owns a part of it, whereas the khalīṭ only has rights, and the neighbour merely has proximity. This order means that if at the time of sale there are multiple potential claimants, the sharīk is given the first chance to exercise shuf'ah; if he declines, then the khalīṭ; if he declines, then the neighbour. The basis is the strength of connection to the property. The hadith is the primary evidence, and the reasoning supports it.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartīb): The order of priority among shuf'ah claimants: sharīk, then khalīṭ, then shafī' (neighbour).
الخليط (al-khalīṭ): A person who shares rights associated with the property, such as rights of way or irrigation, but not ownership of the property itself.
الشفيع (al-shafī'): Here specifically means the neighbour (jār), but in other contexts can include all claimants; in this hadith, it is the neighbour.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith in this passage, who has the highest priority to claim shuf'ah?
A) The neighbour (al-shafī')
B) The co-owner in rights (al-khalīṭ)
C) The co-owner in the property itself (al-sharīk)
D) All have equal right

Key Takeaway
The order of shuf'ah claimants is based on strength of connection: co-owner, then rights-holder, then neighbour.

Priority Order of Pre-emptors: Co-owner, Partner in Rights, Neighbor
Explains the priority hierarchy among pre-emptors with textual and rational proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi priority order of pre-emptors, identify the three categories (sharik, khalit, jar), and apply the order in a given scenario while noting the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
The strength of connection determines priority: co-owner first, then partner in rights, then neighbor.

Pre-emption (shuf'ah) gives a prior right to purchase property from an outsider. But who among several claimants has the strongest right? The Hanafi school has a clear hierarchy based on the strength of the connection (ittisal) to the property. In this passage, Al-Marghinani lays down the order — co-owner, partner in rights, neighbor — supported by the Prophet's hadith and rational proof. We'll also see an important intra-madhhab disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and a response to Imam Shafi'i's theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hadith and Categories
Locate the hadith cited: 'The partner is more entitled than the associate, and the associate is more entitled than the neighbor.' Identify the three categories: sharik (co-owner in property), khalit (partner in rights), and jar (neighbor).
The hadith is the primary textual proof.
2
Understand the Rational Proof (Strength of Cause)
The text argues that preference (tarjih) is based on the strength of the cause (sabab). The co-owner's connection covers every part; the partner in rights shares usufructs; the neighbor's connection is weakest. This yields the order.
This is a qiyas argument: the stronger the ittisal, the stronger the right.
3
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Note that Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the co-owner absolutely excludes all others, even if he relinquishes. Zahir al-Riwayah (the relied-upon position) says the right passes to the next in line if the prior waives it.
The conflict is about the nature of the exclusion: absolute vs. sequential.
4
Examine the Shafi'i Counter-Argument and Hanafi Response
Imam Shafi'i considers the harm of division (darar al-qismah) as the cause of pre-emption. The Hanafi response: harm of division is not a valid cause but can act as a preferrer (murajjih). This limits the scope of pre-emption.
The difference affects when pre-emption arises and who gets priority.
5
Apply the Priority Order
Work through a scenario: if a co-owner, a partner in an irrigation right, and a neighbor all claim pre-emption, determine who gets it. If the co-owner waives, the right passes to the partner in rights, then to the neighbor (according to Zahir al-Riwayah).
The neighbor is defined as the one adjoining the rear of the property with a door in a different alley.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۳ الشريك فى الرقبة لاشفعة لغيره سلم او استوفى لأنهم محجوبون به ترجمه پس اگر دست برداری دے دے وہ ( شریک فی الرقبة ) تو شفعہ راستہ کے شریک کیلئے ہے اگر وہ بھی دست برداری دے دے تو لے لے گا اس کو پڑوسی اسی ترتیب کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور اس جار سے مراد جار ملاصق ہے اور وہ وہ ہے جو دار مشفوعہ کی پشت پر ہو اور اس کا دروازہ دوسری گلی میں ہو اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ شریک فی الرقبہ کے ہوتے ہوئے اس کے غیر کیلئے شفعہ نہیں ہے وہ دست برداری دے یا لے اس لئے کہ وہ شریک کی وجہ سے محجوب ہیں۔
تشریح یعنی شنعاء کے درمیان ترتیب وہی ہے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں لیکن اگر شریک فی الرقبہ شفعہ نہ لے تو شریک فی الطریق اس کو لے سکتا ہے اور اگر وہ نہ لے تو پھر جار لے سکتا ہے۔ پھر مصنف نے جار کی تفسیر کی کہ وہ وہ ہے جو دار شفوعہ کی پشت پر ہو اور اس کا دروازہ دوسری گلی میں ہو ۔ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ دادی کے ہوتے ہوئے نانی محروم ہے کیونکہ پر نانی محجوب ہے دادی کی وجہ سے خواہ دادی خود وارث ہو یا نہ ہو۔ اسی طرح شریک فی الرقبہ کے ہوتے ہوئے دوسرے لوگ مجوب ہیں اور وہ ہر حال میں مجوب رہیں گے خواہ شریک اپنا حق لے یا نہ لے۔
تی مصنف نے جار کی تفسیر یہ فرمائی ورنہ اگر ان کا دروازہ اسی گلی میں ہے اور دونوں کے مکانوں کا اتصال ہے اب دو صورتیں ہیں وہ راستہ نافذ ہے یا غیر نافذ ، اگر غیر نافذ ہے تو پھر یہ شفعہ پائے گا۔ مگر جار ہونے کی حیثیت سے نہیں بلکہ شریک فی الطریق ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اگر نافذ ہے اور دونوں کا راستہ جدا گانہ ہے یعنی دونوں کے مکانوں کے درمیان طریق نافذ ہے تو پھر اس کیلئے شفعہ نہیں ہو گا ۔ اس لئے کہ طریق فارق نے ضرر کو دور کر دیا، کذافی الشامی ص ۴ آج ۵

ووجه الظاهر ان السبب قد تقرر فى الكل الا ان للشريك حق التقدم فاذا سلم كان لمن وليه بمنزلة دين الصحة مع دين المرض
ترجمہ اور ظاہر الروایہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ سبب ( اتصال ) ثابت ہو چکا ہر ایک کے حق میں مگر شریک کیلئے حق تقدم ہے پس جب اس نے دست برداری دے دی تو شفعہ اس کیلئے ہوگا جو اس سے قریب ہے جیسے دین صحبت دین مرض کے ساتھ۔ تشریح اگر کسی شخص پر کچھ لوگوں کا قرض صحت کی حالت کا ہے اور کچھ لوگوں کا مرض الوفات کے وقت کا ، تو اول قرض خواہ کو حق نقدم ہے یعنی میت کے ترکہ سے پہلے ان کا حق ادا کیا جائے پھر اگر بچ جائے تو دوسروں کا۔ لیکن اگر اول فریق اپنا حق معاف کر دے تو پھر اولاً ہی دوسرے فریق کا حق ادا کیا جائے گا۔ بعینہ اسی طرح شفعہ کے مسئلہ میں ہے کہ سبب شفعہ ہر ایک کیلئے ثابت ہے مگر شریک حق کو حق تقدم ہے جب وہ اپنا حق نہ لے۔ دوسروں کو شفعہ ملے گا۔ یہ ظاہر الروایہ کی دلیل ہے۔
شریک فی البیع جار پر مقدم ہے
والشريك فى المبيع قد يكون فى بعض منها كما فى منزل معين من الدار وجدار معين منها وهو مقدم
Book of Pre-emption. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya Volume 13. Part and after it: connection in rights because it is partnership in the usufructs of property, and preference is realized by the strength of the cause. And because the harm of division, if it is not suitable as a cause, it is suitable as a preferrer. Translation: And in any case, the order is due to the command of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that the partner is more entitled than the associate, and the associate is more entitled than the neighbor. So the partner is in the property itself, and the associate is in the rights of the property, and the neighbor is the adjacent owner. And because connection through ownership in the property is stronger because it is in every part, and after that connection in rights because it is connection in the usufructs of property, and preference occurs due to the strength of the cause. And because the harm of division, if it is not suitable as a cause, it is suitable as a preferrer. Commentary: Previously it was said that this speech benefits two things: proof and order. They mention the second thing here, and as proof they present the hadith that the partner is more entitled than the associate, and the associate is more entitled than the neighbor. Now we will explain what is meant by partner, associate, and neighbor. He said: The one who has a share in the property itself is called partner, the one who has partnership in the rights of the property is called associate, and the neighbor is called neighbor (shafi'). Then he presents a rational proof: The connection of the one who has partnership in the property is stronger than others, because this connection is within every part, and after that the connection of rights is stronger than the connection of the neighbor, because this connection is connection in the usufructs of property. And it is an accepted principle that preference is obtained by the strength of the cause, and the strength of the cause is in the first, then in the second. So the same order will apply in receiving pre-emption. 'And because the harm of division...' He says that Imam Shafi'i considered the harm of division as the cause of pre-emption, but that cause could not be established. However, the harm of division can be a preferrer, meaning in the case where the harm of division applies, that person is given priority over others, and that is the partner in the specific property. In the presence of the partner in the property itself, the partner in rights and the neighbor are deprived of pre-emption. He said: And there is no pre-emption for the partner in the path and the right of drinking and the neighbor along with the partner in the property, because we mentioned that he is preferred. Translation: And there is no pre-emption for the partner in the path and the right of drinking and the neighbor along with the partner in the property, due to the proof we mentioned that he is preferred. Commentary: What the author of Hidaya has stated, Imam Quduri expresses it similarly: In the presence of the partner in the property itself, the partner in rights and the neighbor will not get pre-emption, the proofs for which we have passed. In the case of the first's relinquishment, the second entitled person will get the right of pre-emption; the definition of neighbor. He said: If he relinquishes, then pre-emption is for the partner in the path; if he relinquishes, then the neighbor takes it, due to the order we explained. And by this neighbor is meant the contiguous neighbor, who is behind the pre-empted house and his door is in another alley. And from Abu Yusuf: In the presence of the partner in the property, there is no pre-emption for anyone else, whether he relinquishes or takes it, because they are excluded by him. Translation: So if he (the partner in the property) relinquishes, then pre-emption is for the partner in the path; if he also relinquishes, then the neighbor takes it, due to the order we explained. And by this neighbor is meant the contiguous neighbor, and he is the one who is behind the pre-empted house and his door is in another alley. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that in the presence of the partner in the property, there is no pre-emption for anyone else, whether he relinquishes or takes it, because they are excluded by him. Commentary: That is, the order among the pre-emptors is what we have explained. But if the partner in the property does not take pre-emption, then the partner in the path can take it, and if he does not take, then the neighbor can take it. Then the author explained the neighbor: he is the one who is behind the pre-empted house and his door is in another alley. Imam Abu Yusuf says: In the presence of the grandmother (paternal), the maternal grandmother is deprived, because the maternal grandmother is excluded by the paternal grandmother, whether the paternal grandmother herself inherits or not. Similarly, in the presence of the partner in the property, other people are excluded, and they will remain excluded in any case, whether the partner takes his right or not. Then the author gave this explanation of neighbor; otherwise, if their door is in the same alley and there is connection between the two houses, then there are two cases: the path is through (nāfidh) or not through (ghayr nāfidh). If it is not through, then he will get pre-emption, but not as a neighbor, rather as a partner in the path. And if it is through and the two paths are separate, i.e., there is a through path between the two houses, then there is no pre-emption for him, because the separating path removed the harm. Likewise in al-Shami, p. 4, vol. 5. The reason of the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah): 'And the reason of the apparent is that the cause (connection) is established for all, except that the partner has a right of priority. So when he relinquishes, it is for the one after him, like the health debt with the illness debt.' Translation: And the reason of the apparent narration is that the cause (connection) is established for everyone, but the partner has a right of priority. So when he relinquishes, pre-emption will be for the one next to him, like the health debt with the illness debt. Commentary: If a person has some debts from the time of health and some from the time of terminal illness, the first creditors have the right of priority, i.e., their right is paid from the deceased's estate first; then if something remains, the others are paid. But if the first party forgives their right, then the second party's right is paid first. Exactly the same is in the matter of pre-emption: the cause of pre-emption is established for everyone, but the partner has the right of priority. When he does not take his right, others will get pre-emption. This is the proof of Zahir al-Riwayah. The partner in the sale is preferred over the neighbor: 'And the partner in the sale may be in some part of it, as in a specific room of the house and a specific wall of it, and he is preferred.'
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage addresses the priority order among those entitled to pre-emption (shuf'ah). The text begins by stating that the order is based on a hadith: the partner (sharik) is more entitled than the associate (khalit), and the associate is more entitled than the neighbor (jar). Here, 'partner' means a co-owner in the property itself (sharik fi al-mabi'), 'associate' means a partner in rights such as a right of way or irrigation (sharik fi al-huquq), and 'neighbor' means an adjacent owner (jar mulasiq). The author then provides a rational proof: the connection (ittisal) of a co-owner in the property is stronger because it encompasses every part, whereas the connection of a partner in rights is limited to usufructs, and the neighbor's connection is even weaker. Therefore, the strongest cause yields priority. The text also addresses a disagreement with Imam Shafi'i, who considered the harm of division (darar al-qismah) as the cause of pre-emption. The Hanafi response is that it is not a valid cause but can serve as a preferrer. The passage then rules that in the presence of the co-owner (sharik fi al-raqabah), other entitled persons (partner in rights and neighbor) are deprived of pre-emption entirely, according to Imam Abu Yusuf. However, according to the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah), if the co-owner relinquishes his right, the right passes to the next in line: first the partner in the path (sharik fi al-tariq), then the neighbor. The neighbor is specifically defined as one whose house adjoins the rear of the pre-empted house and whose door opens onto a different alley. A distinction is made: if both houses open onto the same alley and there is a through path separating them, the neighbor does not have pre-emption because the path eliminates the harm. The author compares this to debts from health and illness, where illness debt is subordinate but comes into effect if the health debt is waived. Finally, the text notes that a partner in a specific part of the property (e.g., a room or wall) is also considered a co-owner and is preferred over a neighbor.

Key Terms
شریک (sharīk): A co-owner in the property itself (sharik fi al-raqabah), having a share in the substance of the property.
خلیط (khalīṭ): A partner in rights (sharik fi al-huquq), such as a right of way or irrigation, not in the property itself.
شفیع (shafīʿ): The neighbor (jar) who is contiguous (mulasiq) but not a co-owner or partner in rights.
ضرر القسمة (ḍarar al-qisma): The harm that results from dividing a jointly owned property, considered by Shafi'i as the cause of pre-emption.
ظاہر الروایۃ (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The principal and well-known transmission of Imam Muhammad's six books, carrying the weight of the school's primary position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (Zahir al-Riwayah), what happens if the co-owner (sharik fi al-raqabah) relinquishes his right of pre-emption?
A) The right is extinguished and no one else can claim pre-emption.
B) The right passes to the partner in rights (khalit), and if he also relinquishes, to the neighbor.
C) The right passes automatically to the neighbor.
D) The right passes to the partner in the path only, not to the neighbor.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi priority order of pre-emptors is based on the strength of connection: co-owner first, then partner in rights, then neighbor, with the subtlety that the neighbor's right depends on the path configuration.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Hierarchy of Pre-emption Claimants in Hanafi School
Ruling on hierarchy of pre-emption with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy of pre-emption claimants and explain the ruling when the sharik fi al-raqabah is present, including the difference with Abu Yusuf's view.

Core Idea
The partner in the property blocks all others from pre-emption, but if he waives, the right passes to the next in hierarchy.

Pre-emption (shuf'a) is a right that allows certain individuals to purchase sold property before others. The Hanafi school recognizes three categories of claimants, ranked by priority. This lesson examines the highest ranking — the partner in ownership (sharik fi al-raqabah) — and how his presence affects others, including a minority view by Imam Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the claim of pre-emption (shuf'a). The ruling establishes a hierarchy: the partner in the property (sharik fi al-raqabah) has the first right. Others have no right while he exists.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is direct: 'لا شفعة لغيره سلم او استوفى لأنهم محجوبون به' — no pre-emption for anyone else because they are blocked by him. The reason (sabab) is the stronger tie of co-ownership.
The term 'محجوب' is key, as in inheritance law.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'محجوبون' indicates a complete legal impediment. The sharik fi al-raqabah's presence creates a bar that prevents others from claiming, irrespective of his own action.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf argues that the blocking effect is absolute: others are always excluded, even if the sharik fi al-raqabah waives. He analogizes to inheritance where a paternal grandmother blocks a maternal grandmother regardless of inheritance.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Zahir al-Riwayah: if the sharik fi al-raqabah waives, the right passes to the sharik fi al-tariq, then to the neighbour. This is because the cause of shuf'a (adjacency or partnership) remains for them once the priority right is relinquished.
Al-Marghinani and later Hanafi works adopt this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والشريك فى الرقبة لاشفعة لغيره سلم او استوفى لأنهم محجوبون به
And the partner in the property (sharik fi al-raqabah) — there is no pre-emption for anyone else, whether he waives or takes, because they are excluded by him.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the hierarchy of pre-emption rights. The author states that when a partner in the ownership (sharik fi al-raqabah) exists, no one else—be it a partner in the right of way or a neighbour—has any right to pre-emption. This applies regardless of whether the sharik fi al-raqabah chooses to take the sold property or waives his right; the others remain excluded (mahjub). The proof given is that they are 'blocked' (محجوبون) by his presence. The commentator then explains the order: first sharik fi al-raqabah, then sharik fi al-tariq, then jar (neighbour). This is the relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah). However, the text also records a view from Imam Abu Yusuf that the exclusion of others holds in all circumstances, even if the sharik fi al-raqabah does not take his right. This is analogous to inheritance where the presence of a paternal grandmother (dadi) excludes a maternal grandmother (nani) from inheritance, regardless of whether the paternal grandmother inherits or not. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah for the main ruling, while Abu Yusuf's view is a minority position within the Hanafi school. The mufta bihi is the hierarchy allowing others to take if the sharik fi al-raqabah waives, as stated in the commentary.

Key Terms
شريك في الرقبة (sharīk fī al-raqabah): A partner who co-owns the property itself (the 'neck' of the property), not just a right-of-way or water channel.
محجوب (maḥjūb): Legally excluded from claiming pre-emption due to the presence of a prior right-holder.
شريك في الطريق (sharīk fī al-ṭarīq): A partner who shares a right-of-way (e.g., a driveway) with the seller but does not own the property itself.
جار (jār): An adjacent neighbour who shares a boundary with the sold property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi hierarchy of pre-emption, who has the highest right?
A) The neighbour (jar)
B) The partner in the property (sharik fi al-raqabah)
C) The partner in the right of way (sharik fi al-tariq)
D) All have equal rights

Key Takeaway
The partner in ownership (sharik fi al-raqabah) is the highest pre-emptor; if he waives, the right passes to the partner in the right-of-way, then to the neighbour, according to the mufta bihi Hanafi position.

Definition of a Neighbour for Pre-emption (Shuf'a)
Definition of neighbour for shuf'a with door condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the neighbour (jar) eligible for shuf'a according to the Hanafi school and state the condition regarding the location of his door.

Core Idea
An adjacent neighbour whose door is in a different alley qualifies for pre-emption.

In Hanafi law, the right of pre-emption (shuf'a) allows certain parties to replace a buyer in a sale. One such party is a neighbour (jar). However, not every neighbour is eligible. This passage clarifies that only an adjacent neighbour (jar mulasiq) whose door opens into a different alley than the sold property qualifies. If the door is in the same alley, the claim may instead be based on partnership in the way (sharik fi al-tariq).

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal context
Shuf'a is an option to pre-empt a sale. Neighbours are one category of pre-emptors. This step positions the definition within the broader framework.
2
Define the neighbour (jar)
The passage defines the neighbour as 'jar mulasiq' – one whose property is physically adjacent (touching) to the sold property. Not just any nearby neighbour qualifies.
Adjacency is key; a neighbour across a road or separated by a public path is not a jar.
3
Specify the door condition
The jar's door must open into a different alley (zuaq akhar) from the sold property. This distinguishes him from a partner in the way.
If the door is in the same alley, the person is not a jar but may be a sharik fi al-tariq.
4
Understand the exclusion
If the door is in the same alley, the neighbour cannot claim shuf'a as a jar. His claim would be based on partnership in the way, which has its own conditions (e.g., private vs. public path).
This avoids double-counting the same person under two categories.
5
Apply the ruling
When presented with a scenario, check two conditions: (1) physical adjacency, and (2) door in a different alley. Only then does the shuf'a right as a neighbour exist.
If both conditions are met, the jar has the right to pre-empt the sale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجار المراد جار ملاصق وهو الذي دار مشفوعه على ظهره وبابه في زقاق آخر
And the intended neighbour is an adjacent neighbour, and he is the one whose property is at the back of the sold house and his door is in another alley.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage provides the definition of a neighbour (jar) eligible for pre-emption. The commentator explains that the jar is not just any neighbour but specifically one whose property is adjacent (mulasiq) to the sold property, with his door opening into a different alley (zuaq akhar). The implication is that if the door is in the same alley, then he is not considered a jar but could be a sharik fi al-tariq (partner in the way) and claim pre-emption on that basis. The passage then discusses two scenarios: if the path is private (non-nāfidh) and both have doors in the same alley, then the person is a sharik fi al-tariq and may take pre-emption; if the path is public (nāfidh) and separates the properties, then no pre-emption is granted. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
جار ملاصق (jār mulāṣiq): A neighbour whose property is physically adjacent (touching) to the sold property, not just nearby.
زقاق (zuqāq): A narrow street or alley; a path leading to properties.
شريك في الطريق (sharīk fī al-ṭarīq): Partner in the way; a person who shares access to a private path with the seller.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition must be met for a neighbour (jar) to have a right of pre-emption (shuf'a)?
A) The neighbour must be a blood relative of the seller.
B) The neighbour's door must open into a different alley than the sold property.
C) The neighbour must own multiple properties.
D) The neighbour must live in the sold property.

Key Takeaway
A neighbour eligible for pre-emption is one whose property is physically adjacent and whose door is in a different alley from the sold property.

Hierarchy of Pre-emption: The Analogy with Debts of Health and Illness
Analogical reasoning for shuf'a priority transfer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Zahir al-Riwayah position on the transferability of the shuf'a right upon waiver using the analogy of debts and evaluate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Waiver of a priority right transfers it to the next claimant, like a health debt waiver allows illness debt payment.

The rule of pre-emption (shuf'a) gives priority to certain claimants. When the primary claimant (sharik fi al-raqabah) waives his right, does the right vanish or pass on? The Zahir al-Riwayah text uses a striking analogy from debt payments to answer this. In this lesson, we unpack that analogy and see why the Hanafi school holds that the right is transferable, not lost.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Claim of Zahir al-Riwayah
The text states that the cause (sabab) for shuf'a is established for all potential claimants, but the partner (sharik) has a right of priority (haqq al-taqaddum). When he waives, the right goes to the next in line.
This is the operative ruling.
2
Understand the Analogy with Debts
Debts incurred during health (dīn al-ṣiḥḥa) take priority over debts from terminal illness (dīn al-maraḍ). If the health debt creditor waives, the illness debt is paid next. Similarly, the sharik's priority does not extinguish others' rights.
The analogy reveals the principle of transferability.
3
Apply the Analogy to Shuf'a Hierarchy
All adjacent owners/partners have a cause for shuf'a. The sharik's right is only a priority. Upon waiver, the right descends to the next eligible person (e.g., neighbor).
This is the mufta bihi position.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf held that waiver extinguishes the right entirely. The Zahir al-Riwayah position is relied upon for fatwa.
Knowing the dispute sharpens your understanding of school methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووجه الظاهر ان السبب قد تقرر فى الكل الا ان للشريك حق التقدم فاذا سلم كان لمن وليه بمنزلة دين الصحة مع دين المرض
And the reason of the apparent (Zahir al-Riwayah) is that the cause has been established for all, but the partner has a right of priority. When he waives, it goes to the one next to him, like the debt of health with the debt of illness.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage provides the reasoning behind the Zahir al-Riwayah position. The commentator explains that the cause (sabab) for pre-emption—i.e., adjacency or partnership—is established for all potential claimants. However, the partner in the property (sharik fi al-raqabah) has a 'right of prior claim' (haqq al-taqaddum) by virtue of his stronger connection. This does not negate the rights of others entirely; it only postpones them. If the sharik fi al-raqabah waives his right (sallama), then the right moves to the next in line. This is analogous to the situation where a property owner has two types of debts: one incurred during health (dīn al-ṣiḥḥa) and another during a terminal illness (dīn al-maraḍ). The debt from health takes priority in payment from the estate because it is incurred with full legal capacity. However, if the creditor of the health debt waives his claim, then the debt from illness is paid first in order of time. Just as the waiver of the prior creditor allows the subsequent one to step forward, the waiver of the sharik fi al-raqabah allows the next eligible person to claim pre-emption. This is the relied-upon position of the school, as stated in Zahir al-Riwayah. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
دين الصحة (dīn al-ṣiḥḥa): Debt incurred while the debtor was in full health, which takes priority over debts incurred during terminal illness.
حق التقدم (ḥaqq al-taqaddum): The right of prior claim or priority given to the sharik fi al-raqabah due to his stronger connection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah reasoning, what happens when the sharik fi al-raqabah waives his pre-emption right?
A) The right is lost permanently
B) The right passes to the next claimant in order
C) The next claimant must pay a higher price
D) The seller can cancel the sale

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the prior right of the sharik fi al-raqabah is transferable upon waiver, ensuring that the right of pre-emption is not entirely lost.

Partner in Part of Property Gets Pre-emption Over Neighbour
Rule that a partner in part is preferred over the neighbour for shuf'a in all parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a partner in any part of a property is preferred over a neighbour for shuf'a, and explain the reasoning based on the unity of the property and strength of connection.

Core Idea
A share in any part makes you a partner in the whole for pre-emption.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario in Hanafi shuf'a law: when a person owns only a part of a property—like a room or even a wall—does that person have priority over a neighbour when another part of the same property is sold? The answer, based on the stronger narration from Imam Abu Yusuf, is yes, because the entire property is one contiguous unit and the partner's connection is stronger than that of a neighbour.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that the text deals with a partner who owns only a specific part of the property (e.g., a designated room or a wall), not the whole.
The terms used: manzil (room/compartment) and jidar (wall).
2
State the ruling
The partner in part is preferred over the neighbour for pre-emption in that part and also in any other part of the same property.
This is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi).
3
Understand the reasoning
Two reasons: (1) The partner's connection (ittisal) is stronger than the neighbour's. (2) The entire property is considered one contiguous piece of land (buq'ah wahidah), so a share in any part constitutes partnership in the whole.
The principle of buq'ah wahidah is key.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf has two narrations; the text follows the more correct one (asah) that gives priority to the partner in part.
The other narration may have given equal or no priority.
5
Apply the principle
Even if the sold part is a different room or part where the partner has no share, the partner still has priority over a neighbour.
The unity of the property overrides the specific location of the share.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والشريك فى المبيع قد يكون فى بعض منها كما فى منزل معين من الدار وجدار معين منها وهو مقدم على الجار في المنزل وكذا على الجار في بقية الدار في اصح الروايتين عن أبي يوسف لان اتصاله أقوى والبقة واحدة
And the partner in the sold property may be in some part of it, like a specific room of the house and a specific wall of it, and he is preferred over the neighbour in that room, and likewise over the neighbour in the rest of the house, in the more correct of the two narrations from Abu Yusuf, because his connection is stronger, and the piece of land is one.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where a person is a partner not in the entire property but only in a specific part, such as a designated room (manzil) or a wall (jidar) within the property. The ruling is that such a person is still considered a 'partner in the sold property' (sharik fi al-mabi') and is given priority over a neighbour in claiming pre-emption. This applies even if the sold part is a different room or part where he has no share. The commentator explains that the reason is his connection (ittisal) is stronger than that of a neighbour. Moreover, the entire property (dar) is considered one contiguous piece of land (buq'ah wahidah), so a share in any part of it makes one a partner in the whole for the purpose of shuf'a. The text notes that this is the more correct narration from Imam Abu Yusuf (as opposed to another narration where he may have differed). The authority weight is from the narrations of Abu Yusuf, but the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) within the Hanafi school is that a partner in any part is preferred over a neighbour. The commentary clarifies that the term 'manzil' refers to a separate house within a larger compound (haweli), and 'bayt' to a single room. Even if the share is only in one wall, the person is considered a partner in the whole compound and thus has priority over a neighbour.

Key Terms
بقة (buq'ah): A piece of land or estate; here it means the entire property as one unit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If Ali owns only one wall in a large courtyard house, and another part of the house (a different room) is sold to a third party, can Ali claim pre-emption over a neighbour?
A) No, because he only owns a wall.
B) Yes, because the entire house is one contiguous property.
C) Only if the wall is sold as well.
D) Only if the neighbour is a non-Muslim.

Key Takeaway
A partner in any part of a property enjoys pre-emption priority over a neighbour in all parts of that property, due to the unity of the property and the strength of his connection.
