Private Way and Private Water Channel as Conditions for Pre-emption
Defines private way and private water channel for shuf'a.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'private way' and 'private water channel' according to the Hanafi school and identify the difference between the views of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding the latter.

Core Idea
Only private (non-public) ways and water channels grant the right of pre-emption; public ways and navigable rivers do not.

Pre-emption (shuf'a) can be established through partnership in a contiguous property, in a share of the property, or in a common right like a way or water channel. However, not every shared way or water source qualifies. This passage clarifies the crucial condition: the way or water channel must be private (khāṣṣ), not public. It then provides the school's definition of 'private' for each, including a notable difference between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on one side and Abu Yusuf on the other.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for shuf'a through partnership in way or water
The passage states that for pre-emption to be rightful via partnership in a way (ṭarīq) or water channel (sharb), that way or water must be private. Identify this as the core condition.
2
Define private way
A private way is one that is not a thoroughfare (nāfidh). That means it is a dead-end or cul-de-sac that does not lead to a public road. If it is a through-way, it is public and no shuf'a right exists.
The term nāfidh literally means 'penetrating'—a way that allows passage to a public road.
3
Define private water channel according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
They define a private water channel as a river in which boats cannot sail. If boats can navigate, it is public.
This definition emphasizes navigability as the criterion for public/private.
4
Contrast with Abu Yusuf's definition
Abu Yusuf defines a private water channel as a river that irrigates only two or three gardens (qirāḥ). If it irrigates more than that, it is public.
The difference lies in the measure: navigability vs. number of gardens irrigated.
5
Understand the practical consequence
The ikhtilaf (disagreement) between the imams affects which water sources give shuf'a rights. Under Abu Hanifa/Muhammad, a non-navigable river used by many still gives shuf'a? Actually, if boats cannot sail, it is private regardless of number of users? The text says non-navigable is private, navigable is public. Under Abu Yusuf, if many gardens are irrigated, it is public even if non-navigable. So the practical effect is that Abu Yusuf's definition is more restrictive.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم لابد ان يكون الطريق او الشرب خاصاحتى يستحق الشفعة بالشركة فيه فالطريق الخاص ان لا يكون نافذا والشرب الخاص ان يكون نهرا لاتجرى فيه السفن وما تجرى فيه فهو عام وهذا عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد وعن أبي يوسف ان الخاص ان يكون نهرا يسقى منه قراحان او ثلثة وما زاد على ذلك فهو عام
Then it is necessary that the way or the water channel be private for the pre-emption to be rightful by partnership in it. So the private way is that it not be a thoroughfare (nāfidh). And the private water channel is that it be a river in which boats do not sail, and what boats sail in is public. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And from Abu Yusuf: that the private [water channel] is a river from which two or three gardens are irrigated, and what exceeds that is public.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage addresses the conditions for establishing a right to pre-emption through partnership in a common way (tariq) or water channel (sharb). The author states that such way or water must be 'private' (khaṣṣ), not public. A private way is defined as one that is not nāfidh, meaning it is a dead-end or cul-de-sac that does not lead to a public thoroughfare. A private water channel is defined according to two positions within the Hanafi school. The position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad is that a private water channel is a river in which boats cannot sail; if boats can navigate, it is public. Imam Abu Yusuf defines a private water channel as one that irrigates only two or three gardens (qirāḥ, plural of qarīḥ, meaning a garden plot). If it irrigates more than that, it is considered public. The commentator clarifies that this distinction matters because pre-emption based on partnership in a public road (like a highway) or a large river (like the Ganges) is not granted, as they are public utilities and not subject to private claims. The authority weight is from the founding imams and their transmissions; the ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah for the definitions given by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, while Abu Yusuf's view is a separate narration (nawadir). The mufta bihi is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as it is the majority view, though the commentary suggests that Abu Yusuf's view is also considered. The text does not explicitly state a tarjih.

Key Terms
طريق نافذ (ṭarīq nāfidh): A thoroughfare or through-way that leads to a public road; such a way is public and does not give shuf'a rights.
شرب خاص (sharb khāṣṣ): A private water channel, defined either as a non-navigable river or one irrigating only a few gardens.
قراح (qirāḥ): Plural of qarīh, a garden plot or agricultural land irrigated from the water channel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, what condition makes a water channel private for pre-emption?
A) It irrigates only two gardens.
B) Boats cannot sail in it.
C) It is dug by the owners.
D) It has no outlet.

Key Takeaway
A way or water channel must be private (not a thoroughfare or navigable) for partnership in it to give the right of pre-emption.

Distribution of Pre-emption Among Multiple Shuf'aa
Explaining why pre-emption is divided equally among co-shareholders

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the distribution of pre-emption among multiple pre-emptors, explain the reasoning based on the cause of connection (ittisal), and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Pre-emption is divided equally because the cause (connection) is the same for all—strength, not quantity, determines entitlement.

This passage from the Hanafi tradition addresses a key dispute: how should pre-emption be distributed when multiple co-sharers are entitled? Some might assume it follows ownership shares, but the Hanafi school rules equally. We will explore the reasoning based on the nature of the cause (sabab) and the refutation of the Shafi'i view that pre-emption is an accessory to ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause (sabab) of pre-emption
The text states that pre-emption arises from the connection (ittisal) to the property, not from ownership itself. This cause is shared by all co-sharers equally.
Connection is the sole cause in Hanafi law.
2
Trace the Hanafi argument for equal distribution
If only one pre-emptor remains, he gets the entire right – this proves the cause is perfect in each individual. Therefore, when multiple exist, their entitlement is equal because the cause is identical in all.
This is a key proof: the hypothetical of a single pre-emptor.
3
Address the objection: connection varies in quantity
The text distinguishes between abundance (kathrah) and strength (quwwah) of the cause. Preference is based on strength, not quantity. Since each pre-emptor's connection is equally strong (each could take the whole if alone), they remain equal.
Strength is evidenced by the fact that one pre-emptor's right does not disappear when another appears.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i view
Imam al-Shafi'i considered pre-emption an accessory (marafiq) to ownership, so distribution should follow ownership shares. The Hanafi response: if it were an accessory, every acquisition of another's property would involve one's own ownership (like a father owning his son's slave – but that is not from his ownership).
The distinction: fruits are produced by property, pre-emption is not.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Hanafi, equal division; under Shafi'i, proportional division. This difference alters actual rulings in disputes between co-sharers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الشفعة

الاخراى علت کی صفت ہے اور " ہ " کا مرجع صاحب کثرت لیا جائے اور عنایہ میں یہ عبارت اس طرح ہے الاخرى بمقابلتها ، اب " ھا کا مرجع علت ہوگا۔ - شافعی نے شفعہ کو مرافق ملک شمار کیا تھا اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں۔ و تملک ملک غیر .... الخ جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ شفعہ کو مرافق ملک میں شمار نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ ورنہ ہر تملک کے اندر اپنی ملک کا دخل ہونا چاہئے ۔ جیسے باپ اپنے بیٹے کی باندی کا مالک ہو سکتا ہے مگر یہ ملک اس کی ملک کا ثمرہ نہیں ہے۔ لہذا شفعہ کو مرافق ملک نہیں کہا جا سکتا۔ البتہ پھل وغیرہ میں پیداوار ملک کا ثمرہ ملک ہوگا اور اسی وجہ سے بقدر ملک تقسیم ہوگا۔ ( کما مر )
The statement does not hold that if one of them is alone, he would be entitled to the full pre-emption, and this is a sign of the perfection of the cause. And the abundance of connection informs about the abundance of the cause, and preference occurs due to the strength of the proof, not its abundance, and here there is no strength because the other appears in comparison to him, and owning the property of someone else will not be counted. He takes it as one of the fruits of his ownership, unlike fruit and its like. Explanation: In our view, pre-emption among all pre-emptors will be in proportion to their numbers. Because due to connection, all have pre-emption, and in the essence of connection all share, so it is known that they are equal in the cause, therefore entitlement should also be equal. It can be understood in a simple way: if only one of them remains and the other partners do not take pre-emption, then the entire pre-emption goes to him. So this ruling is evidence that the cause is perfect, otherwise without perfection of cause he would not get the entire pre-emption. Question: Connection varies in less and more, so how can it be correct to call it equal? Answer: It is accepted that connection has less and more; in other words, there is abundance in the property, but preference is not given due to abundance of the cause, rather it is based on strength of the cause, and here the one with more cannot be described as strong. Because if there were strength in him, the other would not appear before him, just as when a partner exists, others do not get a share. And here the one with more appears before the one with less, so it is known that this is only abundance of the cause, not strength, otherwise the other would not appear. 'Al-ukhra bi-muqabilatihi...' – Al-ukhra is a description of the cause, and 'ha' refers to the one with abundance, and in 'Inayah the phrase is 'al-ukhra bi-muqabilatiha', now 'ha' refers to the cause. – Al-Shafi'i considered pre-emption as an accessory to ownership; this is being answered. 'Wa tamalluka mulki ghayr...' meaning that pre-emption will not be counted among the accessories of ownership. Otherwise, every acquisition should involve one's own ownership. For example, a father can own his son's slave girl, but this ownership is not a fruit of his ownership. Therefore pre-emption cannot be called an accessory of ownership. However, fruit etc., the produce is a fruit of ownership, and therefore it is distributed according to ownership. (As before)
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage addresses the Hanafi position on the distribution of pre-emption (shuf'ah) among multiple pre-emptors. The author first establishes that if only one pre-emptor exists, he gets the entire right – this proves the cause (sabab) is perfect in him. However, when multiple exist, the right is divided equally, not according to shares of ownership. The reason is that the cause is the 'connection' (ittisal) to the property, and all co-sharers share this connection equally. Even if one has a larger share, his connection is not stronger – the cause is the same. The author refutes a potential objection: if connection varies, why treat equally? He explains that preference is based on strength of the cause, not its quantity. Since each person's connection is equally strong (each could take the whole if alone), they are equal. The passage also refutes the Shafi'i view that pre-emption is an accessory to ownership; the Hanafi position is that pre-emption is a separate right established by the cause of connection, not an accessory that follows ownership like fruits.

Key Terms
اتصال (ittisāl): The connection of a co-sharer to the property, which is the cause (sabab) for pre-emption right.
شفعہ (shuf‘ah): The right of a co-sharer to pre-empt the sale of a share to an outsider by paying the price.
مرافق ملک (marāfiq al-milk): Accessories or appurtenances of ownership; rights that follow ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, when multiple co-sharers are entitled to pre-emption, how is the right distributed?
A) According to their ownership shares in the property
B) Equally among all pre-emptors
C) Only to the one with the largest share
D) According to the order of their request

Key Takeaway
Pre-emption is divided equally among co-sharers because the cause (connection) is the same for all, and strength (not quantity) determines preference.

Division of Pre-emption After One Drops His Right
Ruling when one pre-emptor drops his right

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when one pre-emptor drops his right and explain the rationale based on muzāḥamah.

Core Idea
When one pre-emptor drops his right, the remaining divide the property equally—competition ends, but each cause remains perfect.

In Hanafi law, when multiple people hold a right of pre-emption (shuf'a), each has a perfect legal cause (sabab) for the entire property. The reason each initially takes only a share is the competition (muzāḥamah) of others. This lesson examines the effect when one pre-emptor voluntarily drops his right—a scenario that clarifies the nature of shuf'a as a right attached to the person, not the share.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states that if some pre-emptors drop their right, the remaining pre-emptors take the entire property according to their number (i.e., equally).
2
Understand the rationale: cause vs. competition
The reduction in each pre-emptor's share was solely due to competition (muzāḥamah), not a deficiency in their cause. Since the cause is perfect for each, once the competition is removed, the remaining acquire the full right equally.
The cause (sabab) of pre-emption is the same for all co-pre-emptors; competition only affects distribution.
3
Apply the rule to a hypothetical
Suppose three pre-emptors (A, B, C) and A drops his right. The ruling says B and C now have the right to pre-empt the entire property equally (50% each), regardless of their original shares in the property.
This illustrates that shuf'a is not tied to ownership shares but to the status of being a pre-emptor.
4
Distinguish from other distributions
Some might think the dropped share returns to others proportionally to their ownership, but the Hanafi position is equal division by number of remaining claimants.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اسقط بعضهم حقه فهى للباقين فى الكل على عددهم لان الانتقاص للمزاحمة مع كمال السبب في حق كل منهم وقد انقطعت ترجمہ اور اگر ساقط کر دیا ان میں سے بعض نے اپنے حق کو تو شفعہ باقی لوگوں کیلئے ہو گا تمام مبیع میں ان کے عدد کے مطابق اسلئے کہ حصہ گھٹنا مزاحمت کی وجہ سے تھا ان میں سے ہر ایک کے حق میں کمال سبب کے باوجود اور مزاحمت منقطع ہو چکی ہے۔ تشریح یعنی اگر شفعاء میں سے کسی نے اپنا حق ساقط کر دیا تو اب شفعہ باقی شفعاء کیلئے ہوگا۔ ان کے عدد روس کے مطابق ۔ اسلئے کہ کمال سبب ہر ایک کو حاصل ہے۔ پھر مستحقین کی کثرت کی وجہ سے بر بنائے مزاحمت ہر ایک کے حصہ میں کمی واقع ہو رہی تھی لیکن اب مزاحمت نہیں رہی اسلئے باقی حضرات شفعہ کے مستحق ہوں گے۔
And if some of them drop their right, then the pre-emption is for the remaining ones in the entire property according to their number, because the reduction was due to competition despite the perfection of the cause in each of them, and now the competition has ceased. Translation: And if some of them drop their right, then the pre-emption will be for the remaining people for the entire property according to their number, because the reduction of the share was due to competition in the presence of the perfection of the cause in each of them, and the competition has ceased. Explanation: That is, if one of the pre-emptors drops his right, then the pre-emption will be for the remaining pre-emptors according to their numbers. Because the perfection of the cause exists for each. Then due to the multiplicity of claimants, based on competition, each's share was reduced, but now competition is gone, so the remaining people are entitled to the pre-emption.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This is a direct ruling from the matn (likely al-Hidayah). The rule: if multiple pre-emptors exist and one drops his right, the remaining pre-emptors take the entire property divided equally among them. The reason is that the original reduction in each's share was only due to the competition (muzāḥamah) of others, not because of any deficiency in their own cause. Since each has a perfect right (kāmil sabab), when the competition is removed, the remaining ones revert to the default division equal on the basis of number. This is consistent with the earlier principle that the cause is equal for all.

Key Terms
مزاحمت (muzāḥamah): Competition among multiple claimants that reduces each share proportionally.
سبب (sabab): Legal cause; here the reason for entitlement to pre-emption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If there are three pre-emptors and one drops his right, how is the pre-emption divided among the remaining two?
A) Equally between them
B) According to their ownership shares
C) Only to the one who was present first
D) The one who dropped decides the division

Key Takeaway
When a pre-emptor drops his right, the remaining pre-emptors take the entire right equally—by their number, not by ownership—because competition is removed while the cause remains perfect.

Absent Pre-emptors: Distribution Among Present Ones
Ruling on pre-emption when some claimants are absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on distribution of pre-emption rights when some claimants are absent, and apply the rule to scenarios involving subsequent appearances.

Core Idea
A judicial decision cuts off the absent pre-emptor's right only partially, ensuring equality among all claimants.

Pre-emption (shuf'a) is a right of a co-owner to acquire a sold share. When multiple pre-emptors exist but some are absent, the Hanafi school provides detailed rules to balance interests. This lesson unpacks the key scenario from al-Hidayah: the judge initially ignores absent claimants, but if they appear later, their rights revive partially. Understanding this teaches us about the effect of judicial decisions on vested rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
There are multiple pre-emptors, some absent. What does the judge do initially? He considers only the present ones.
2
Understand the initial ruling
The judge divides the entire pre-emption right equally among the present pre-emptors, ignoring the absent.
Reason: the absent might not demand.
3
Trace the subsequent appearance
If an absent appears after judgment, what share does he get? The text gives scenarios: if only one present got the whole, the absent gets half; if two had received, the absent gets one-third, etc.
4
Distinguish based on taking
Note the difference if the present who received judgment surrendered his right. The absent still gets only half, not the whole, because the judgment itself altered rights.
5
Contrast with pre-judgment scenario
If the absent appears before any judgment, he gets the full share (the whole) because no judicial decision has cut off his right.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو كان البعض غيبا يقضى بها بين الحضور على عددهم لان الغائب لعله لا يطلب وان قضى الحاضر بالجميع ثم حضر اخر يقضى له بالنصف ولو حضر ثالث فبثلث مافى يدكل واحد تحقيقا للتسوية فلو سلم الحاضر بعد ما قضى له بالجميع لا ياخذ القادم الا النصف لان قضأ القاضى بالكل للحاضر قطع حق الغائب عن النصف بخلاف ما قبل القضاء ترجمہ اور بعض غائب ہوں تو حاضرین کے درمیان ان کے عدد کے مطابق شفعہ کا فیصلہ کر دیا جائے گا۔ اسلئے کہ غائب شاید طلب نہ کرے اور اگر تمام کا فیصلہ ایک کیلئے کر دیا گیا اور پھر دوسرا حاضر ہو گیا تو اس کیلئے نصف کا فیصلہ کر دیا جائے گا اور اگر تیسرا حاضر ہو گیا تو ہر ایک کے قبضہ میں جو کچھ ہے اس کے تہائی کا فیصلہ کر دیا جائے گا۔ برابری کو ثابت کرنے کیلئے۔ پس اگر حاضر نے اس کے حق میں جمیع کا فیصلہ کئے جانے کے بعد دست برداری دے دی تو آنے والا نہیں لے گا مگر نصف کو اسلئے کہ قاضی کے فیصلہ نے حاضر کیلئے مکمل کے سلسلہ میں منقطع کر دیا اس نے نصف کے حق میں غائب کے حق کو بخلاف اس صورت کے جو قضاء قاضی سے پہلے ہو ۔ تشریح چند شفیع ہیں مگر ان میں سے کوئی غائب ہے اور کچھ موجود ہیں تو موجودین کے حق میں قاضی ان کی طلب پر شفعہ کا فیصلہ کر دے گا اور غائب کا کوئی لحاظ نہیں کرے گا ۔ بلکہ موجود ین کے درمیان ان کے عدد روس کے مطابق اس کو تقسیم کر دیا جائے گا۔ غائب کے عدم لحاظ کیوجہ یہ ہے کہ شاید وہ شفعہ کا مطالبہ نہ کرے۔ قاضی اولاً تو غائب کا لحاظ نہیں کرے گا لیکن اگر فیصلہ کے بعد وہ آکر شفعہ کا مطالبہ کرے حالانکہ ایک موجود شفیع کیلئے قاضی نے پورے شفعہ کا فیصلہ کر دیا تھا تو اب قاضی آنے والے کیلئے نصف کا فیصلہ کر دے گا اور اگر تیسرا اور بھی آگیا اور اس نے بھی شفعہ طلب کیا تو دونوں کے قبضہ میں جو ہے ان میں سے ایک ایک ثلث قاضی دلوائے گا کیونکہ اس صورت میں تینوں کے درمیان مساوات ہو جائے گی۔ شفیع حاضر نے شفعہ کا دعوی کیا اور قاضی نے پورے شفعہ کا اس کے حق میں فیصلہ کر دیا لیکن پھر حاضر نے لیا نہیں اب شفیع غائب آتا ہے اور شفعہ طلب کرتا ہے تو اس کو پورا تو نہیں ملے گا بلکہ اس کا نصف ملے گا۔ اسلئے کہ ملے گا بہر حال قضاء قاضی سے پہلے نصف ساقط نہیں ہوگا۔
And if some are absent, the judge decides among the present ones according to their number, because the absent one might not demand. And if he judged for the present one with the whole, then another came, he judges for him with half, and if a third came, then with one-third of what is in each one's hand, to achieve equality. So if the present one surrendered after judgment for him with the whole, the newcomer does not take except half, because the judgment of the judge for the present with the whole cut off the absent one's right from half, contrary to before the judgment. Translation: And if some are absent, then among the present ones, judgment will be given on their number, because the absent one might not demand. And if judgment was given for the whole to one, and then another became present, then for him judgment will be given for half, and if a third becomes present, then for one-third of what is in each one's hand, to establish equality. So if the present one, after judgment for him for the whole, handed over, the newcomer will not take except half, because the judge's judgment for the present for the whole cut off the absent one's right from half, unlike the case before the judgment. Explanation: There are several pre-emptors, but some are absent and some are present. The judge will give judgment for the present ones upon their demand and will not consider the absent one. Rather, among the present ones, it will be divided according to their number. The reason for not considering the absent one is that he might not demand the pre-emption. Initially, the judge does not consider the absent one, but if after judgment he comes and demands pre-emption, even though the judge had given judgment for the whole to one present pre-emptor, then the judge will give judgment for half for the newcomer. And if a third also comes and demands pre-emption, the judge will make each of them give one-third of what is in their hands, because in that case equality among the three will be achieved. The present shafi' claimed pre-emption and the judge gave judgment for the whole, but then the present one did not take. Now the absent shafi' comes and demands pre-emption, then he will not get the whole but only half. Because when the judge gave judgment for the whole to the present, but then he did not take, the judge's judgment cut off the newcomer's right from half. And if the judge has not yet given judgment and the absent one comes, then he will get the whole pre-emption. In any case, before the judge's judgment, half is not cut off.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage provides rules for when some pre-emptors are absent. The judge first considers only present pre-emptors, dividing the right equally among them. The absent is ignored because he might not claim. However, if an absent later appears after a judgment, he gets half if there was only one present who received the whole. If another appears later, each present must give a third to achieve equality among all. Importantly, if the present pre-emptor surrenders his right after judgment, the newcomer only gets half, because the judgment itself has fixed the rights: the present got the whole, but the judgment also implicitly cut off half from the absent (since the absent's right to half was not extinguished entirely). Before judgment, the absent would take the whole if he appeared. This shows the effect of qada' (judicial decision) in establishing rights.

Key Terms
شفیع (shafi'): Pre-emptor: a co-owner who has the right of shuf'a.
شفعۃ (shuf'a): Pre-emption: the right of a co-owner to buy a sold share from the buyer.
قضاء (qada'): Judicial decision or verdict.
غائب (gha'ib): Absent: a pre-emptor not present at the time of judgment.
حاضر (hadir): Present: a pre-emptor who is present and claims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If there are two pre-emptors (one present, one absent) and the judge gives the whole to the present, then the absent appears after the present has taken, what does the absent get?
A) The whole property
B) Nothing, because he was absent
C) Half of the property
D) One-third of the property

Key Takeaway
A judicial decision in pre-emption cases only partially cuts off the absent claimant's right, allowing later revival to maintain equality.

When is Pre-emption Established? Cause vs. Manifestation
Clarification of shuf'ah's cause and timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the cause (sabab) of pre-emption and its manifesting event, and state the Hanafi ruling on when the right arises.

Core Idea
Pre-emption right arises from connection, not from sale; the sale only reveals it.

In this passage, al-Hidayah clarifies a subtle legal point: the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) becomes established upon the sale contract, but its underlying cause is the pre-existing connection (ittisal) to the property. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion about timing and proof. We will unpack the text and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The matn states: 'Pre-emption is established by the contract of sale.' This is the explicit ruling – the right arises at the moment of sale.
2
Note the clarification
The author immediately adds 'not that it is the cause.' The sale is not the sabab; it only manifests the pre-existing right.
This distinguishes between the legal cause and the event that triggers its enforcement.
3
Understand the real cause
The true cause is the connection (ittisal) between the pre-emptor and the property – typically co-ownership or a right of easement. The sale merely makes this known.
Hanafi usul holds that the cause is foundational; the sale is a condition (shart) for claiming.
4
Apply the evidence
The text proves this by saying that if the seller admits the sale but the buyer denies it, the pre-emptor can still take the property. This shows the right depends on the seller's willingness to separate, not on the buyer's contract.
The seller's admission is sufficient to establish the fact of sale for the pre-emptor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال والشفعة تجب بعقد البيع ومعناه بعده لا انه هو السبب لأن سببها الاتصال على ما بيناه والوجه فيه ان الشفعة انما تجب اذا رغب البائع عن ملك الدار والبيع يعرفها ولهذا يكتفى يثبوت البيع في حقه حتى ياخذها الشفيع اذا اقر البائع بالبيع وان كان المشترى يكذبه
He said: Pre-emption is established by the contract of sale, and its meaning is after it, not that it is the cause, because its cause is the connection as we have explained, and the face of it is that pre-emption is established only when the seller desires to separate from ownership of the house, and the sale makes it known, and for this reason it is sufficient to establish the sale in his right so that the pre-emptor takes it if the seller admits the sale even if the buyer denies it.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This clarifies the basis of pre-emption (shuf'ah). The matn states that shuf'ah is established (tajibu) with the contract of sale but its meaning (i.e., the actual right to enforce) comes after the sale, not that the sale itself is the cause. The cause is the pre-existing connection (ittisal) to the property. The sale merely reveals or identifies the right. Evidence: even if the buyer denies the sale but the seller admits it, the pre-emptor can still take the property. This shows the right is not dependent on the buyer's acknowledgment but on the fact of the sale as known to the seller.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The cause of pre-emption, which is the connection (ittisal) to the property, not the sale.
اتصال (ittisal): The pre-existing connection (e.g., co-ownership or easement) that gives rise to the right of pre-emption.
شفعة (shuf'ah): Pre-emption right: the right of a co-owner to take a sold share at the sale price, voiding the buyer's ownership.

Ruling on Pre-emption When Some Pre-emptors Are Absent
Ruling on distribution of shuf'ah among present and absent pre-emptors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on distributing shuf'ah among present and absent pre-emptors after the qadi's judgment.

Core Idea
The qadi's judgment for present pre-emptors severs absent pre-emptors' right to half.

This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling on pre-emption (shuf'ah) when some co-owners are absent at the time of adjudication. According to the Hanafi school, the qadi passes judgment only among the present pre-emptors, and later-arriving absentees receive only a proportionate share. The binding effect of the qadi's decree (qada') plays a central role in cutting off the absent parties' rights to the extent adjudicated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and parties
Determine that there are multiple pre-emptors (shuf'a) for a sold property, some present and some absent. The qadi is asked to decide on the pre-emption claim.
2
Understand the initial ruling for present pre-emptors
The qadi ignores the absent pre-emptors and adjudicates the entire shuf'ah among the present ones, dividing it equally according to their number. Reason: the absent one may not demand his right.
This is based on the principle that the right is for those who claim it.
3
Trace the effect when an absent pre-emptor appears after judgment
If an absent pre-emptor appears after the qadi has already given the whole shuf'ah to a single present pre-emptor, the newcomer receives half of what was adjudicated. If a third appears, each holder gives one-third to achieve equality.
The share is determined by the number of pre-emptors, not by the actual shares in the property.
4
Distinguish the effect of qada' versus voluntary relinquishment
If the present pre-emptor voluntarily relinquishes his right after judgment, the newcomer still gets only half, not the whole. This is because the qadi's judgment has already cut off the absent's right to half.
Before any judgment, the absent pre-emptor could claim the whole, but after judgment, his right is reduced.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعض شفیع غائب ہوں اور تقسیم کے بعد آکر مطالبہ کریں تو کس طرح ان میں تقسیم کیا جائے گا
ولو كان البعض غيبا يقضى بها بين الحضور على عددهم لان الغائب لعله لا يطلب وان قضى الحاضر بالجميع ثم حضر اخر يقضى له بالنصف ولو حضر ثالث فبثلث مافى يدكل واحد تحقيقا للتسوية فلو سلم الحاضر بعد ما قضى له بالجميع لا ياخذ القادم الا النصف لان قضأ القاضى بالكل للحاضر قطع حق الغائب عن النصف بخلاف ما قبل القضاء
ترجمہ اور بعض غائب ہوں تو حاضرین کے درمیان ان کے عدد کے مطابق شفعہ کا فیصلہ کر دیا جائے گا۔ اسلئے کہ غائب شاید طلب نہ کرے اور اگر تمام کا فیصلہ ایک کیلئے کر دیا گیا اور پھر دوسرا حاضر ہو گیا تو اس کیلئے نصف کا فیصلہ کر دیا جائے گا اور اگر تیسرا حاضر ہو گیا تو ہر ایک کے قبضہ میں جو کچھ ہے اس کے تہائی کا فیصلہ کر دیا جائے گا۔ برابری کو ثابت کرنے کیلئے۔ پس اگر حاضر نے اس کے حق میں جمیع کا فیصلہ کئے جانے کے بعد دست برداری دے دی تو آنے والا نہیں لے گا مگر نصف کو اسلئے کہ قاضی کے فیصلہ نے حاضر کیلئے مکمل کے سلسلہ میں منقطع کر دیا اس نے نصف کے حق میں غائب کے حق کو بخلاف اس صورت کے جو قضاء قاضی سے پہلے ہو ۔ تشریح چند شفیع ہیں مگر ان میں سے کوئی غائب ہے اور کچھ موجود ہیں تو موجودین کے حق میں قاضی ان کی طلب پر شفعہ کا فیصلہ کر دے گا اور غائب کا کوئی لحاظ نہیں کرے گا ۔ بلکہ موجود ین کے درمیان ان کے عدد روس کے مطابق اس کو تقسیم کر دیا جائے گا۔ غائب کے عدم لحاظ کیوجہ یہ ہے کہ شاید وہ شفعہ کا مطالبہ نہ کرے۔
قاضی اولاً تو غائب کا لحاظ نہیں کرے گا لیکن اگر فیصلہ کے بعد وہ آکر شفعہ کا مطالبہ کرے حالانکہ ایک موجود شفیع کیلئے قاضی نے پورے شفعہ کا فیصلہ کر دیا تھا تو اب قاضی آنے والے کیلئے نصف کا فیصلہ کر دے گا اور اگر تیسرا اور بھی آگیا اور اس نے بھی شفعہ طلب کیا تو دونوں کے قبضہ میں جو ہے ان میں سے ایک ایک ثلث قاضی دلوائے گا کیونکہ اس صورت میں تینوں کے درمیان مساوات ہو جائے گی۔ شفیع حاضر نے شفعہ کا دعوی کیا اور قاضی نے پورے شفعہ کا اس کے حق میں فیصلہ کر دیا لیکن پھر حاضر نے لیا نہیں اب شفیع غائب آتا ہے اور شفعہ طلب کرتا ہے تو اس کو پورا تو نہیں ملے گا بلکہ اس کا نصف ملے گا۔ اسلئے کہ جب قاضی نے حاضر کیلئے سارے کا فیصلہ کر دیا تھا لیکن پھر اس نے لیا نہیں تھا تو قاضی کے فیصلہ نے آنے والے کا حق نصف سے ساقط کر دیا اور اگر ابھی تک قاضی نے فیصلہ نہیں کیا کہ غائب آ گیا تو پورا شفعہ اس کو ملے گا بہر حال قضاء قاضی سے پہلے نصف ساقط نہیں ہوگا۔
If some are absent, judgment is passed among those present according to their number, because the absent one perhaps will not demand. If judgment is passed in favor of one present for the whole, then another comes, judgment is passed for him for half. If a third comes, then for one-third of what each holds, to establish equality. If the present one relinquishes after judgment for the whole, the newcomer takes only half, because the qadi's judgment for the whole for the present one cut off the absent one's right to half, unlike before judgment.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter on pre-emption (shuf'ah). It addresses the scenario where there are multiple pre-emptors (shuf'a) but some are absent. The ruling states that the qadi should adjudicate the pre-emption only among those present, dividing it equally among them according to their number. The reason given is that the absent pre-emptor may not demand his right. If after adjudication for one present, another absent pre-emptor appears, the newcomer gets half of what was adjudicated. If a third appears, each of the two present gives one-third of what they hold, to achieve equality. If the present pre-emptor voluntarily relinquishes his right after adjudication, the newcomer still only gets half, not the whole. This is because the qadi's judgment for the whole for the present pre-emptor has severed the absent pre-emptor's right to half, as opposed to a situation before any judgment. The commentary then explains that the qadi first ignores the absent one, but if he later comes and demands, he gets a share proportionate to the number of pre-emptors. The key principle is that the qadi's judgment cuts off the right of the absent pre-emptor to the extent adjudicated.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'ah): Pre-emption: the right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a sold property by substituting the buyer.
قضاء (qada'): The judge's official judgment or decree.

B) Half of the shuf'ah
C) One-third of the shuf'ah
D) Nothing

Cause of Pre-emption: Ittisal over Sale
Clarifies that shuf'ah's cause is ittisal, not sale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why shuf'ah is established by ittisal (connection) rather than by the sale itself, according to Hanafi law, and apply the distinction between cause (sabab) and condition (shart).

Core Idea
Shuf'ah's cause is connection (ittisal), not the sale — sale only makes it enforceable.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a common confusion: is the sale of a property the cause that gives rise to pre-emption rights, or is it something else? The Hanafi school takes a precise position: the cause is the physical connection (ittisal) between the pre-emptor's property and the sold property. The sale is merely a condition that brings the right into effect. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying shuf'ah rules, especially when the sale is contested.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between sabab and shart
Identify the author's claim: shuf'ah is established by the contract of sale (bi 'aqd al-bay'), but the meaning is 'after the sale', not that the sale is the cause. Recognize that 'bi' here indicates accompaniment, not causation. The cause (sabab) is ittisal; the sale is a condition (shart) that activates the right.
In Hanafi usul, a cause generates a ruling; a condition is a prerequisite for the ruling to be actualized.
2
Understand the role of i'rad (withdrawal)
The text says shuf'ah is established when the seller withdraws (i'rad) from ownership. Sale makes this withdrawal known. So, the basis of shuf'ah is the seller's relinquishment, not the transaction itself. The sale is just an indicator.
I'rad is the substantive basis; sale is its evidence.
3
Apply the rule to a contested sale
If the seller admits the sale but the buyer denies it, shuf'ah is still established because the seller's admission proves his withdrawal. Since the cause (ittisal) is present and the condition (sale) is proven by admission, the pre-emptor can claim the property.
This shows that the right does not depend on the buyer's acknowledgment.
4
Contrast with opposing views
Note that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may consider the sale itself as the cause. This leads to practical differences: under Hanafi, if the sale is void (e.g., due to gharar), shuf'ah still arises if i'rad is present? Actually, the text implies that shuf'ah requires a valid sale? This is nuanced. The main difference is the reliance on seller's admission.
The Hanafi view emphasizes the pre-emptor's right as arising from the property relationship, not the contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شفعہ کا حق کب، کس طرح اور کیوں ثابت ہوتا ہے
قال والشفعة تجب بعقد البيع ومعناه بعده لا انه هو السبب لأن سببها الاتصال على ما بيناه والوجه فيه ان الشفعة انما تجب اذا رغب البائع عن ملك الدار والبيع يعرفها ولهذا يكتفى يثبوت البيع في حقه حتى ياخذها الشفيع اذا اقر البائع بالبيع وان كان المشترى يكذبه
ترجمہ اور شفعہ ثابت ہوتا ہے عقد بیع سے اور اس کے معنی بعد البیع کے ہیں۔ یہ بات نہیں ہے کہ بیچ سبب ہو اسلئے کہ شفعہ کا سبب اتصال ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ شفعہ ثابت ہوتا ہے جبکہ بائع گھر کی ملکیت سے اعراض کرے اور بیج اس اعراض کی معرف ہے اور اسی وجہ سے اکتفاء کیا جاتا ہے۔ ثبوت بیچ پر بائع کے حق میں یہاں تک کہ شفیع لے لے گا گھر کو جبکہ بائع نے بیع کا اقرار کر لیا ہوا گر چہ مشتری اس کی تکذیب کرے۔
تشریح ماقبل میں تفصیل سے گزر چکا کہ سبب شفعہ اتصال ہے اور اس کی شرط بیج ہے اگر اتصال ہو اور بیج نہ پائی جائے تو شفعہ ثابت نہ ہوگا۔
و معناه بعده کهہ کر مصنف یا اشارہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بعقد البیع میں باء برائے سبب نہیں ورنہ یہ لازم آتا کہ بیچ سبب شفعہ ہے حالانکہ سبب اتصال ہے۔ پھر یہاں ایک سوال پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ بعد بیع شفعہ کیوں ہے تو فرمایا کہ گھر دراصل مالک کی ملکیت ہے جس کو وہاں سے الگ نہیں کیا جا سکتا۔ ہاں اگر مالک اپنے اس گھر سے اعراض کرے اور کسی اور کو دینا چاہے اور بیچے تو اس کا اعراض کرنا سمجھ میں آتا ہے کیونکہ اقدام علی السمیع نے اس کے اعراض کو ظاہر کر دیا اور جب اعراض پایا جاتا ہے تبھی شفعہ ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے ہم نے کہا کہ شفعہ بیع کے بعد ثابت ہوگا۔ جب شفعہ کا مدار بائع کے اعراض پر ہے تو اس کی جانب سے بیج کا پایا جانا ثبوت شفعہ کیلئے کافی ہے۔ لہذا اگر بائع نے بیع کا اقرار کرلیا اور مشتری انکار کرتا ہے تو شفیع کو شفعہ ملے گا کیونکہ بائع کے اقرار کی وجہ سے اس کا اعراض پایا گیا اور یہی شرط شفعہ ہے۔
He (al-Quduri) said: Shuf'ah is established by the contract of sale, and its meaning is after the sale, not that it is the cause. Because its cause is connection (ittisal) as we explained. The reason is that shuf'ah is established only when the seller withdraws from ownership of the house, and sale is what makes this withdrawal known. Hence, proof of sale in his favor suffices, so that the pre-emptor takes the house if the seller admits the sale, even if the buyer denies it.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage defines the legal cause (sabab) of shuf'ah. The author clarifies a common misconception: shuf'ah is not caused by the sale itself; rather, the cause is the connection (ittisal) between the property and the pre-emptor's property. Sale is merely a condition (shart) that makes the right enforceable after it occurs. The commentary explains that the seller's withdrawal (i'rad) from ownership is the true basis, and sale is the indicator of that withdrawal. Therefore, even if the buyer denies the sale, the pre-emptor can claim shuf'ah based on the seller's admission, because the seller's admission proves his withdrawal. This is a unique Hanafi position emphasizing the pre-emptor's right as arising from the connection, not the transaction.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): Legal cause: the effective factor that generates a ruling. Here it is ittisal (connection) for shuf'ah.
اتصال (ittisal): Connection: the physical contiguity or shared boundary of properties that gives rise to pre-emption rights.
اعراض (i'rad): Withdrawal: the seller's relinquishment of ownership, which is the basis for shuf'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the cause (sabab) of shuf'ah (pre-emption)?
A) The contract of sale
B) The buyer's purchase
C) The connection (ittisal) between properties
D) The seller's withdrawal (i'rad)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, shuf'ah is caused by the physical connection of properties, not by the sale; the sale is merely a condition that makes the right enforceable.

Definition and Cause of Shuf'ah (Pre-emption)
Defines shuf'ah, distinguishing cause from condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the cause (sabab) and condition (shart) of shuf'ah in Hanafi fiqh and apply the ruling when the buyer denies the sale.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah's cause is contiguity, not sale — sale is merely the condition and indicator of the seller's abandonment.

This passage from the Book of Shuf'ah clarifies a common misconception: the sale contract does not cause the right of pre-emption; rather, it activates a right that exists due to property contiguity. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying shuf'ah rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that shuf'ah is a right of pre-emption that enables a co-owner or neighbor to take ownership of a sold property by paying its price.
The right is established at the time of sale, but not because of sale.
2
Locate the cause vs condition distinction
The text explicitly states that the sale is not the cause (sabab); the cause is contiguity (ittisal). The sale is a condition (shart) and an indicator of the seller's abandonment.
The Arabic phrase 'bi aqd al-bay'' uses the preposition 'ba' for accompaniment, not causation.
3
Analyse the reasoning
Shuf'ah is established when the seller abandons ownership (i'rad). The sale manifests this abandonment, so the sale is sufficient as evidence.
The seller's willingness to part with the property is central.
4
Apply the condition
If contiguity exists but no sale, shuf'ah is not established. If sale occurs without contiguity, shuf'ah is also not established.
Both contiguity and sale must be present for the right to arise.
5
Note the exceptional case
The shafi' can take the property even if the buyer denies the sale, as long as the seller confesses to it. The seller's confession proves abandonment.
This shows that the right is based on the seller's action, not the buyer's acknowledgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الشفعة
ترجمہ اور شفعہ ثابت ہوتا ہے عقد بیع سے اور اس کے معنی بعد البیع کے ہیں۔ یہ بات نہیں ہے کہ بیچ سبب ہو اسلئے کہ شفعہ کا سبب اتصال ہے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ شفعہ ثابت ہوتا ہے جبکہ بائع گھر کی ملکیت سے اعراض کرے اور بیج اس اعراض کی معرف ہے اور اسی وجہ سے اکتفاء کیا جاتا ہے۔ ثبوت بیچ پر بائع کے حق میں یہاں تک کہ شفیع لے لے گا گھر کو جبکہ بائع نے بیع کا اقرار کر لیا ہوا گر چہ مشتری اس کی تکذیب کرے۔
تشریح ماقبل میں تفصیل سے گزر چکا کہ سبب شفعہ اتصال ہے اور اس کی شرط بیج ہے اگر اتصال ہو اور بیج نہ پائی جائے تو شفعہ ثابت نہ ہوگا۔
و معناه بعده کهہ کر مصنف یا اشارہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بعقد البیع میں باء برائے سبب نہیں ورنہ یہ لازم آتا کہ بیچ سبب شفعہ ہے حالانکہ سبب اتصال ہے۔ پھر یہاں ایک سوال پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ بعد بیع شفعہ کیوں ہے تو فرمایا کہ گھر دراصل مالک کی ملکیت ہے جس کو وہاں سے الگ نہیں کیا جا سکتا۔ ہاں اگر مالک اپنے اس گھر سے اعراض کرے اور کسی اور کو دینا چاہے اور بیچے تو اس کا اعراض کرنا سمجھ میں آتا ہے کیونکہ اقدام علی السمیع نے اس کے اعراض کو ظاہر کر دیا اور جب اعراض پایا جاتا ہے تبھی شفعہ ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے ہم نے کہا کہ شفعہ بیع کے بعد ثابت ہوگا۔ جب شفعہ کا مدار بائع کے اعراض پر ہے تو اس کی جانب سے بیج کا پایا جانا ثبوت شفعہ کیلئے کافی ہے۔ لہذا اگر بائع نے بیع کا اقرار کرلیا اور مشتری انکار کرتا ہے تو شفیع کو شفعہ ملے گا کیونکہ بائع کے اقرار کی وجہ سے اس کا اعراض پایا گیا اور یہی شرط شفعہ ہے۔
Book of Pre-emption. Translation: Pre-emption is established by a contract of sale, and its meaning is after the sale. It is not that the sale is the cause, because the cause of pre-emption is contiguity, according to the detail we have explained. The reason for this is that pre-emption is established when the seller abandons ownership of the house, and the sale is an indicator of this abandonment, and for this reason it is sufficient to base it on the sale. It is established by the sale from the seller's side, to the extent that the pre-emptor will take the house when the seller has confessed to the sale, even if the buyer denies it. Commentary: It has already been described in detail that the cause of pre-emption is contiguity and its condition is sale. If contiguity exists but no sale occurs, pre-emption is not established. And 'its meaning after it' means that the author indicates that in 'by a contract of sale', the preposition 'ba' is not for cause; otherwise it would necessitate that the sale is the cause of pre-emption, whereas the cause is contiguity. Then here a question arises: why is pre-emption after sale? So he said that the house is essentially owned by the owner and cannot be separated from him. However, if the owner abandons his house and wants to give it to someone else and sells it, then his abandonment is understood because the action of selling manifests his abandonment, and when abandonment is found, only then is pre-emption established. Therefore we said that pre-emption is established after sale. Since the basis of pre-emption is the seller's abandonment, the existence of sale from his side is sufficient for the establishment of pre-emption. Hence, if the seller confesses to the sale and the buyer denies it, the pre-emptor will get pre-emption because due to the seller's confession, his abandonment is found, and this is the condition for pre-emption.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage defines the nature of shuf'ah (pre-emption) in Hanafi fiqh. It first clarifies that the Arabic phrase 'shuf'ah thabitah bi aqd al-bay' means that shuf'ah is established at the time of the sale contract, not that the sale is the cause. The actual cause (sabab) is contiguity (ittisal) of properties, while the sale is a condition (shart) and an indicator of the seller's willingness to part with the property. The text emphasizes that the shafi' (pre-emptor) can take the property even if the buyer denies the sale, as long as the seller confirms it, because the seller's confession proves his abandonment of ownership. This ruling highlights that the right of shuf'ah is not a transfer of ownership by sale but a right to take over a sold property due to proximity.

Key Terms
شفعہ (shuf'ah): A right of pre-emption enabling a co-owner or neighbor to take ownership of a sold property by paying its price to the buyer.
اتصال (ittisāl): Physical contiguity or shared ownership between properties that gives rise to the right of shuf'ah.
اعراض (i'rāḍ): Abandonment or turning away from ownership, manifested by the seller's act of selling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the actual cause (sabab) of shuf'ah?
A) The sale contract
B) The buyer's demand
C) The contiguity of properties
D) The seller's abandonment

Key Takeaway
Shuf'ah is caused by contiguity, not by sale; the sale is merely the condition that activates the right.

The Two Demands: Immediate Demand and Testimony for Shuf'ah
Explains the necessity of immediate demand and testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two obligatory demands for establishing shuf'ah and explain why both are necessary.

Core Idea
Shuf'ah is a weak right — silence loses it; immediate demand and testimony prove desire, not abandonment.

In Hanafi fiqh, pre-emption (shuf'ah) does not vest automatically upon sale. The pre-emptor (shafi') must take active steps to claim his right. This passage explains two essential demands: immediate demand (talab al-muathabah) and testimony demand (ishhad). They serve to demonstrate the shafi's interest and preserve evidence for court.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two demands
Locate the two demands mentioned: 'طلب المواثبة' (immediate demand) and 'الإشهاد' (testimony demand). Note that the text says both are necessary ('لا بد من').
The term 'طلب المواظبہ' in the Arabic is a variant spelling.
2
Understand why shuf'ah is a 'weak right'
The text explicitly calls shuf'ah a 'حق ضعيف' (weak right). This means it is easily lost; any indication of abandonment (i'rad) nullifies it.
Contrast with strong rights (e.g., ownership) which are not so easily lost.
3
Explain how silence indicates abandonment
If the shafi' learns of the sale and remains silent without excuse, that silence is evidence of abandonment (i'rad). The demands counteract this by showing desire.
The text emphasizes that demands prove 'رغبته فيه' (his desire for it) and not abandonment.
4
Recognize the sequential order
First, immediate demand upon knowledge. Second, testimony to witnesses. Third, formal claim before a judge (demand of contestation). The order is logical: first express desire, then secure proof, then litigate.
The commentary notes that details of the order are coming in subsequent chapters.
5
Apply the ruling: consequence of omission
If either demand is omitted, the shuf'ah right is lost. The text states that without these, the right is nullified by presumed abandonment.
This is wajib; omission leads to loss of the right.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طلب اشہاد اور طلب مواشبہ کی حیثیت
قال وتستقر بالإشهاد ولا بد من طلب المواثبة لانه حق ضعيف يبطل بالاعراض فلا بد من الاشهاد والطلب ليعلم بذالك رغبته فيه دون اعراضه عنه ولانه يحتاج الى اثبات طلبه عند القاضى ولا يمكنه الا بالاشهاد
ترجمہ اور شفعہ پختہ ہوتا ہے طلب اشہاد سے اور ضروری ہے طلب مواشبہ کا ہونا اسلئے کہ شفعہ حق ضعیف ہے جو اعراض سے باطل ہو جاتا ہے تو ضروری ہے اشہاد اور طلب کا ہونا تا کہ طلب سے شفیع کی اس میں رغبت معلوم ہو جائے نہ کہ اس سے اس کا اعراض اور اس لئے کہ شفیع محتاج ہے اپنی طلب کو ثابت کرنے کی جانب قاضی کے سامنے اور اس کو اثبات ممکن نہیں ہو گا مگر اشہاد کے ساتھ ۔
تشریح شفعہ کا سبب تو اتصال ہے اور شرط بیغ ہے لیکن ان دونوں کے باوجود اگر شفیع بلا عذر خاموش ہو جائے تو شفعہ نہیں ملے گا بلکہ معلوم ہوتے ہی طلب مواہبہ ضروری ہے پھر احتیاطا اس کے اوپر گواہ قائم کرنا پھر طلب خصومت یعنی قاضی کی عدالت میں جا کر شفعہ کو طلب کرنا۔ ان طلبوں کے درمیان بھی ترتیب ہے جس کی تفصیل ابھی آرہی ہے۔
یہاں تو مصنف نے یہ بتایا کہ شفعہ کے اندر پختگی طلب اشہاد اور طلب مواشبہ سے آئے گی کیونکہ اگر معلوم ہونے کے بعد طلب نہ کرے تو یہ دلیل اعراض ہے اور شفعہ حق ضعیف ہے جو اعراض سے باطل ہو جاتا ہے تو ضروری ہوا کہ ایسی دلیل ہو جائے جو اسکے اعراض نہ کرنے کو ثابت کر سکے اور وہ طلب مواہبہ اور اشہاد ہے اب ان سے یہ معلوم ہو جائے گا کہ شفیع نے شفعہ سے اعراض نہیں کیا بلکہ اس میں راغب تھا۔
طلب مواظبہ کے بعد طلب اشہاد کی ضرورت اس لئے ہے تا کہ شفیع قاضی کے سامنے اپنی طلب کو ثابت کر سکے اور اس کے اثبات کا ذریعہ اشہاد ہے اسلئے اثبات طلب کیلئے اشہاد ضروری ہے۔ طلب کی مزید تفصیل اگلے باب میں آ رہی ہے۔
The Status of Testimony Demand and Immediate Demand. He said: And it is established by testimony [ishhad], and immediate demand [talab al-muathabah] is necessary because it [shuf'ah] is a weak right that is nullified by abandonment; therefore testimony and demand are necessary so that by that his desire for it is known, not his abandonment of it. And because he needs to prove his demand before the judge, and he cannot do so except by testimony. Translation: Pre-emption becomes firm by testimony demand, and immediate demand is necessary because pre-emption is a weak right that is invalidated by abandonment, so testimony and demand are necessary so that by the demand the pre-emptor's desire for it is known, not his abandonment of it. And because the pre-emptor needs to prove his demand before the judge, and it is not possible for him except by testimony. Commentary: The cause of pre-emption is contiguity and the condition is sale, but despite both, if the pre-emptor remains silent without excuse, he will not get pre-emption; rather, as soon as he learns, immediate demand is necessary. Then, out of caution, he should have witnesses, then demand contestation, i.e., go to the judge's court to demand pre-emption. There is an order among these demands, the detail of which is coming. Here the author has stated that firmness in pre-emption will come from testimony demand and immediate demand because if he does not demand after learning, that is evidence of abandonment, and pre-emption is a weak right that is nullified by abandonment. So it became necessary to have evidence that proves his non-abandonment, and that is immediate demand and testimony. Thus it will be known that the pre-emptor has not abandoned pre-emption but was desirous of it. The need for testimony demand after immediate demand is so that the pre-emptor can prove his demand before the judge, and the means of proof is testimony; therefore testimony is necessary for proving the demand. Further detail of the demand is coming in the next chapter.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage discusses the two essential demands in shuf'ah: immediate demand (talab al-muathabah) and testimony demand (talab al-ishhad). The text stresses that shuf'ah is a weak right (haqq da'if) that is lost by any indication of abandonment (i'rad). Therefore, upon learning of the sale, the shafi' must immediately express his desire to claim the property in the presence of witnesses. This immediate demand (talab al-muathabah) shows his interest, while testimony serves as proof for future litigation. The commentator explains that these demands are sequential: first immediate demand upon knowledge, then testimony, then formal claim before a judge. The underlying reasoning is to protect the weak right from being nullified by silence, and to provide evidence for the shafi' to prove his claim in court.

Key Terms
طلب مواثبہ (ṭalab al-muāthabah): The immediate demand made by the pre-emptor upon learning of the sale, without delay.
اشہاد (ishhād): Testimony; the act of having witnesses testify to the demand.
حق ضعیف (ḥaqq ḍaʿīf): A weak right that is easily lost by acts indicating abandonment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a shafi' learns of the sale but remains silent without making any demand?
A) Shuf'ah is established after a long period
B) Shuf'ah is lost due to presumed abandonment
C) Shuf'ah is established upon testimony
D) Shuf'ah is transferred to the heir

Key Takeaway
Immediate demand and testimony are both wajib in Hanafi fiqh to preserve the weak right of shuf'ah from being nullified by silence.

When Ownership Transfers in Shuf'ah: Delivery or Decree
Explains that ownership transfers only by delivery or judge's decree, with three derivative cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions for ownership transfer in shuf'ah and apply them to determine ownership in three derivative scenarios.

Core Idea
Ownership transfers only by delivery or decree, not by demand alone.

You may think that after making the two demands (talab muwathaba and talab ishhad), the shafi' immediately owns the preempted property. This lesson clarifies that ownership only transfers when the buyer voluntarily delivers the property or a judge issues a decree. This is based on qiyas with the revocation of a gift. We will explore the ruling, its proof, and three practical scenarios that show the consequence of this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
The passage states that the shafi' becomes owner by taking (milk bil-akhdh) only when the buyer delivers or a judge decrees. Note that this is a condition (sabab) for ownership transfer.
The ruling is a hukm wad'i (legal cause), not a taklifi obligation.
2
Locate the proof: Qiyas on gift revocation
The author draws an analogy to revocation of a gift (ruju' fi al-hiba). Just as a donor cannot take back a gift without the donee's consent or a judge's decree, the shafi' cannot take the property from the buyer without delivery or decree.
The 'illa (cause) is that both the buyer and the donee have complete ownership (tam al-milk).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Complete ownership means the owner's right is exclusive; it cannot be removed except by the owner's will or a judicial order. Thus, in shuf'ah, the buyer's ownership is firm, so transfer requires his consent or a court order.
This is a qiyas jali (clear analogy).
4
Apply to the three derivative cases
The text gives three scenarios: (1) shafi' dies after demands but before delivery/decree → property not inherited; (2) shafi' sells his own contiguous property → shuf'ah right voided; (3) adjacent property sold before completion → no right because shafi' lacked contiguous ownership. Each illustrates that ownership did not transfer due to missing delivery/decree.
These cases show the practical benefit (thamarah) of the rule.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that ownership transfers only by taslim or hukm al-hakim. This is the standard Hanafi ruling from Zahir al-Riwayah, agreed upon by all schools.
No intra-Hanafi disagreement is reported.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شفیع دارمشفوعہ کا کب مالک بن جاتا ہے، تجب بعقد البيع‘ کی عبارت کا فائدہ
قال وتملك بالاخذ اذا سلمها المشترى او حكم بها الحاكم لان الملك للمشترى قدتم فلا ينتقل الى الشفيع الا بالتراضى اوقضاء القاضي كما في الرجوع فى الهبة وتظهر فائدة هذا فيما اذا مات الشفيع بعد الطلبين او باع داره المستحق بها الشفعة أو بيعت دار بجنب الدار المشفوعة قبل حكم الحاكم او تسليم المخاصم لا تورث عنه فى الصورة الاولى وتبطل شفعته في الثانية ولا يستحقها في الثالثة لا نعدام له ثم قوله تجب بعقد البيع بيان انه لا يجب الاعند معاوضة المال بالمال على ما نبينه ان شاء الله تعالى والله سبحانه اعلم بالصواب
الملک
ترجمہ فرمایا قدوری نے اور گھر مملوک ہوگا اپنے کے ساتھ جبکہ مشتری نے اس کو سپرد کر دیا ہو یا حاکم نے اس کا حکم کر دیا ہو اسلئے کہ مشتری کی ملکیت تام ہو چکی ہے تو وہ شفیع کی جانب منتقل نہ ہوگی مگر رضا مندی سے یا قاضی کے فیصلہ سے جیسا کہ بہہ میں رجوع کی صورت میں اور ظاہر ہوگا اس کا فائدہ اس صورت میں جبکہ شفیع دونوں طلبوں کے بعد مرجائے یا وہ اپنے اس گھر کو فروخت کر دے جس کی وجہ سے وہ شفعہ کا مستحق بن رہا ہے یا دار مشفوعہ کے پہلو میں کوئی گھر فروخت کیا جائے حاکم کے حکم یا مخاصم کی تعلیم سے پہلے تو پہلی صورت میں اس کی جانب سے گھر میراث میں تقسیم نہ ہوگا اور دوسری صورت میں اس کا شفعہ باطل ہو جائے گا اور تیسری صورت میں اس کی ملک نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے وہ اس دار کا مستحق نہ ہوگا۔ پھر قدوری کا قول تجب بعد البیع اس بات کا بیان ہے کہ شفعہ ثابت نہیں ہوتا مگر مال کے معاوضہ کے وقت مال کے ساتھ اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم انشاء اللہ بیان کریں گے اور اللہ سبحانہ ہی ٹھیک جانے والا ہے۔
تشریح مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ اتصال اور بیع کے باوجود اور طلب مواشبہ اور اشہاد کے باوجود بھی شفیع اس مکان کا مالک نہیں ہوا بلکہ مالک بننے کی دو ہی صورتیں ہیں یا تو مشتری شفیع کو وہ مکان حوالہ کر دے یا قاضی اس کا فیصلہ کر دے۔ دونوں صورتوں میں سے جو بھی صورت پائی جائے گی شفیع اس کا مالک بن جائے گا کیونکہ مشتری اس مکان کا مالک ہو چکا ہے اور اس کی ملکیت تامہ ہے اب اس مکان کو اس کی ملیکت سے نکالنے کیلئے رضامندی سے سپردگی پائی جائے یا حاکم کا فیصلہ پایا جائے كما في الرجوع في الهبة اگر کسی شخص نے کسی کو اپنا مکان ہبہ کر دیا اور قبضہ بھی کرا دیا اب واہب اس کو موہوب لڑ سے واپس لینا چاہتا ہے تو اس کی دو ہی صورتیں ہیں یا تو موہوب لہ اپنی رضامندی سے دے دے یا حاکم اس کا فیصلہ کر دے۔ بعینہ یہی صورت یہاں ہے کہ با ت شفیع خود دے دے یا حاکم کا فیصلہ ہو جائے۔ ناج کی ملکیت، ثابت ہونے کیلئے امرین میں سے کوئی ایک ہونا ضروری ہے ورنہ ملکیت نہیں ہوگی اب اس پر تین مسائل متفرع کر
When does the shafi' become owner of the property subject to shuf'ah? Benefit of the phrase 'it is established by the contract of sale'. He said: And he becomes owner by taking (akhdh) when the buyer delivers it or the judge decrees it, because the buyer's ownership is firm; it does not transfer to the shafi' except by mutual consent or the judge's decree, as in returning a gift. The benefit of this appears: if the shafi' dies after the two demands, or if he sells his house by which he was entitled to shuf'ah, or if a house adjacent to the subject property is sold before the judge's decree or the opponent's delivery, then in the first case the house is not inherited from him, in the second his shuf'ah is voided, and in the third he does not become entitled due to lack of ownership. Then his statement 'it is established by contract of sale' explains that it is not established except at the time of exchange of property for property, as we will explain, God willing. And Allah knows best. [Commentary] The author says: Despite contiguity, sale, and the two demands, the shafi' does not become owner of the property. There are only two ways to become owner: either the buyer hands over the property to the shafi', or a judge decrees it. Whichever occurs, the shafi' becomes owner. Because the buyer has already become owner, and his ownership is complete; to remove the property from his ownership, either voluntary delivery or a judge's decree is needed, as in the case of revocation of a gift. If someone gives his house as a gift and delivers possession, and then wants to revoke it, there are only two ways: either the donee returns it voluntarily, or the judge decrees it. Exactly the same situation applies here: either the shafi' himself delivers (the price) or the judge decrees. For ownership of the property to be established, one of these two things is necessary; otherwise, ownership does not occur. Now three derivative cases based on this:
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage addresses when ownership of the subject property actually transfers to the shafi'. The key point is that despite the existence of contiguity, sale, and the two demands, the shafi' does not automatically own the property. Ownership only transfers by one of two methods: (1) the buyer voluntarily delivers the property, or (2) a judge issues a decree awarding it. This is analogous to the revocation of a gift (ruju' fi al-hiba), where the donor can take back the gift only by the donee's consent or a judge's order. The text then provides three practical scenarios to illustrate the benefit of this ruling: (a) if the shafi' dies after making the two demands but before delivery or decree, the property is not inherited from him because he never owned it; (b) if the shafi' sells his own house (which gave him the right to shuf'ah), his right is voided because he no longer has contiguous property; (c) if a house adjacent to the subject property is sold before the process completes, he does not acquire the right because his ownership of the adjacent property is lacking. These scenarios emphasize that ownership transfer requires actual delivery or judicial intervention.

Key Terms
ملک بالاخذ (milk bil-akhdh): Ownership achieved by taking possession; in shuf'ah, this occurs upon delivery or decree.
تسلیم (taslīm): Delivery; the buyer handing over the property voluntarily.
حکم حاکم (ḥukm al-ḥākim): Decree of a judge; a judicial order transferring ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a shafi' makes both demands but dies before the buyer delivers the property, what happens to the property?
A) The property goes to his heirs
B) The buyer retains the property
C) The property is sold by the court
D) The shuf'ah right is inherited

Key Takeaway
Ownership in shuf'ah transfers only by buyer's delivery or judge's decree; demands alone do not confer ownership.

Ownership Transfer in Pre-emption: Delivery or Decree
determining ownership transfer and its consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two events that transfer ownership in shuf'ah and apply the ruling to the three derived cases (furu') of death, sale of own house, and sale of adjacent house.

Core Idea
The pre-emptor does not own until the buyer hands over or the judge decrees.

In the previous lesson, we learned that the shafi' makes two demands to claim pre-emption. But do those demands alone make him the owner? Al-Quduri's matn, as expanded by the Hidayah, clarifies that ownership only transfers when either the buyer willingly surrenders the property or a judge issues a decree. The proof is analogous to revoking a gift (hibah). The commentators then derive three practical scenarios that test this principle—each illustrating what happens when ownership has not yet passed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Locate Al-Quduri's statement that the shafi' 'becomes owner by taking possession' (tamalluk bi al-akhdh). Identify the two conditions that effect ownership: buyer's surrender or judge's decree.
The phrase 'bi al-akhdh' means 'by taking possession', which occurs only through delivery or judgment.
2
Understand the proof (qiyas)
The text cites qiyas to revoking a gift (al-ruju' fi al-hibah). Explain why the illa (effective cause) is the same: complete ownership in the recipient (buyer/donee) cannot be undone without consent or judicial intervention.
This is a qiyas khafi because the analogy is based on a shared legal attribute, not an explicit text.
3
Apply the ruling to three furu'
Work through each derived case: (1) death of shafi' after demands but before delivery/decree, (2) shafi' sells his own adjacent house after demands, (3) a third adjacent house is sold. Determine the shafi's ownership status in each.
Use the principle: no ownership means no inheritance, loss of adjacency voids the right, and adjacency to a non-owned house gives no right.
4
Expand the scope of the cause
Note the author's clarification that Al-Quduri's phrase 'tajib bi 'aqd al-bay'' means any monetary exchange (mu'awadah al-mal bi al-mal), not just sale. This broadens the application of shuf'ah.
This is an expansion (tawsi') of the sabab.

He said: And he becomes owner by taking possession when the buyer surrenders it or the judge decrees it, because ownership of the buyer is complete and does not transfer to the pre-emptor except by mutual consent or the judge's decree, as in the case of revoking a gift. The benefit of this appears if the pre-emptor dies after the two demands, or sells his house by virtue of which pre-emption is established, or a house adjacent to the pre-empted house is sold before the judge's decree or the opponent's surrender: it is not inherited from him in the first case, his pre-emption is invalid in the second, and he does not become entitled in the third due to lack of ownership. Then his statement: 'it becomes obligatory by the contract of sale' clarifies that it is only obligatory upon a monetary exchange, as we will explain if Allah wills. And Allah Almighty knows best the truth. Translation: Al-Quduri stated: The house will become owned by the pre-emptor when the buyer surrenders it to him or the judge decrees it, because the buyer's ownership is complete, so it will not transfer to the pre-emptor except by mutual consent or the judge's decision, as in the case of revoking a gift. The benefit appears when the pre-emptor dies after the two demands, or he sells his house by virtue of which he becomes entitled to pre-emption, or a house adjacent to the pre-empted house is sold before the judge's decree or the opponent's surrender: in the first case the house will not be inherited from him, in the second his pre-emption becomes void, and in the third he is not entitled to it due to lack of ownership. Then Al-Quduri's statement 'it becomes obligatory by the contract of sale' clarifies that pre-emption is only established upon monetary exchange, as will be explained. Explanation: The author says that despite adjacency, sale, immediate demand and notarization, the pre-emptor does not become owner until two things: either the buyer delivers the house to him or the judge decrees it. Whichever occurs, the pre-emptor becomes owner. Analogy to revoking a gift: if someone gifts a house and takes possession, the revoker can only take back with consent or judge's decree. Similarly here. So for ownership to be established, one of these two is necessary. Then three cases are derived: (1) Pre-emptor dies after the two demands: the house was not yet owned by him, so it is not part of inheritance. If heirs want it, they must claim pre-emption anew. (2) Pre-emptor sells his own house after the two demands: his pre-emption right is void because the cause (adjacency) is removed. (3) During the two demands, another adjacent house is sold: the pre-emptor cannot take that second house because he does not own the first house yet to establish adjacency. But he can take the original pre-empted house because it is in the buyer's ownership. Then the author of al-Hidayah explained that Al-Quduri's statement means pre-emption is established not only by sale but by any monetary exchange, as will be detailed.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and casuistic application. Al-Quduri states in the matn that the shafi' (pre-emptor) becomes owner of the pre-empted property only by taking possession (al-akhdh) when the buyer surrenders it or the judge decrees it. The reason is that the buyer has complete ownership, and transferring it to the shafi' requires either mutual consent or judicial decree, analogous to revoking a gift (al-hibah) where the donor cannot take back the gift without consent or court order. The commentator then highlights the practical benefit (fā'idah) by deriving three cases: (1) If the shafi' dies after making the two demands (talab al-muwathabah and talab al-ishhad) but before taking possession or judgment, the house does not become part of his estate and is not inherited; his heirs must claim pre-emption anew. (2) If the shafi' sells his own house (the one that gave him the right of pre-emption due to adjacency) after the two demands, his right to pre-emption is void because the cause (sabab), namely adjacency (ittisāl), is destroyed. (3) If another house adjacent to the pre-empted house is sold after the two demands but before possession or judgment, the shafi' cannot claim that new house because he does not yet own the original pre-empted house to establish adjacency. However, he can still claim the original pre-empted house from the buyer. Finally, the passage clarifies that Al-Quduri's phrase 'it becomes obligatory by the contract of sale' (tajib bi 'aqd al-bay') is not limited to sale but applies to any monetary exchange (mu'āwaḍah al-māl bi al-māl), as will be explained later. This is a standard Hanafi expansion of the scope of pre-emption beyond just sales.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'ah): The right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a property that has been sold to an outsider, under certain conditions.
طلب المواثبة (talab al-muwathabah): Immediate demand made upon first knowledge of the sale.
اشهاد (ishhad): Notarization or making witnesses to the demand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) At the moment of the sale contract.
D) Only after paying the price.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the pre-emptor's ownership only transfers upon actual delivery or a judge's decree, not by mere demands.
