اور امام محمد اور ز فر نے کہا کہ اگر ایک مہینہ تاخیر کر دی تو شفعہ باطل ہو جائے گا اور امام ابو یوسف کا دوسرا قول یہ ہے کہ جب شفیع کو معلوم ہے کہ قاضی فلاں روز اپنی کچہری میں بیٹھتا ہے اور اس کو کوئی عذر نہیں ہے اس کے باوجود بھی اس نے طلب خصومت نہیں کی تو شفعہ باطل ہو گیا۔ اس لئے کہ یہ اس کے اعراض پر دال ہے اور نہ لینے پر دال ہے۔ تاخیر مسقط ہے یا نہیں ، یہ اختلاف اس وقت ہے جب کہ تاخیر بغیر عذر کے ہو ورنہ عذر کی وجہ سے تاخیر بالاتفاق شفعہ کو ساقط نہیں کرے گی ۔ تو یہاں تین قول ہو گئے :-

امام محمد کے قول کی دلیل
وجه قول محمد انه لو لم يسقط بتاخير الخصومة منه ابدا يتضرر به المشترى لانه لا يمكنه التصرف حذار نقضه من جهة الشفيع فقدرناه بشهر لانه آجل و ما دونه عاجل على مامر في الايمان ترجمہ محمد کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اگر یہ ساقط نہ ہو خصومت کی تاخیر سے شفیع کی جانب سے تو مشتری اس سے ضر ر ا ٹھائے گا اس لئے کہ اس کو تصرف ممکن نہ ہو گا اس تصرف کے ٹوٹ جانے کے ڈر سے شفیع کی جانب سے تو ہم نے مقدر کر دیا اس کو ایک ماہ کے ساتھ اس لئے کہ یہ مؤخر ہے اور جو اس سے کم ہے وہ عاجل ( ہے ) جیسا کہ ایمان میں گذر چکا ہے۔ تشریح یہاں سے امام محمد سے قول کی دلیل پیش فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کبھی تک بھی خصومت کی تاخیر سے شفعہ باطل نہ ہو تو اس میں مشتری کا ضرر ہے کیونکہ وہ کبھی بھی اس میں تصرف نہیں کر سکے گا اس لئے کہ اس کو یہ خوف دامن گیر رہے گا کہ شفیع میرے تصرف کو توڑ دے گا تو ضروری ہوا کہ اس میں کچھ میعاد مقرر کر دی جائے تو ہم نے ایک مہینہ کی میعاد مقرر کر دی کہ اس سے پہلے پہلے تاخیر مسقط نہیں اور ایک مہینہ
Will pre-emption lapse due to delay in this demand? Statements of the jurists. No, pre-emption does not lapse due to delay in this demand according to Abu Hanifa, and it is also a narration from Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: If he abandons it for a month after the witnesses, it becomes void, and this is the statement of Zufar, meaning when he abandons it without excuse. And from Abu Yusuf: If he abandons litigation in one of the qadi's sessions, his pre-emption becomes void, because when a session of his courts passes and he did not litigate in it voluntarily, that indicates his turning away and surrender. Explanation: In the previous section, it passed that after the two demands, the pre-emption becomes firm. So Imam Abu Hanifa said, and this is also one narration from Abu Yusuf, that delay in the demand of litigation will not invalidate pre-emption. And Imam Muhammad and Zufar said: If he delays for one month, the pre-emption becomes void. And Imam Abu Yusuf's second saying is: When the pre-emptor knows that the qadi sits in his court on a certain day and he has no excuse, yet he did not demand litigation, then his pre-emption becomes void, because this indicates his turning away and relinquishment. Delay is cancellative or not? This difference is when the delay is without excuse; otherwise, with excuse, delay does not cancel pre-emption by consensus. So here there are three statements: 1. Statement of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's one narration): delay is not cancellative. 2. Statement of Muhammad and Zufar: it hinges on one month. 3. Statement of Abu Yusuf: missing a qadi's session without excuse is cancellative. Note: Al-Hidayah and Muntqa al-Abhur consider Imam's (Abu Hanifa's) statement as the apparent school and give fatwa on it, while Zayla'i, Majma' al-Anhar, and Sakb al-Anhar give fatwa on Imam Muhammad's statement. Rather, in Sakb al-Anhar vol. 2 p. 407, it says: 'And in al-Sharnablaliyya from al-Burhan that it is the most correct to give fatwa, so memorize.' Al-Shami vol. 5 p. 144 narrates both fatwas and prefers Imam Muhammad's statement. The Proof of Imam Muhammad's Statement: The basis of Muhammad's statement is that if it does not lapse due to delay in litigation from him ever, the buyer will be harmed because he cannot transact for fear of annulment from the pre-emptor. So we set a limit of a month, because it is a delayed period, and less than that is immediate, as passed in oaths. Explanation: Here he presents the proof of Imam Muhammad's statement: If pre-emption never lapses due to delay in litigation from the pre-emptor, then the buyer would be harmed because he would never be able to transact, fearing that the pre-emptor will break his transaction. So it became necessary to fix a term. So we set a term of one month such that delay before that does not cancel, and one month...
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether delaying the third demand (talab al-khusumah wa al-tamalluk) before the qadi invalidates the right of pre-emption. The text summarizes the views: Abu Hanifa holds that delay does not cause lapse; one narration from Abu Yusuf agrees. Muhammad and Zufar say that a delay of one month without excuse invalidates the right. Another narration from Abu Yusuf states that missing a single session of the qadi's court voluntarily indicates abandonment and thus invalidates the right. The commentary clarifies that if there is a valid excuse, delay does not invalidate by consensus. After presenting the positions, the text provides a tarjih (preference): Al-Hidayah and Muntqa al-Abhur follow Abu Hanifa's view as the apparent school, but later authorities like Zayla'i, Majma' al-Anhar, and Sakb al-Anhar prefer Muhammad's view, and al-Shami also inclines toward Muhammad. Finally, the proof for Muhammad's view is given: to prevent harm to the buyer, who otherwise would be indefinitely unable to use the property for fear of the pre-emptor's claim. Thus, a one-month limit is set as a reasonable period for the pre-emptor to act.

Key Terms
طلب الخصومة (talab al-khusumah): The third demand of pre-emption, made before the qadi, involving litigation and formal claim for ownership.
مخاصمة (mukhasama): The act of litigating or contesting the right in court.
اعراض (i'rad): Turning away or abandoning the right, evidenced by inaction.
مسقط (musqit): That which causes the right to lapse or be cancelled.

Checkpoint
According to the text, which authority's view on delay in talab al-khusumah is preferred by later Hanafi jurists such as al-Zayla'i and al-Shami?
A) Abu Hanifa's view that delay never invalidates pre-emption.
B) Muhammad's view that delay of one month without excuse invalidates pre-emption.
C) Abu Yusuf's second narration that missing a court session invalidates pre-emption.
D) Zufar's view that any delay without excuse invalidates pre-emption.

Key Takeaway
Within the Hanafi school, delay in talab al-khusumah can cause lapse of pre-emption, but the threshold differs by imam; later authorities prefer a one-month limit (Muhammad's view).

The Proof for Muhammad's Position: Qiyas Based on Harm to the Buyer
Explains the proof (dalil) for Imam Muhammad's position on delay in talab al-khusumah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the qiyas (analogical reasoning) used by Imam Muhammad to set a one-month limit for lapse of pre-emption due to delay in talab al-khusumah, and evaluate its strength.

Core Idea
Imam Muhammad uses qiyas: indefinite delay harms the buyer, so a one-month limit is set by analogy to oaths.

In the previous lesson, we learned that Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar held that a delay of one month without excuse in talab al-khusumah invalidates pre-emption. But what is their proof? This lesson unpacks the qiyas (analogical reasoning) behind their position. Understanding this proof is essential for appreciating how Hanafi jurists derive rulings from rational considerations when no direct textual evidence exists.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling to be justified
The ruling is that delay in talab al-khusumah for one month without excuse causes the pre-emption right to lapse. This is the hukm of the far' (new case).
Imam Muhammad and Zufar hold this view; others do not.
2
Identify the illa (effective cause) for the ruling
The illa is the harm (darar) inflicted upon the buyer if the pre-emptor can delay indefinitely. The buyer cannot freely use or sell the property because of the constant threat of the pre-emptor's claim.
Harm to a third party is a recognized legal consideration in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Determine the asl (original case) used for analogy
The asl is the ruling in the chapter of oaths (al-ayman) where a period of one month is considered 'delayed' (ajal) and less than that is 'immediate' (ajal). The text says 'as passed in oaths'.
In oaths, if someone swears to do something 'delayed', a month is the minimum period that counts as delay.
4
Map the qiyas structure
Asl: oath - delay of a month counts as delayed. Hukm asl: a delayed action is not immediate. Far': pre-emptor's delay in talab al-khusumah. Illa: the need for a definite time limit to avoid harm. Hukm far': if delay reaches one month, the right lapses.
This is a qiyas jali (clear analogy) because the illa is explicit: setting a time limit to prevent harm.
5
Evaluate the strength of the proof
The proof is based on qiyas and istihsan (juristic preference) to prevent harm. It is not from Quran or Sunnah directly. Some Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa) did not accept this qiyas, considering the established right too strong to lapse by mere time.
The text notes this can be overridden by istihsan, meaning another stronger consideration (preserving the pre-emptor's right) may prevail.

تنبیہ ہدایہ اور منتقی الا بحر میں امام صاحب کے قول کو ظاہر مذہب بتا کر اسی پر فتویٰ دیا ہے، اور زیلعی اور مجمع الانہر اور سکب الانہر میں امام محمد کے قول پر فتویٰ دیا ہے بلکہ سکب الانہر ص ۷ ۴۰ ج ۲ پر یہ الفاظ ہیں وفی الشرنبلالة عن البرهان انه اصح ما يُفتى به فلی حفظ ، شامی ص ۱۴۴ ج ۵ پر دونوں فتوے نقل کر کے قول امام محمد کوترجیح دی ہے۔
امام محمد کے قول کی دلیل
وجه قول محمد انه لو لم يسقط بتاخير الخصومة منه ابدا يتضرر به المشترى لانه لا يمكنه التصرف حذار نقضه من جهة الشفيع فقدرناه بشهر لانه آجل و ما دونه عاجل على مامر في الايمان ترجمہ محمد کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اگر یہ ساقط نہ ہو خصومت کی تاخیر سے شفیع کی جانب سے تو مشتری اس سے ضر ر ا ٹھائے گا اس لئے کہ اس کو تصرف ممکن نہ ہو گا اس تصرف کے ٹوٹ جانے کے ڈر سے شفیع کی جانب سے تو ہم نے مقدر کر دیا اس کو ایک ماہ کے ساتھ اس لئے کہ یہ مؤخر ہے اور جو اس سے کم ہے وہ عاجل ( ہے ) جیسا کہ ایمان میں گذر چکا ہے۔ تشریح یہاں سے امام محمد سے قول کی دلیل پیش فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کبھی تک بھی خصومت کی تاخیر سے شفعہ باطل نہ ہو تو اس میں مشتری کا ضرر ہے کیونکہ وہ کبھی بھی اس میں تصرف نہیں کر سکے گا اس لئے کہ اس کو یہ خوف دامن گیر رہے گا کہ شفیع میرے تصرف کو توڑ دے گا تو ضروری ہوا کہ اس میں کچھ میعاد مقرر کر دی جائے تو ہم نے ایک مہینہ کی میعاد مقرر کر دی کہ اس سے پہلے پہلے تاخیر مسقط نہیں اور ایک مہینہ
Will pre-emption lapse due to delay in this demand? Statements of the jurists. No, pre-emption does not lapse due to delay in this demand according to Abu Hanifa, and it is also a narration from Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: If he abandons it for a month after the witnesses, it becomes void, and this is the statement of Zufar, meaning when he abandons it without excuse. And from Abu Yusuf: If he abandons litigation in one of the qadi's sessions, his pre-emption becomes void, because when a session of his courts passes and he did not litigate in it voluntarily, that indicates his turning away and surrender. Explanation: In the previous section, it passed that after the two demands, the pre-emption becomes firm. So Imam Abu Hanifa said, and this is also one narration from Abu Yusuf, that delay in the demand of litigation will not invalidate pre-emption. And Imam Muhammad and Zufar said: If he delays for one month, the pre-emption becomes void. And Imam Abu Yusuf's second saying is: When the pre-emptor knows that the qadi sits in his court on a certain day and he has no excuse, yet he did not demand litigation, then his pre-emption becomes void, because this indicates his turning away and relinquishment. Delay is cancellative or not? This difference is when the delay is without excuse; otherwise, with excuse, delay does not cancel pre-emption by consensus. So here there are three statements: 1. Statement of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's one narration): delay is not cancellative. 2. Statement of Muhammad and Zufar: it hinges on one month. 3. Statement of Abu Yusuf: missing a qadi's session without excuse is cancellative. Note: Al-Hidayah and Muntqa al-Abhur consider Imam's (Abu Hanifa's) statement as the apparent school and give fatwa on it, while Zayla'i, Majma' al-Anhar, and Sakb al-Anhar give fatwa on Imam Muhammad's statement. Rather, in Sakb al-Anhar vol. 2 p. 407, it says: 'And in al-Sharnablaliyya from al-Burhan that it is the most correct to give fatwa, so memorize.' Al-Shami vol. 5 p. 144 narrates both fatwas and prefers Imam Muhammad's statement. The Proof of Imam Muhammad's Statement: The basis of Muhammad's statement is that if it does not lapse due to delay in litigation from him ever, the buyer will be harmed because he cannot transact for fear of annulment from the pre-emptor. So we set a limit of a month, because it is a delayed period, and less than that is immediate, as passed in oaths. Explanation: Here he presents the proof of Imam Muhammad's statement: If pre-emption never lapses due to delay in litigation from the pre-emptor, then the buyer would be harmed because he would never be able to transact, fearing that the pre-emptor will break his transaction. So it became necessary to fix a term. So we set a term of one month such that delay before that does not cancel, and one month...
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether delaying the third demand (talab al-khusumah wa al-tamalluk) before the qadi invalidates the right of pre-emption. The text summarizes the views: Abu Hanifa holds that delay does not cause lapse; one narration from Abu Yusuf agrees. Muhammad and Zufar say that a delay of one month without excuse invalidates the right. Another narration from Abu Yusuf states that missing a single session of the qadi's court voluntarily indicates abandonment and thus invalidates the right. The commentary clarifies that if there is a valid excuse, delay does not invalidate by consensus. After presenting the positions, the text provides a tarjih (preference): Al-Hidayah and Muntqa al-Abhur follow Abu Hanifa's view as the apparent school, but later authorities like Zayla'i, Majma' al-Anhar, and Sakb al-Anhar prefer Muhammad's view, and al-Shami also inclines toward Muhammad. Finally, the proof for Muhammad's view is given: to prevent harm to the buyer, who otherwise would be indefinitely unable to use the property for fear of the pre-emptor's claim. Thus, a one-month limit is set as a reasonable period for the pre-emptor to act.

Key Terms
طلب الخصومة (talab al-khusumah): The third demand of pre-emption, made before the qadi, involving litigation and formal claim for ownership.
ضرر (darar): Harm or injury; a key legal principle: 'no harm and no reciprocating harm' (la darar wa la dirar).
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning in Islamic law; deriving a ruling for a new case from an original case due to shared effective cause (illa).
آجل (ajal): Delayed; a period that is not immediate. In oaths, a month is considered ajal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Imam Muhammad's qiyas for the lapse of pre-emption, what is the effective cause (illa) that connects the original case (oaths) to the new case (delay in talab al-khusumah)?
A) The need to punish the pre-emptor for laziness.
B) The need to set a definite time limit to prevent harm to the buyer.
C) The similarity of the legal procedures in oaths and pre-emption.
D) The consensus of the companions.

Key Takeaway
Imam Muhammad's proof for lapse after one month is a qiyas based on preventing harm to the buyer, using the one-month benchmark from oaths.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Effect of Delay in Litigation on the Right of Preemption
Intra-Hanafi dispute on delay in litigation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three Hanafi positions on whether delay in litigation cancels shuf'a and evaluate the proofs of each position.

Core Idea
A right, once established, is not lost by mere delay—unless a specific term (one month) or overt aversion is proven.

The right of pre-emption (shuf'a) gives a co-owner or neighbor the power to step into a sale. But what if the pre-emptor delays in taking the buyer to court? Does inaction forfeit the right? The Hanafi school has multiple views on this question, reflecting deeper principles about the stability of rights and the need to protect buyers from indefinite uncertainty. This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi dispute, guiding you through the proofs of each position and their practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Hanafi positions
From the passage, list the three views: (1) Abu Hanifa and one narration of Abu Yusuf: delay does not nullify; (2) Muhammad and Zufar: delay of one month nullifies; (3) Second narration of Abu Yusuf: missing a judge's session without excuse nullifies. Note that this dispute applies only when delay is without excuse.
All positions agree that delay with an excuse (like absence of a judge) does not nullify by consensus.
2
Analyze the proof of Muhammad and Zufar
Understand their qiyas: they analogize to the chapter on oaths, where a month is considered a deferred (ājil) period. The effective cause (illa) is the buyer's harm—if delay were infinite, the buyer could never safely dispose of the property. So they set a fixed one-month limit.
Zufar agreed with Muhammad on this point.
3
Analyze the proof of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa argues from the principle that a stable right falls only by explicit waiver (isqat). He counters the buyer's harm by pointing out that harm also exists when the pre-emptor is absent (travel), yet the right remains. Therefore, harm alone does not justify nullification.
Abu Hanifa also uses the case of the absence of a judge: if no judge is available, delay is excused and the right is preserved by consensus.
4
Examine the fatwa variance
Later Hanafi authorities differ on which position is operative for fatwa. The Hidayah and Muntqa al-Abhur give fatwa on Abu Hanifa's view, while Zayla'i, Majma' al-Anhur, Saqb al-Anhur, and Shami prefer Muhammad's view. A student of fiqh must be aware of both.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is clear: a pre-emptor who delays may or may not lose his right depending on which view is followed.

ترجمہ اور شفعہ ساقط نہیں ہوگا اس طلب کو مؤخر کرنے کی وجہ سے ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اور یہی ایک روایت ہے ابو یوسف سے ، اور محمد نے کہا کہ اگر اس نے اشہاد کے بعد ایک مہینہ تک خصومت کو چھوڑ دیا تو شفعہ باطل ہو جائیگا اور یہی زفر کا قول ہے اس کے معنی یہ ہیں جب کہ وہ خصومت کو بلا نظیر کے چھوڑے، اور ابو یوسف سے دوسری روایت ہے کہ جب اس نے قاضی کی مجلسوں میں سے کسی مجلس کے اندر مخاصمت کو چھوڑ دیا تو اس کا شفعہ باطل ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ جب قاضی کی مجلسوں میں سے کوئی مجلس گذرگئی اور اس نے اختیار سے اس مجلس میں مخاصمت نہیں کی تو یہ اس کے اعراض اور اس کی تسلیم پر دال ہے۔ تشریح ماقبل میں گذر چکا ہے کہ طلبین کے بعد شفعہ میں پختگی پیدا ہو جاتی ہے۔ لہذا امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا اور امام ابو یوسف کی بھی یہی ایک روایت ہے کہ طلب خصومت میں تا خیر شفعہ کو باطل نہیں کرے گی۔

وجه قول محمد انه لو لم يسقط بتاخير الخصومة منه ابدا يتضرر به المشترى لانه لا يمكنه التصرف حذار نقضه من جهة الشفيع فقدرناه بشهر لانه آجل و ما دونه عاجل على مامر في الايمان

ترجمہ محمد کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اگر یہ ساقط نہ ہو خصومت کی تاخیر سے شفیع کی جانب سے تو مشتری اس سے ضر ر ا ٹھائے گا اس لئے کہ اس کو تصرف ممکن نہ ہو گا اس تصرف کے ٹوٹ جانے کے ڈر سے شفیع کی جانب سے تو ہم نے مقدر کر دیا اس کو ایک ماہ کے ساتھ اس لئے کہ یہ مؤخر ہے اور جو اس سے کم ہے وہ عاجل ( ہے ) جیسا کہ ایمان میں گذر چکا ہے۔

تشریح یہاں سے امام محمد سے قول کی دلیل پیش فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کبھی تک بھی خصومت کی تاخیر سے شفعہ باطل نہ ہو تو اس میں مشتری کا ضرر ہے کیونکہ وہ کبھی بھی اس میں تصرف نہیں کر سکے گا اس لئے کہ اس کو یہ خوف دامن گیر رہے گا کہ شفیع میرے تصرف کو توڑ دے گا تو ضروری ہوا کہ اس میں کچھ میعاد مقرر کر دی جائے تو ہم نے ایک مہینہ کی میعاد مقرر کر دی کہ اس سے پہلے پہلے تاخیر مسقط نہیں اور ایک مہینہ

تک تاخیر مسقط ہے اس لئے کہ ہدایہ ص ۴۸۵ ج ۲ کتاب الایمان میں ایک ماہ سے کم کو قلیل مدت اور ایک ماہ اور اس سے زیادہ کو بعید مدت شمار کیا گیا ہے۔

امام ابوحنیفہ کے قول کی دلیل
ووجه قول ابى حنيفة وهو ظاهر المذهب وعليه الفتوى ان الحق متى ثبت واستقر لا يسقط الاباسقاطه وهو التصريح بلسانه كما في سائر الحقوق وما ذكر من الضرر يشكل بما اذا كان غائبا ولا فرق في حق المشترى بين الحضر والسفر ولو علم انه لم يكن فى البلدة قاض لا تبطل شفعته بالتاخير بالاتفاق لانه لا يتمكن من الخصومة الاعند القاضى فكان عذرا

ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کے قول کی وجہ اور یہی ظاہر مذہب ہے اور اسی پر فتویٰ ہے یہ ہے کہ حق جب ثابت اور پختہ ہو گیا ساقط نہیں ہوگا مگر اس کے (صاحب حق کے ) ساقط کرنے سے اور وہ اس کی زبان سے تصریح کرنا ہے جیسا کہ تمام حقوق میں اور جو ضر ر ذ کر کیا گیا ہے اس پر اشکال کیا جاتا ہے اس صورت کے ساتھ جب کہ شفیع غائب ہو اور مشتری کے حق میں حضر اور سفر کے درمیان کوئی فرق نہیں ہے اور اگر یہ بات معلوم ہوئی کہ شہر میں قاضی نہیں تھا تو بالا تفاق تاخیر کی وجہ سے اس کا شفعہ باطل نہیں ہو گا اس لئے کہ وہ خصومت پر قادر نہیں تھا مگر قاضی کے سامنے تو یہ عذر ہو گیا۔

تشریح یہ امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل ہے جس کے بارے میں ہم کچھ عرض کر چکے ہیں۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں: اصول یہ مقرر ہے کہ حق ثابت ہو جاتا ہے پھر ختم نہیں ہوتا ، ہاں صاحب حق ہی ساقط کر دے تو اور بات ہے لیکن اسقاط و تو ہمات سے اسقاط نہیں ہوتا بلکہ صاحب حق کی زبانی صراحت درکار ہے۔ تمام حقوق میں یہی اصول ہے، لہذا حق شفعہ میں بھی یہی اصول جاری ہوگا۔

امام محمد نے یہاں ایک دلیل پیش کی تھی کہ اگر شفعہ ثابت نہ ہو تو مشتری کو نقصان پہنچے گا؟ اس کو جواب دیا کہ اگر شفیع غائب ہو جب بھی اسے معلوم ہوگا اس کو شلوہ ملے گا حالانکہ ضرر یہاں بھی موجود ہے تو جب شفیع کے سفر کی صورت میں مشتری کے ضر کو برداشت کیا گیا ہے، شفیع کے حضر میں رہتے ہوئے بھی اس ضرر کو برداشت کرنا چاہئے کیونکہ سفر اور حضر کے درمیان مشتری کے حق میں کوئی فرق نہیں ہے۔ یہاں ہدایہ کے حاشیہ میں اچھا اشکال و جواب ہے ، اگر عذر کی وجہ سے تاخیر ہو جائے تو بالا تفاق شفعہ ساقط نہیں ہوتا، لہذا اگر شہر میں قاضی نہ ہو اور اس کی وجہ سے تاخیر ہوگئی تو یہ تاخیر بالعذر ہے۔ اس تاخیر کی وجہ سے بالا تفاق شفعہ باطل نہ ہو گا کیونکہ جب قاضی ہی نہیں تھا تو وہ مخاصمت کہاں کرتا ؟
Translation: And pre-emption will not be invalidated due to delay in this demand according to Abu Hanifa, and this is one narration from Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: if after making witnesses he left the litigation for one month, then pre-emption becomes invalid, and this is the statement of Zufar. Its meaning is when he leaves litigation without an excuse. And from Abu Yusuf there is another narration: when he has left litigation within one of the judge's sessions, then his pre-emption becomes invalid because when one of the judge's sessions has passed and he did not litigate intentionally in that session, this indicates his turning away and his acceptance. The explanation has passed previously that after the two demands, pre-emption becomes firmly established. Therefore Imam Abu Hanifa said, and this is one narration from Abu Yusuf, that delay in litigation will not invalidate pre-emption. And Imam Muhammad and Zufar said: if he delays for one month, pre-emption will become invalid. And the second statement of Imam Abu Yusuf is: when the pre-emptor knows that the judge sits in his court on a certain day and he has no excuse, yet he did not demand litigation, then his pre-emption becomes invalid, because this indicates his aversion and his non-acceptance. Delay is a cause of annulment or not? This disagreement is when the delay is without excuse; otherwise, by excuse, delay does not annul pre-emption by consensus. So here three statements emerge: (1) Statement of the two shaykhs: delay does not annul. (2) Statement of Muhammad and Zufar: based on one month. (3) Statement of Abu Yusuf: delay from the judge's session without excuse is annulling. Note: In Hidayah and Muntqa al-Abhur, the statement of Imam is considered the apparent madhhab and fatwa is given on it. And in Zayla'i, Majma' al-Anhur, and Saqb al-Anhur, fatwa is given on Muhammad's statement. Rather, in Saqb al-Anhur vol.2 p.740 it is written: 'And from Shurunbulali from al-Burhan that it is the soundest on which fatwa is given, so memorize it.' In Shami vol.5 p.144, both fatwas are transmitted and preference is given to Muhammad's statement. The proof of Muhammad's statement: 'The basis of Muhammad's statement is that if it were not annulled by delay in litigation on the part of the pre-emptor forever, the buyer would suffer harm because he would not be able to transact out of fear of being undone by the pre-emptor, so we set it at one month because it is deferred and what is less than it is immediate, as passed in oaths.' Translation of Muhammad's statement's reason: It is that if it were not annulled by delay in litigation from the side of the pre-emptor, the buyer would suffer harm from it because he would not be able to transact out of fear of being undone by the pre-emptor, so we estimated it with one month because it is deferred and what is less than it is immediate, as passed in oaths. Explanation: Here he presents the proof of Muhammad's statement: if even for a long time pre-emption were not invalidated by delay in litigation, there would be harm to the buyer because he would never be able to transact, since the fear would haunt him that the pre-emptor might break his transaction. So it was necessary to fix a term; we fixed one month as the term: before it delay does not annul, and after one month delay annuls, because in Hidayah vol.2 p.485 in the Book of Oaths, less than one month is considered a short period, and one month and more is considered a long period. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa's statement: 'And the basis of Abu Hanifa's statement, and it is the apparent madhhab and on it is fatwa, is that when a right is established and stable, it does not fall except by its relinquishment by the owner, which is explicit verbal expression as in all other rights. And what is mentioned about harm is problematic in the case when the pre-emptor is absent, and there is no difference in the right of the buyer between residence and travel. And if it is known that there was no judge in the town, his pre-emption is not invalidated by delay by consensus because he is not able to litigate except before the judge, so this is an excuse.' Translation: And the reason of Abu Hanifa's statement, and this is the apparent madhhab and on it is fatwa, is that when a right is established and stable, it will not fall except by its relinquishment, which is explicit verbal expression as in all rights. And the harm that was mentioned is problematic with the case when the pre-emptor is absent, and there is no difference for the buyer between residence and travel. And if it is known that there was no judge in the town, his pre-emption is not invalidated by delay by consensus, because he is not able to litigate except before the judge, so this becomes an excuse. Explanation: This is the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa, about which we have already discussed somewhat. He says: The principle is established that a right becomes established and then does not end; yes, if the owner himself relinquishes it, that is different, but relinquishment is not through intentions; rather, explicit verbal expression from the owner is required. This principle applies to all rights; therefore, it will apply to the right of pre-emption as well. Imam Muhammad had presented a proof here: if pre-emption were not established, would the buyer suffer loss? He responds: if the pre-emptor is absent, even then he will be known and he will receive the property, although harm exists here as well. So when in the case of the pre-emptor's travel the buyer's harm is tolerated, then while the pre-emptor is present, this harm should also be tolerated because between travel and residence there is no difference in the right of the buyer. Here in the margin of Hidayah there is a good objection and answer: if delay occurs due to an excuse, then by consensus pre-emption does not fall. So if there is no judge in the city and due to that delay occurred, then this delay is with excuse. Due to this delay, by consensus pre-emption will not be invalidated because if there is no judge, where would he litigate?
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether the right of pre-emption (shuf'a) is lost when the pre-emptor delays in filing a lawsuit (khusumat) after making the initial demands. The text presents three positions: (1) Imam Abu Hanifa and one narration of Abu Yusuf hold that mere delay does not invalidate shuf'a, because a right once established does not fall except by explicit waiver. (2) Imam Muhammad and Zufar hold that delay beyond one month invalidates shuf'a, based on the harm to the buyer who cannot freely dispose of the property if the pre-emptor may challenge him at any time; they analogize to the fixed period in oaths. (3) The second narration of Abu Yusuf holds that missing a session of the judge without excuse invalidates shuf'a, as this indicates the pre-emptor's aversion. The passage notes that fatwa has been given on both Abu Hanifa's and Muhammad's positions in different works, with some preferring Muhammad's view. The commentary here follows the order: it states the issue, gives the three positions, then provides the proof for Muhammad's view (the buyer's harm and the one-month limit based on 'ajil and ajil from the chapter on oaths), followed by the proof for Abu Hanifa's view (the stability of rights and the analogy to the absentee pre-emptor, who does not lose his right despite prolonged absence). Abu Hanifa's proof also uses the case of the absence of a judge as an excuse that preserves the right. The teacher concludes by reinforcing the principle that the right of shuf'a, like all rights, is not forfeited by mere inaction but only by explicit renunciation.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'a): Right of pre-emption, the legal right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase a property that has been sold to an outsider.
طلب خصومت (talab khusumat): The third demand or formal claim before a judge after the initial two demands (طلب طلب and طلب اشهاد).
مخاصمت (mukhasamat): Litigation or formal legal proceeding, the act of bringing the case to the judge.
اسقاط (isqat): Relinquishment or annulment of a right by the owner through explicit verbal expression.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, how long can a pre-emptor delay litigation after making witnesses before the right of pre-emption becomes invalid?
A) The delay of any period invalidates it.
B) The delay of more than one month invalidates it.
C) The delay of more than one year invalidates it.
D) Delay never invalidates it.

Key Takeaway
The right of pre-emption is not automatically lost by delay; its persistence depends on whether there is explicit waiver, a fixed term (one month), or evidence of aversion, and the Hanafi school has multiple valid positions on this issue.

Abu Hanifa's Proof That Delay Does Not Nullify Shuf'ah
Presents Abu Hanifa's rational proof for shuf'ah not lapsing by delay.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's position on the effect of delay on shuf'ah and evaluate his rational proof against the opposing view of Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
An established right is not lost by delay, only by explicit renunciation.

This passage presents Abu Hanifa's rational argument (dalil aqli) that the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) is not forfeited by mere delay. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, contrary to a contrary view attributed to Imam Muhammad. The reasoning is based on a general principle: once a right is established, it only falls by the right-holder's explicit waiver, just like all other rights.

Guided Path
1
State the legal issue
The issue is whether mere delay in claiming shuf'ah after knowledge of the sale causes the right to be forfeited. Identify the core question: does inaction without explicit renunciation nullify the right?
The issue arises when the shafi' knows of the sale but does not immediately demand his right.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position
From the text, extract the Hanafi position: 'the right, when established and confirmed, does not fall except by its renunciation, and that is explicit statement by his tongue.' This is the mufta bihi view.
The text explicitly states 'wa hwa zahir al-madhhab wa alayhi al-fatwa'.
3
Identify the opposing view
Although not directly named in the text, the opposing position is held by Imam Muhammad (and some later scholars): that delay may nullify shuf'ah due to harm to the buyer. Infer this from the refutation.
The text refutes an objection based on harm, which is the basis of the opposing view.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's dalil aqli
Break down the rational argument: (a) general principle – rights do not fall without renunciation; (b) comparison to absence – harm exists even when pre-emptor is absent but right remains; (c) the exception – if no judge exists, delay is excused by consensus.
The argument uses analogy (qiyas) to other rights and the absence scenario.
5
Apply the exception
Note the consensus case: if there is no judge in the city, delay does not void shuf'ah at all. This strengthens the principle that only inability to litigate excuses delay, not mere inaction.
This shows that the determining factor is ability to claim, not time elapsed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووجه قول ابى حنيفة وهو ظاهر المذهب وعليه الفتوى ان الحق متى ثبت واستقر لا يسقط الاباسقاطه وهو التصريح بلسانه كما في سائر الحقوق وما ذكر من الضرر يشكل بما اذا كان غائبا ولا فرق في حق المشترى بين الحضر والسفر ولو علم انه لم يكن فى البلدة قاض لا تبطل شفعته بالتاخير بالاتفاق لانه لا يتمكن من الخصومة الاعند القاضى فكان عذرا
And the argument of Abu Hanifa — and it is the apparent madhhab and upon it is the fatwa — is that the right, whenever it is established and confirmed, does not fall except by its renunciation, and that is the explicit statement by his tongue, as in all other rights. And what was mentioned of harm is problematic with the case where he (the pre-emptor) is absent, and there is no difference in the right of the buyer between residence and travel. And if it is known that there was no judge in the city, his pre-emption does not become void by delay by consensus, because he is not able to litigate except before the judge, so this becomes an excuse.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage presents Abu Hanifa's rational proof (dalil aqli) for the position that the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) is not forfeited by mere delay. The reasoning is based on a general principle: once a right is established and confirmed, it ceases only through the right-holder's explicit renunciation, just like all other rights. The objection that delay harms the buyer is answered with the example of an absent pre-emptor — harm exists there too but does not nullify the right. Similarly, the buyer's potential harm is tolerated regardless of whether the pre-emptor is present or traveling. The only exception is when there is no judge in the town; in that case, delay is excused by consensus because the pre-emptor cannot initiate litigation. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'ah): The right of a co-owner or adjacent neighbour to purchase jointly-owned property from a buyer at the same price.
شفيع (shafi'): The person entitled to pre-emption (shuf'ah).
الظاهر المذهب (al-zahir al-madhhab): The most authoritative and well-known position within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when does the right of shuf'ah fall (become void)?
A) After one month of knowledge without claiming
B) Only by the pre-emptor's explicit renunciation or statement
C) Automatically if the pre-emptor travels abroad
D) When the buyer takes possession of the house

Key Takeaway
The right of shuf'ah, once established, remains until explicitly renounced; delay alone does not nullify it.

Procedure of Qadi When Pre-emptor Claims in Court
Describes the steps the qadi follows before hearing the buyer's response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the procedural steps the qadi must follow when a pre-emptor claims in court and identify the rationale for each step.

Core Idea
The qadi must first verify the pre-emptor's ownership evidence and specify the property and cause before hearing the buyer.

This passage details the procedural sequence a qadi must observe when a pre-emptor (shafi') approaches the court. The qadi cannot simply turn to the buyer; he must first ensure the pre-emptor has a valid basis for his claim. Understanding this process is crucial for anyone studying the Hanafi law of pre-emption (shuf'ah), as it ensures justice and prevents frivolous claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence of inquiries
Read the passage and list the three main questions the qadi asks: (1) verification of ownership, (2) location and boundaries, (3) cause of pre-emption.
The order is important: first ownership, then specification, then cause.
2
Understand the role of possession (yad)
Note why yad is insufficient as proof. Think about the legal category of yad as a zanni (probabilistic) indicator, not a qati (certain) proof.
Possession may be based on lease, amana, etc. hence requires evidence.
3
Distinguish between two types of specification
The pre-emptor must specify the property in which he claims the right (the purchased property) and also the property that gives him the right (e.g., his own house).
Al-Khassaf's view: specifying the adjoining property is required.
4
Link to the cause of pre-emption
The cause (co-ownership or neighbourhood) determines the validity of the claim. The qadi asks to ensure the pre-emptor has a valid sabab.
If he claims neighbourhood, he must identify his own adjoining property.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال واذا تقدم الشفيع الى القاضى فادعى الشر أو طلب الشفعة سال القاضى المدعى عليه فان اعترف بملكه الذي يشفع به والا كلفه باقامة البينة لان اليد ظاهر محتمل فلا تكفى لاثبات الاستحقاق قال يسال القاضي المدعى قبل ان يقبل على المدعى عليه عن موضع الدار وحدودها لانه ادعى حقافيها فصار كما اذا ادعى رقبتها واذا بين ذلك يساله عن سبب شفعته لاختلاف اسبابها فان قال انا شفيعها بدارلى تلاصقها الان تم دعواه على ما قاله الخصاف وذكر في الفتاوى تحديد هذه الدار التي يشفع بها ايضا وقد بيناه في الكتاب الموسوم بالتجنيس والمزيد
He said: When the pre-emptor comes to the judge and claims the purchase or requests pre-emption, the judge asks the defendant. If he (the defendant) acknowledges his (the plaintiff's) ownership by which he claims pre-emption, (well and good); otherwise, he (the judge) requires him (the plaintiff) to produce evidence, because possession is an apparent matter that is probabilistic and thus insufficient to prove entitlement. He said: The judge asks the claimant before turning to the defendant about the location of the house and its boundaries, because he has claimed a right in it, so it becomes like when one claims its ownership. When he (the claimant) clarifies that, he asks him about the cause of his pre-emption, because the causes of pre-emption differ. If he says: 'I am a pre-emptor because of my house adjoining it,' then his claim is complete according to what al-Khassaf said. And it is mentioned in the Fatawa that the determination of this house by which he pre-empts is also required. And we have explained that in the book entitled al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage outlines the procedural steps the qadi must follow when a pre-emptor (shafi') comes to court. First, the qadi asks the defendant (buyer) whether he acknowledges the plaintiff's ownership of the property that gives him the right of pre-emption. If the buyer admits it, no further proof is needed; if not, the pre-emptor must present evidence. Mere possession (yad) is not sufficient because it could be based on a loan, lease, etc. Then, before even hearing the buyer's side, the qadi asks the claimant to specify the location and boundaries of the property in which he claims a right of pre-emption. This is similar to a claim of ownership. After that, the qadi asks the cause of pre-emption (e.g., co-ownership, adjoining rights). If the claimant says he is a neighbour (jar) with an adjoining property, his claim becomes complete as per the view of Imam al-Khassaf. The Fatawa also require specifying the boundaries of the property that gives rise to the pre-emption right. The author (likely al-Marghinani) mentions that he has elaborated on this in his work al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid.

Key Terms
يد (yad): Possession of the property, which is a probabilistic indicator of ownership but not conclusive evidence.
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, typically two male witnesses, required to prove ownership in court.
سبب الشفعة (sabab al-shuf'ah): The legal cause that entitles one to pre-emption: either co-ownership (shirkah) in the property or adjoining (jīwār).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the qadi ask the pre-emptor about the location and boundaries of the property before asking the buyer?
A) To determine the price of the house
B) Because the pre-emptor has claimed a right in that specific property, just like a claim of ownership
C) To check if the house has a fence
D) To see if the pre-emptor is wealthy enough to buy

Key Takeaway
The qadi must follow a precise order: verify ownership, specify property, then determine the cause of pre-emption before hearing the buyer.

Dispute on Requiring Pre-emptor to Bring Price Before Judgment
Intra-Hanafi dispute on pre-emption procedural condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on whether the pre-emptor must bring the price before the judge's decree, and explain the reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
The pre-emptor may contest without the price; the buyer's right to detain property prevents loss.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute about the procedural requirements for a pre-emption claim. The central question is whether the pre-emptor must physically bring the sale price to the court before the judge can hear his case. We will explore the ruling of Zahir al-Riwayah and the opposing view from Imam Muhammad, along with the principles that justify each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Zahir al-Riwayah position
Identify the relied-upon view: contestation is permissible without bringing the price; only after the judge decrees must the pre-emptor bring it.
This is the apparent ruling from the original books.
2
Identify the intra-madhhab variant
Note that Imam Muhammad and a narration from Abu Hanifa (via Hasan) require the price to be brought before the judge hears the case.
This is a minority view within the school.
3
Follow the opposing proof
Understand the opponent's concern: the pre-emptor may be insolvent, so delaying the decree until the price is brought protects the buyer from loss.
The phrase 'حتى لا يتوى مال المشترى' captures this.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Zahir al-Riwayah rebuttal: before the decree, the pre-emptor owes nothing; thus bringing the price is not a condition. The buyer can retain the property until paid.
The buyer's right to detain suffices.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: under the mufta bihi view, the pre-emptor immediately sues; under the other, he must first arrange the price or be denied hearing.
The school favors immediate access to litigation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وتجوز المنازعة فى الشفعة وان لم يحضر الشفيع الثمن الى مجلس القاضى فاذا قضى القاضي بالشفعة لزمه احضار الثمن وهذا ظاهر رواية الأصل وعن محمد انه لا يقضى حتى يحضر الشفيع الثمن وهو رواية الحسن عن ابي حنيفة لأن الشفيع عساه يكون مفلسا فيتوقف القضاء على احضاره حتى لا يتوى مال المشترى وجه الظاهر انه لا ثمن له عليه قبل القضاء ولهذا لا يشترط تسليمه فكذا لا يشترط احضاره ترجمہ فرمایا قدوری نے اور شفعہ کے اندر منازعت جائز ہے۔ اگر چہ شفیع مجلس قاضی میں شمن کو حاضر نہ کرے۔ پھر جب قاضی نے شفعہ کا فیصلہ کر دیا توشفیع کولازم ہے کہ ثمن حاضر کرے اور یہی مبسوط کی روایت کا ظاہر ہے۔ اور حد سے منقول ہے کہ قاضی فیصلہ نہ کرے۔ یہاں تک کہ شفیع ثمن حاضر کر دے اور یہی ابو حنیفہ سے حسن کی روایت ہے۔ اسلئے کہ شفیع بھی مفلس ہوتا ہے تو قاضی کا فیصلہ موقوف رہے گا۔ یمن کے حاضر کرنے پر تاکہ مشتری کا مال بلاک نہ ہو۔ ظاہر الروایہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مشتری کیلئے شفیع کے اوپر کوئی ثمن نہیں قاضی کے فیصلہ سے پہلے اور اسی وجہ سے شمن کی تسلیم شرط نہیں ہے۔ اسی طرح اس کا احضار شرط نہیں ہے۔ تشریح شفیع کیلئے ضروری نہیں کہ قاضی کی مجلس میں شمن لے کر حاضر ہو یعنی بغیر تمن کے لئے ہوئے منازعت و خصومت جائز ہے۔ ہاں جب قاضی کا فیصلہ ہو گیا اب شمن کو حاضر کرنالازم ہے۔

اس پر صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مبسوط کی روایت کا ظاہر اسی حکم کی جانب مشیر ہے یعنی مبسوط میں یہ مسئلہ صراحہ ایسے مذکور نہیں ۔ البتہ وہاں کی عبارت سے یہی بات ظاہر ہوتی ہے کہ بغیر احضارشمن کے منازعت جائز ہے کیونکہ مبسوط کی عبارت اس طرح است للمشترى ان يحبس الدار حتى يستوفى الثمن منه او من ورثته ان مات - امام محمد فرماتے ہیں کہ بغیر احضار شتمن کے قاضی فیصلہ نہیں کرے گا ۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ سے حسن نے بھی اسی طرح روایت کیا ہے۔ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ہوسکتا ہے شفیع مفلس ہو تو اگر قضاء کیلئے شن کے احضار کو شرط کہ دیں تو قضاء احتضاع یمن پر موقوف رہے گی تا کہ مشتر نما کا مال ہلاک نہ ہو کہ گھر کا فیصلہ شفیع کیلئے ہو گیا اور ابھی وہ شمن ادا نہیں کر رہا ہے تو وہ انتظار میں بیٹھا رہے گا اس کو ہلاکت سے تعبیر کیا ہے۔ ظاہر الروایہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قضاء قاضی سے پہلے شفیع پر ادائیگی من واجب نہیں ہے۔ لہذا جب شمن کی ادائیگی شرط نہیں ہے تو شمس کو لے کر آنا بھی شرط نہیں ہوگا۔
He said: Contesting in pre-emption is permitted even if the pre-emptor does not bring the price to the judge's assembly. When the judge decrees pre-emption, it becomes necessary for him to bring the price. This is the apparent (ruling) of the original narration (Zahir al-Riwayah). And from Muhammad (it is narrated) that he does not decree until the pre-emptor brings the price, and this is the narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifa. Because the pre-emptor may be insolvent, so the judgment is suspended upon his bringing the price so that the buyer's wealth is not lost. The apparent proof is that there is no price owed by him before the judgment, and therefore delivery is not a condition, so similarly bringing it is not a condition. Translation: Quduri said: Contesting in pre-emption is permitted even if the pre-emptor does not bring the price to the judge's assembly. When the judge decrees pre-emption, it becomes necessary for him to bring the price. This is the apparent (ruling) of the narration of al-Mabsut. And it is narrated from Muhammad that he does not decree until the pre-emptor brings the price, and this is the narration of Hasan from Abu Hanifa. Because the pre-emptor may be insolent, the judge's decree will be suspended upon his bringing the price so that the buyer's property is not blocked. The evident proof of Zahir al-Riwayah is that there is no price owed by the pre-emptor to the buyer before the judge's decree, and for this reason delivery of the price is not a condition, so similarly bringing it is not a condition. Explanation: It is not necessary for the pre-emptor to bring the price to the judge's assembly, i.e., contesting and litigation are permitted without the price. Yes, when the judge decrees, then bringing the price becomes necessary. On this, the author of al-Hidayah says: The apparent meaning of the narration of al-Mabsut indicates this ruling, i.e., in al-Mabsut this issue is not explicitly mentioned, but from its wording it is apparent that contestation without bringing the price is permitted, because the wording of al-Mabsut is: 'The buyer has the right to retain the house until he recovers the price from him or from his heirs if he dies.' Imam Muhammad says: The judge will not decree without the bringing of the price. And Hasan also narrated similarly from Abu Hanifa. Imam Muhammad's proof is that the pre-emptor may be insolvent, so if bringing the price is made a condition for judgment, then the judgment will be suspended upon the bringing of the price so that the buyer's property is not destroyed. Because the decree for the house is made for the pre-emptor, and if he does not pay the price, the buyer will be waiting, and that is termed destruction. The proof of Zahir al-Riwayah is that before the judge's decree, payment is not obligatory upon the pre-emptor. Therefore, when payment is not a condition, bringing the price is also not a condition.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether the pre-emptor (shafi') must produce the price (thaman) in the judge's court at the time of claiming his right of pre-emption. The Zahir al-Riwayah position, attributed to Abu Hanifa through Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), is that it is permissible to initiate the lawsuit without bringing the price. The judge's decree of pre-emption makes the payment obligatory, but payment is not a precondition for the hearing. The opposing view, transmitted from Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) and also from Imam Abu Hanifa through Hasan ibn Ziyad, holds that the judge should not even hear the case until the price is brought, out of concern that the pre-emptor might be insolvent, which would leave the buyer's property vulnerable. The Zahir al-Riwayah reasoning is that before the judge's decree, the pre-emptor owes nothing to the buyer; therefore, neither delivery nor bringing the price is a condition. The passage also clarifies that even after the decree, if the pre-emptor delays payment upon the judge's order, his pre-emption is not invalidated because it has been confirmed through litigation.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'ah): The right of a co-owner or neighbor to purchase the sold property by substituting the buyer and paying the price.
ثمن (thaman): The price paid by the buyer to the seller; the pre-emptor must pay this to the buyer to take the property.
زاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani containing the authoritative transmitted rulings of the Hanafi school.
حلف على السبب (half 'ala al-sabab): An oath regarding the cause of a legal event, as opposed to the event itself. Mentioned in prior context.
حلف على الحاصل (half 'ala al-hasil): An oath regarding the actual result or outcome of a cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, when must the pre-emptor bring the price?
A) Before the judge hears the case
B) After the judge decrees pre-emption
C) At the same time as the lawsuit is filed
D) Only if the buyer demands it

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the pre-emptor may initiate litigation without the price; the buyer's right to retain the property until paid suffices to protect his interest.

Buyer's Right to Detain Property After Shuf'ah Judgment
Ruling statement on buyer's retention right and pre-emption validity after delay

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the buyer's right to detain property after a shuf'ah judgment and explain why the pre-emptor's delay in payment does not invalidate the pre-emption.

Core Idea
A pre-emptor's delay in payment does not invalidate his right once confirmed by litigation.

This passage addresses what happens after the judge has decreed shuf'ah. It clarifies that the buyer may retain the property until paid, and that the pre-emptor's right, once established in court, is not lost by mere delay in paying the price. This ruling touches on the interplay between procedural requirements and substantive rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State the buyer's right as given in the text: he can retain the property until he receives the price.
The right is established after the judge decrees shuf'ah in favor of the pre-emptor.
2
Understand the condition for the right
The right arises after judgment. The buyer can detain until full payment of the price.
It is not a permanent retention; it ends upon payment.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi agreement
Even Imam Muhammad, who normally requires the price to be brought before judgment, agrees the judgment is executed.
This shows the ruling is unanimous in effect.
4
Explain the concept of 'mujtahad fihi'
The matter is subject to ijtihad, so a valid judgment stands even if it contradicts a preferred procedure.
This principle reinforces the stability of court decisions.
5
Determine the consequence of delay
If the pre-emptor delays payment after the judge's order, his shuf'ah is not invalidated because it was strengthened by the contestation before the judge.
The right is 'confirmed' (mu'akkadah) by litigation.

And when it is decreed for him (the pre-emptor) regarding the house, the buyer has the right to detain it until he recovers the price. And the judgment is executed according to Muhammad as well, because it is a matter of ijtihad (mujtahad fihi), and the price becomes obligatory upon him, so he (the buyer) detains it for the price. If he (the pre-emptor) delays paying the price after the judge said to him: 'Pay the price to him,' his pre-emption is not invalidated, because it has been strengthened by the contestation before the judge. Translation: And when the house is decreed for the pre-emptor, the buyer has the right to detain the house until he receives the price. And according to Muhammad, the judgment is also executed, because this is a matter of ijtihad, and the price becomes obligatory upon the pre-emptor, so the property is detained for the price. If the pre-emptor delays paying the price after the judge told him: 'Give the price to the buyer,' his pre-emption is not invalidated because it has become strong due to contestation before the judge. Explanation: When contestation without bringing the price is permitted (as mentioned), then the buyer has the right not to hand over the property until the pre-emptor pays the price. Question: According to Imam Muhammad, judgment without bringing the price is not permitted, so how can this be? Answer: He (Muhammad) required bringing the price, but this issue is a matter of ijtihad. Therefore, if the judge decreed without the price being brought, the judgment is executed. If the judge told the pre-emptor to pay the price and he delayed, still his pre-emption is not invalidated because it has become strong due to contestation before the judge.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage deals with the consequences after the judge has decreed pre-emption. The buyer (mushtari) has the right to retain possession of the property until he receives the full price from the pre-emptor. This applies even according to Imam Muhammad, who normally required the price to be brought before judgment; however, once a judgment is passed (even in violation of his preferred procedure), the judgment is valid because the matter is subject to ijtihad (mujtahad fihi). The shuf'ah right, once established through litigation, becomes strong and is not invalidated by delay in payment. Even if the judge orders the pre-emptor to pay and the pre-emptor delays, the pre-emption remains valid. The text also answers a question: how can Imam Muhammad accept execution of a judgment if it contradicts his requirement? The response is that the issue is one of ijtihad; the judgment stands as a valid judicial decision.

Key Terms
حبس (habs): The buyer's right to retain possession of the property until payment of the price.
مجتهد فيه (mujtahad fihi): A matter open to ijtihad, meaning valid differences of scholarly opinion; a judge's ruling in such matters is enforceable even if it does not align with one's own view.
باطل (batil): A term meaning invalid; here it indicates that the shuf'ah right is not nullified by delay in payment after judgment.

The buyer's right to detain property after a shuf'ah judgment is a valid right; the pre-emptor's delay in payment does not nullify his established right.

Pre-emptor Contesting the Seller When Property Is in Seller's Possession
Procedural ruling for pre-emptor when seller holds property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the procedure for a pre-emptor when the sold property remains in the seller's possession and explain why the buyer must be present in court.

Core Idea
Buyer's ownership and seller's possession make both parties essential for the pre-emptor's claim.

This passage from Quduri's matn, clarified in the commentary, addresses a procedural nuance: though the pre-emptor may initially contest the seller, the judge cannot adjudicate until the buyer attends. The ruling ensures that the rights of all parties—seller's lawful possession, buyer's ownership, and pre-emptor's claim—are properly considered.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and condition
The act is the pre-emptor contesting the seller. The condition is that the sold property remains in the seller's possession (yad mustahaqqah).
2
State the ruling
The pre-emptor has the right (hukm: mubah) to bring the seller to court and contest him for pre-emption.
This is because the seller's possession is legally recognized.
3
Recognize the procedural limitation
The judge will not hear evidence or proceed until the buyer is present in court.
The buyer holds ownership (milk) even though possession remains with the seller.
4
Understand the judicial act
Once the buyer attends, the judge annuls the sale (faskh al-bay'), decrees the pre-emption against the seller, and makes the seller liable for warranty ('uhdah).
5
Grasp the rationale (talil)
Both parties are needed because the judge's decree affects both ownership (buyer's right) and possession (seller's right) which together transfer to the pre-emptor.
Without both, the decree would be incomplete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

He said: And if the pre-emptor brings the seller while the sold property is in his hand (possession), then he may contest him in pre-emption, because the hand is his and it is a rightful hand. And the judge will not hear evidence until the buyer is present. Then he annuls the sale in his presence and decrees pre-emption against the seller and makes the responsibility (for warranty) upon him, because ownership is for the buyer and possession is for the seller, and the judge decrees both for the pre-emptor, so their presence is necessary. Translation: Quduri said: If the pre-emptor brings the seller before the judge while the sold property is in his possession, then the pre-emptor has the right to contest him in pre-emption, because the seller has possession, and it is a rightful possession. The judge will not hear evidence until the buyer arrives. Then the judge annuls the sale in the presence of the buyer and decrees pre-emption against the seller and makes the warranty responsibility upon him, because ownership belongs to the buyer and possession to the seller, and the judge decrees both for the pre-emptor, so the presence of both is necessary. Explanation: If the sold property is still in the possession of the seller, it is permissible for the pre-emptor to contest the seller and bring him before the judge. But since ownership is with the buyer, the judge will not hear evidence until the buyer arrives; he will hear after his arrival. Then...
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage explains the procedure when the pre-emptor seeks to exercise his right but the sold property is still in the seller's possession. The pre-emptor may bring the seller to court and contest him directly, because the seller has actual possession (yad mustahaqqah). However, since ownership (milk) has transferred to the buyer, the judge cannot hear the case or accept evidence until the buyer is present. Once the buyer attends, the judge annuls the sale (yafsakh al-bay') in the buyer's presence and decrees the pre-emption against the seller, making the seller responsible for any warranty claims (al-'uhdah). The reason for requiring both parties is that the judge's decree affects both the ownership (which belongs to the buyer) and the possession (which belongs to the seller); hence both must be present to ensure proper adjudication.

Key Terms
يد مستحقة (yad mustahaqqah): Possession that is legally recognized as rightful, even if the possessor is not the owner.
فسخ البيع (faskh al-bay'): Annulment of the sale by the judge, canceling the buyer's ownership due to the pre-emptor's right.
عهدة ('uhdah): The responsibility for warranty, meaning the seller becomes liable for any defects or claims against the property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When the sold property remains in the seller's possession, the pre-emptor may contest the seller, but the judge will not decide until the buyer attends, after which the sale is annulled, pre-emption decreed, and warranty placed on the seller.

Partial Annulment of Sale and Its Effect on Preemption and Warranty
Legal reasoning on partial annulment preserving preemption basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that annulment of a sale in favor of a preemptor is partial, preserving the preemption base, and distinguish the warranty liability based on whether the buyer has taken possession.

Core Idea
The sale is annulled only for the buyer, not completely—preemption remains valid because the contract's basis stays intact.

If a judge annuls a sale so that the preemptor can take the property, does that not destroy the very sale on which preemption is based? The Hanafis resolve this apparent contradiction by distinguishing between complete and partial annulment. This passage explains the legal reasoning (ta'lil) behind this distinction and then shows how the location of warranty (uhdah) changes depending on whether the buyer had taken possession before the annulment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contradiction
The preemptor's right depends on the existence of a valid sale. But annulling that sale would seem to remove the basis for preemption. Pinpoint this conflict.
This is the objection the passage addresses.
2
Classify the type of annulment
The passage explains that the annulment is only 'fi haqq al-mushtari' (in respect of the buyer) because his purpose (possession) is prevented. The original contract (asl al-bay') remains.
Hanafis call this partial annulment (faskh qismi), not total nullification (ibtal).
3
Analyze the legal fiction: the preemptor steps into the buyer's place
The transaction shifts to the preemptor as if he bought directly from the seller. This preserves the sale for preemption purposes.
This is a legal constructive transfer (tahawwul al-safqah).
4
Apply the two scenarios for warranty
If the buyer had not yet taken possession (first case), the warranty is on the seller because the buyer's right was annulled. If the buyer had taken possession, the warranty is on the buyer because his ownership was complete by possession.
This distinction follows from the rule that warranty follows ownership at the time of transfer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بیع کو فسخ قرار دینے سے شفعہ کی بنیاد ہی ختم ہو جاتی ہے، پھر شفیع کو شفعہ کیوں ملتا ہے

ثم وجه هذا الفسخ المذكور أن ينفسخ فى حق الأضافة لا متناع المشترى بالأخذ بالشفعة وهو يوجب الفسخ الا انه يبقى اصل البيع لتعذر انفساخه لان الشفعة بناء عليه ولكنه تتحول الصفقة اليه ويصير كانه و المشترى منه فلهذا يرجع بالعهدة على البائع

ترجمہ پھر اس فسخ مذکور کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ مشتری کی جانب اضافت کے حق میں فسخ ہو جائے گا۔ شفعہ میں لئے جانے کی وجہ سے مشتری کے قبضہ کے ممتنع ہونے کی وجہ سے اور یہ (امتناع) فسخ کو واجب کرتا ہے۔ مگر تحقیق اصل باقی رہے گا ۔ اس کے انفساخ کے متعذر ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اس لئے کہ شفعہ اس پر مبنی ہے لیکن معاملہ شفیع کی جانب متحول ہو جائے گا۔ اور ہو جائے گا گویا کہ شفیع ہی بائع سے خریدنے والا ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے ذمہ داری بائع کی جانب راجع ہوگی۔

تشریح ماقبل میں یہ بات آچکی ہے کہ بیع کے اوپر ثبوت شفعہ کا مدار ہے اور یہاں آپ نے بیع کو فسخ قرار دیا تو شفعہ کی بنیاد منہدم ہو گئی ۔ لہذا پھر شفیع کو شفعہ نہیں ملنا چاہئے؟ تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ بیع بالکلیہ منعدم نہیں ہوگی بلکہ مشتری کے حق میں فسخ ہوگی کیونکہ جب شفیع اس کو شفعہ میں لینا چاہتا ہے تو پھر مشتری کا قبضہ ممنوع ٹھہر یعنی مشتری کے حق میں بیع کا مقصد متحقق نہیں ہوا۔ حالانکہ ہر کام کا ایک مقصد ہوتا ہے۔ تو جب یہ مقصد پورا نہ ہوا تو بیع کو مشتری کے حق میں فسخ کرنا پڑا۔ مگر چونکہ شریعت نے شفیع کو حق شفعہ دیا ہے اسلئے اصل عقد بیع کی بقاء بھی ضروری ہے۔ لہذا بائع کا ایجاب باقی رکھا گیا اور بائع سے براہ راست شفیع کو خریدنے والا قرار دیا گیا۔ ورنہ اس کے بغیر شفعہ ہی نہیں مل سکے گا۔ اس لئے کہا کہ اصل بیع موجود ہے مگر عقد کی نسبت بدل گئی بجائے مشتری کے شفیع کی جانب ہوگئی ۔ یہی تو وجہ ہے کہ عقد کی ذمہ داری بائع پر عائد کی گئی ہے۔ مشتری کی ملکیت اور قبضہ کی صورت میں شفیع مبیع مشتری سے وصول کرے گا

بخلاف ما اذا قبضه المشترى فاخذه من يده حيث تكون العهدة عليه لانه تم ملكه بالقبض وفى الوجه الأول امتنع قبض المشترى وانه يوجب الفسخ وقد طولنا الكلام فيه فى كفاية المنتهى بتوفيق الله تعالى ترجمہ بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ مشتری نے اس پر قبضہ کر لیا ہو تو لے گا شفیع مبیع کو مشتری کے قبضہ سے۔ اس حیثیت سے کہ ہوگی ذمہ داری مشتری کے اوپر اسلئے کہ قبضہ کی وجہ سے اس کی ملکیت عام ہوگئی اور پہلی صورت میں مشتری کا قبضہ منع ہوگیا۔ اور یہ امتناع فسخ کو طلب کرتا ہے۔ اور ہم اس کلام میں طویل کلام اللہ کی توفیق سے کفایۃ المنتہی میں کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح مذکورہ تفصیلات اس وقت تھیں جبکہ مبیع بائع کے قبضہ میں ہو اور اگر مشتری کے قبضہ میں ہو تو اب ملکیت اور قبضہ دونوں اسی کے ہیں تو اس وقت میں شفیع مبیع کو مشتری سے لے گا اور ذمہ داری مشتری پر ہوگی۔
Then, since declaring the sale void destroys the very basis of preemption, why does the preemptor still get preemption? Then, the explanation (wajh) of this aforementioned annulment is that it is annulled in respect of [the buyer's] right of addition (idafah) due to the prevention (imtina') of the buyer from taking by preemption, and this necessitates annulment. But the original sale remains because its annulment is impossible, since preemption is based upon it. However, the transaction shifts to him (the preemptor), and he becomes as if he is the buyer from the seller; therefore, the warranty returns to the seller. Translation: Then the reason for this mentioned annulment is that it will be annulled in respect of the [buyer's] right of addition, due to the prevention of the buyer's possession because of being taken by preemption, and this (prevention) necessitates annulment. But the original remains, due to the impossibility of its annulment, because preemption is based upon it. However, the transaction shifts to the preemptor, and it becomes as if the preemptor is the one buying from the seller. For this reason, responsibility returns to the seller. Explanation: It has already passed that the proof of preemption is based on the sale, and here you have declared the sale void, so the foundation of preemption collapsed. Therefore, the preemptor should not get preemption? The answer given is that the sale is not completely nullified; rather, it is annulled in respect of the buyer, because when the preemptor wants to take it by preemption, the buyer's possession becomes prevented; i.e., the purpose of the sale in respect of the buyer is not achieved. Although every act has a purpose. So when this purpose is not fulfilled, the sale had to be annulled in respect of the buyer. But because the Sharia has given the preemptor the right of preemption, the maintenance of the original sale contract is also necessary. Therefore, the seller's offer (ijab) is kept intact, and the preemptor is considered directly as the buyer from the seller. Otherwise, without it, preemption cannot be obtained. Hence it is said that the original sale exists, but the attribution of the contract has changed; instead of the buyer, it goes to the preemptor. This is the reason why the responsibility of the contract is placed on the seller. In the case of the buyer's ownership and possession, the preemptor takes the sold item from the buyer. Contrary to when the buyer has taken possession, then he (the preemptor) takes it from his hand, and the warranty is upon him (the buyer) because his ownership became complete by possession. In the first case, the buyer's possession was prevented, and this prevention necessitates annulment. And we have spoken at length about this in Kifayat al-Muntaha, by the grace of Allah Almighty. Translation: Contrary to the case when the buyer has taken possession of it, then the preemptor will take the sold item from the buyer's possession, such that the warranty is upon the buyer because his ownership became general due to possession, and in the first case, the buyer's possession was prevented, and this prevention demands annulment. And we have given a long discussion on this in Kifayat al-Muntaha, by the grace of Allah. Explanation: The mentioned details were for when the sold item is in the seller's possession; but if it is in the buyer's possession, then both ownership and possession belong to him; in that case, the preemptor takes the sold item from the buyer, and the warranty is upon the buyer.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection: If the judge annuls the sale, the basis for preemption (which is the sale) disappears, so how can the preemptor still get preemption? The answer is that the sale is annulled only in relation to the buyer (fi haqq al-mushtari) because his taking possession is prevented by the preemptor's claim. The original sale contract remains intact as the foundation for preemption, but the transaction shifts to the preemptor, who becomes as if he bought directly from the seller. Therefore, the warranty (uhdah) lies with the seller. Then it contrasts the case where the buyer has taken possession: then the preemptor takes the property from the buyer, and the warranty is on the buyer because his ownership became complete by possession. The author refers to his longer discussion in Kifayat al-Muntaha. The legal reasoning (ta'lil) here is that the annulment is partial; it only affects the buyer's right, not the contract's existence. This preserves the basis for preemption.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Annulment; nullification of a contract, here specifically in relation to the buyer while the original contract remains.
عہدہ (uhdah): Warranty or responsibility; the obligation to compensate the preemptor if the property is found defective or if there is a claim.
شفعة (shuf'ah): The right of preemption; the ability to substitute the buyer in a sale of property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the legal effect of the judge's annulment of the sale in favor of the preemptor?
A) The entire sale is nullified, and the preemptor gets the property for free.
B) The sale is annulled only in relation to the buyer, but the original contract remains as the basis for preemption.
C) The seller must pay the preemptor the price from his own pocket.
D) The buyer retains ownership, and the preemptor only gets possession.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school preserves the preemption basis by treating the annulment as partial, shifting the transaction to the preemptor without destroying the original sale.

Annulment of Sale in Pre-emption and Shift of Liability
Explaining the annulment of sale in relation to the buyer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the annulment of sale in pre-emption and determine who bears liability based on whether the buyer has taken possession.

Core Idea
The sale is annulled only relative to the buyer, preserving the contract for the pre-emptor.

Pre-emption (shuf'ah) gives a co-owner or neighbour the right to step into a sale. But how does this affect the original contract? This lesson explores the Hanafi view: the sale is not completely voided; instead, it is annulled only for the buyer, and the transaction shifts to the pre-emptor. This careful balance maintains the basis for pre-emption while protecting the pre-emptor's right.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the annulment (faskh) of the sale in the context of pre-emption. The ruling is that the sale is annulled partially (only in relation to the buyer) and the transaction shifts to the pre-emptor.
The annulment is not absolute; the original contract remains for the seller-pre-emptor relationship.
2
Locate the dalil
The author does not cite a specific hadith but relies on istihsan (juristic preference) and the principle that every action aims at a purpose. The prevention of the buyer's possession necessitates annulment, but the Shari'ah preserves the contract to uphold pre-emption.
This is an example of qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) and istihsan.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prevention of the buyer's possession makes the sale ineffective for the buyer, so it is annulled relative to him. However, the contract must survive for the pre-emptor to claim his right. Therefore, the contract is preserved but attributed to the pre-emptor.
The key legal link is that pre-emption is built upon the existence of the sale, so the sale cannot be completely void.
4
Note the ikhtilaf based on possession
If the buyer has already taken possession before the pre-emptor claims, then the buyer's ownership is complete. In that case, the pre-emptor takes from the buyer, and liability falls on the buyer.
This shows that the ruling depends on the factual circumstance of possession.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is who bears liability (uhdah) for defects or claims on the property. If the buyer has not taken possession, the seller bears liability; if the buyer has taken possession, the buyer bears liability.
This distinction affects the pre-emptor's recourse in case of defects.

Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining the nature of the annulment of the sale in the context of pre-emption (shuf'ah). The author begins by stating that when the pre-emptor exercises his right, the sale is annulled only in relation to the buyer (mush'tari), not absolutely. The reason is that the buyer is prevented from taking possession because the pre-emptor takes the property. This prevention necessitates annulment, but the original contract cannot be completely annulled because pre-emption is based on its existence. Instead, the transaction is transferred to the pre-emptor, as if he were the direct buyer from the seller. Consequently, the liability (al-uhdah) for any defects or claims reverts to the seller, not the buyer. The author then contrasts this with the case where the buyer had already taken possession before the pre-emptor's claim. In that scenario, the buyer's ownership is complete through possession, so the pre-emptor takes the property from the buyer, and the liability remains on the buyer. The author also references his own work, Kifayat al-Muntaha, for further detail. This explanation resolves the apparent contradiction: how can pre-emption exist if the sale is annulled? The answer is a partial annulment, preserving the contract but shifting its effects to the pre-emptor. This is a characteristic Hanafi application of istihsan (juristic preference) to balance the rights of the pre-emptor with the integrity of the original sale.

Key Terms
شفعة (shuf'ah): The right of a co-owner or neighbour to acquire a sold property by compulsory purchase, overriding the buyer.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment or rescission of a contract; here applied partially to the sale in relation to the buyer.
عهدة (uhdah): Liability for defects or claims on the sold property; the duty to indemnify the buyer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, when the pre-emptor claims before the buyer takes possession, who bears the liability (uhdah) for the sold property?
A) The buyer
B) The pre-emptor
C) The seller
D) Both the buyer and seller equally

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the exercise of pre-emption annuls the sale only relative to the buyer, transferring the contract to the pre-emptor and placing liability on the seller (unless the buyer had already taken possession).

The Agent as Opponent of the Pre-emptor
Stating that an agent who buys for another is the opponent of the pre-emptor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the opponent (khasm) in a pre-emption case when an agent is involved and state the determining factors of possession and delivery.

Core Idea
The agent is the pre-emptor's opponent until he delivers the property to the principal.

This lesson explains who the pre-emptor must sue when the buyer is an agent. The ruling from Quduri establishes that the agent is the direct party because he made the contract. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly applying the right of pre-emption in agency transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
List the seller, buyer (agent), principal, and pre-emptor. Determine who made the contract.
The agent is the legal buyer even though he acts for another.
2
Determine the contracting party
The agent is the contractor because he performed the sale transaction.
Rights of the contract attach to the contractor.
3
Apply the general rule
Since pre-emption is a right of the contract, the agent is the opponent.
The pre-emptor sues the agent, not the principal.
4
Consider the exception
If the agent delivers the property to the principal, the principal becomes the opponent because the agent loses possession and ownership.
Delivery transfers the right to sue.
5
Understand the agency distinction
Unlike a direct seller, the agent stands in place of the principal, so the principal's presence is not required when the agent is present.
This is because the agent is the principal's representative.
